1001 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Indiana High School Athletic Ass'n v. Schafer


No. 37A05-9201-CV-19


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


598 N.E.2d 540; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 1363



August 24, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied December 16, 1992.
Transfer denied by, 12/16/1992
Costs and fees proceeding at Ind. High Sch. Ath. Ass'n v. Schafer, 913 N.E.2d 789, 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 1970 (Ind. Ct. App., 2009)
Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by Ind. High Sch. Ath. Ass'n v. Schafer, 2013 Ind. App. LEXIS 620 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 17, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE JASPER CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Raymond D. Kickbush, Special Judge. Cause No. 37C01-9111-CP-236.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff student filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant Indiana High School Athletic Association, Inc. (IHSAA), claiming that the IHSAA's rules were unconstitutional. The student sought to enjoin the IHSAA from prohibiting the student from participating in interscholastic sports. The Jasper Circuit Court (Indiana) held in favor of the student. The IHSAA appealed.


OVERVIEW: As a junior, the student played high school basketball. The high school was a member of the IHSAA. During the spring of his junior year, the student withdrew from school because he had a serious sinus infection. The student had received poor grades during the fall semester because of the sinus infection. As such, the high school permitted him to repeat his junior year. However, the IHSAA forbade him to play basketball during his repeated junior year under a rule which limited athletic eligibility to the eight semesters of high school and provided that after being enrolled 16 or more school days in each of 4 fall semesters, a student was ineligible for further participation. The IHSAA denied him relief under a rule, providing that the 16 days were not counted if the student withdrew from school due to a serious illness. The court held that the IHSAA was engaged in state action, but that there was no violation of procedural due process. However, the court found that the student did not repeat his junior year coursework in an attempt to gain an advantage in sports competition. As such, the court held that not allowing the student to play was arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

 

1002 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hatcher v. Barnes


No. 45A03-9106-CV-184


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


597 N.E.2d 974; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 1316



August 18, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] INTERLOCUTORY APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT, ROOM 4. The Honorable Gerald Svetanoff, Judge. Cause No. 45D04-9105-CP-00369



DISPOSITION: It follows that candidate Hatcher was entitled to proceed under IC 3-12-8-1 et seq. to challenge the results of the primary election for fraud and the court erred in dismissing that count of his petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate filed an interlocutory appeal challenging a judgment from the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which awarded partial summary judgment to respondents, a declared winning nominee and opposing candidates. The trial court granted respondents' motion to dismiss, holding that absent an allegation of grounds for contest under Indiana's election contest statute, Ind. Code § 3-12-8-1 et seq., it lacked jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The candidate filed a complaint seeking a recount of all votes cast in all districts and precincts in a mayoral election. He also sought to contest the election on the basis of fraud and irregularities and misconduct by the people associated with the election process. The winning nominee moved to dismiss, asserting that the candidate's complaint was jurisdictionally defective because it was not properly verified and it failed to allege the required statutory grounds for contesting an election. The candidate responded that if the election statute precluded election contests on grounds of fraud, it would unconstitutionally deny him due process under both the Indiana and United States Constitutions. The court held that: (1) it would appear that the legislature by its 1988 amendments to the election statute removed fraud as a ground for contesting the results of an election; (2) however, the election belonged to the sovereign people and the legislature had to stay within its constitutional powers; and (3) therefore, the candidate was entitled to be accorded the opportunity to challenge fraud in the conduct of the primary election, although quo warranto was not available.


OUTCOME: The court held that the nominee was entitled to proceed under the election statute to challenge the results of the primary election for fraud, and the trial court erred in dismissing that count of the candidate's petition.

 

1003 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Demontigney v. State


No. 45A04-9110-CR-3511


1 This case was diverted by direction of the Chief Judge on 4/23/92.


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


593 N.E.2d 1270; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 1011



June 22, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 1, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James Letsinger, Judge. Cause Nos. 45G02-9105-CF-90 and 45G02-9105-CF-91



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is in all things affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the decision of the Lake County Superior Court (Minnesota), which convicted defendants of a class D felony for cruelly confining their six-year old son, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4.


OVERVIEW: A neighbor found the child shackled to his bed. Defendants were tried and convicted of cruelly confining the child, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4. On defendants' appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court determined that § 35-46-1-4 made it a crime to confine a dependent cruelly, and that a statute was not unconstitutionally vague if individuals of ordinary intelligence comprehended it adequately. The court had amply defined "cruelly" in its rulings, and that, applying the standards, the statute was constitutional. Although defendants claimed they were only punishing the child and there was no mens rea, the court applied an objective standard of cruelty. Defendant father claimed he was out of the house under arrest for two days and challenged the sufficiency of the evidence against him, however, based on the test for sufficiency of the evidence, viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the verdict, the evidence was overwhelmingly sufficient to sustain his conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, convicting defendants of cruelly confining their son and upholding the constitutionality of the statute.

 

1004 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Kosciusko County Drainage Bd. Elaine Wood


No. 43A03-9109-CV-274


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


594 N.E.2d 798; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 960



June 16, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 29, 1992. Transfer Denied October 26, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE KOSCIUSKO CIRCUIT COURT, ON PETITION FOR JUDICIAL REVIEW OF DRAINAGE BOARD DECISION. The Honorable Richard W. Sand, Judge. Cause No. 43C01-9012-CP-859



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owners sought review of the judgment by the Kosciusko Circuit Court (Indiana), which affirmed the designation by respondent Kosciusko County Drainage Board (board) of a subsurface drain on respondent adjoining property owners' property as a "regulated drain" under the Indian Drainage Code, Ind. Code § 36-9-27-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Under Indiana's Code a mutual drain was convertible into a regulated drain only if: (1) The owners of more than 50 percent in acreage of the affected land would have been benefited if the drain was made a regulated drain under this chapter; and (2) The benefit to owners benefited was likely to have been greater than the damages to owners damaged by reason of the mutual drain being made a regulated drain. The court affirmed, finding that more than 50 percent of the affected land was benefited as the drain affected more than 36 acres, and most of those acres were benefited by the regulated drain. There was no requirement that the adjoining property owners own more than 50 percent of the land benefited. The court held that the affected area did not include lakes and the drain converted was a mutual drain. Finally, the court held that Ind. Code § 36-9-27-19(c) was not constitutionally defective as it provided fair warning of the criteria by which petitions were considered and that the establishment of a regulated drain was not an unconstitutional taking of property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the designation by the board of a subsurface drain on the adjoining property owners' property as a "regulated" drain.

 

1005 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


St. Anthony Medical Center, Inc. v. Smith


No. 37A04-9010-CV-4601


1 This case was transferred to this office by order of the Chief Judge on March 26, 1992.


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


592 N.E.2d 732; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 858



May 28, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied August 27, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE JASPER CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable E. Duane Daugherty, Judge. Cause No. 37C01-8910-CT-226



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital appealed a judgment from the Jasper Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered an order in favor of plaintiff, personally and as administratrix the estate of the decedent in a wrongful death action. The administratrix filed a cross-appeal challenging both the reduction of the jury's award of damages from $ 937,000 to $ 500,000 and the constitutionality of the Indiana Medical Malpractice Act.


OVERVIEW: One day after the administratrix filed her medical malpractice complaint against the hospital for the wrongful death of decedent, she filed an identical complaint with state's medical review panel (panel) for it to render an opinion, notwithstanding that the Indiana Medical Malpractice Act (Act), Ind. Code § 16-9.5-9-2 required that the panel's decision was a jurisdictional prerequisite to commencing an action. However, the hospital neglected to file any motion challenging the trial court's subject matter jurisdiction until over two years later, by which time the panel had concluded that the hospital had failed to comply with the appropriate standard of care. The administratrix then filed a motion to reinstate the original complaint with the trial court which was granted and after a trial, the jury awarded damages in the amount of $ 937,000. Upon the hospital's motion, the trial court reduced the judgment to $ 500,000, the cap provided under the Act. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that under the peculiar facts of the case, the motion to reinstate constituted a refiling of the complaint. On the cross-appeal, the court affirmed the constitutionality of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which denied the hospital's motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction and granted the administratrix' motion to reinstate the medical malpractice complaint.

 

1006 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


McElroy v. State


No. 49A04-9109-CR-282


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


592 N.E.2d 726; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 867



May 27, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied July 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Gary Miller, Judge. Cause No. 49G05-8911-CF-131615.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of rape, a violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-4-1(a); two counts of battery, a violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1; three counts of robbery, a violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-5-1; and three counts of confinement, a violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-3-3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape, two counts of battery, three counts of robbery, and three counts of confinement and was sentenced to a total of 186 years imprisonment. He argued, among other things, that the chain of custody for evidence used for deoxyribonucleic acid identification was broken by a laboratory technician's failure to testify, that his convictions for confinement and robbery violated double jeopardy, and that his sentence was manifestly unreasonable. The court found that the testimony of a Federal Bureau of Investigation agent was sufficient to establish chain of custody in the face of a challenge raising only the mere possibility of tampering, substitution, or alteration. The separate convictions for robbery and confinement did not violate double jeopardy because the charging instruments broke down the separate acts of the confinements and the robberies with specificity. The robberies were effectuated by putting the victims in fear, and the confinements were not co-extensive with the robberies. The court did not find the sentences to be manifestly unreasonable in light of the nature of the offenses and the risk that defendant would repeat the offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1007 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Breeck v. Madison


No. 40A01-9111-CV-349


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


592 N.E.2d 700; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 860



May 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied August 26, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE JENNINGS CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Larry J. Greathouse, Judge. Cause No. 40C01-8709-CP-177



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff barge owner appealed the decision of the Jennings Circuit Court (Indiana) entering summary judgment for defendants, city, county, captain of a sheriff's department, marine service, and its owner, in his action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for the return and repair of his barge after the city removed it from a riverbank.


OVERVIEW: The barge was beached on the city's riverbank and remained there for several months. The city became concerned that the barge posed a safety hazard, but it was unable to find the owner of the barge. The city contracted with the marine service and its owner to remove the barge. Later, the barge owner took the barge from the marine service's facility. The captain of the sheriff's department arrested the barge owner for disorderly conduct. The barge owner filed a § 1983 action for the return and repair of the barge against defendants. The barge owner also asked for punitive damages. The trial court granted summary judgment for defendants. The barge owner appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the barge owner was not entitled to punitive damages because the city and county were immune from such damages under § 1983. Also, the marine service owner was acting pursuant to a contract with the city and the captain acted in the course of his duties as a member of the sheriff's department. The court found that the barge owner failed to show issues of material fact regarding a city or county policy or custom that caused a deprivation of his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the entry of partial summary judgment for defendants in the barge owner's § 1983 action for the return and repair of his barge.

 

1008 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Sowell v. State


No. 49A05-9105-CR-153


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


590 N.E.2d 1123; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 597



April 28, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied June 17, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. CRIMINAL DIVISION, ROOM NUMBER 15. The Honorable Richard F. Sallee, Judge. Cause No. 49F15-9009-CF-110583



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Marion County Municipal Court (Indiana), which convicted him of prostitution, enhanced his sentence, and imposed an 11-year sentence with two years suspended.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with prostitution, a class A misdemeanor, and with being a class D felony habitual offender. Within the last 10 years of his arrest, defendant had been convicted nine times for prostitution. Two of the nine prostitution convictions were class D felonies. The trial court found defendant guilty of prostitution. It then determined that defendant was guilty of prostitution as a class D felony. Based upon evidence incorporated from the prior proceedings, the trial court held that defendant was a habitual class D felony offender and enhanced his three-year sentence by eight-years, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-50-2-7.1. On appeal, the court noted that nothing in § 35-50-2-7.1 prohibited incorporating evidence from the earlier phases of defendant's trifurcated trial. Thus, defendant failed to show that the evidence did not support the trial court's habitual offender finding. While enhancement on the basis of the nature of the present offense was not justified, defendant had a long history of prior offenses. Under the facts and circumstances, the court could not conclude that defendant's sentence was manifestly unreasonable or unconstitutionally disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Kleiman v. State


No. 49A04-9102-CR-49


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


590 N.E.2d 660; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 563



April 23, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied June 1, 1992. Transfer Denied July 22, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. The Honorable A. Tony Cordingley, Judge. Cause No. 49F10-8909-CM-101819


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant arrestee sought review of an order from the Marion Municipal Court (Indiana), which was in favor of appellee state in the arrestee's action for expungement of his arrest record after he was acquitted of public indecency.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee filed a petition for expungement of his arrest record after he was acquitted of public indecency in a bench trial. The trial court found that Ind. Code § 35-38-5-1 permitted expungement only if the charges had been dropped before trial and denied the arrestee's petition. The arrestee contended on appeal that the trial court had discretion to order expungement of arrest records without specific statutory authority and that § 35-38-5-1 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's order in favor of the state. The court found that § 35-38-5-1 provided the only means for the expungement of arrest records. The court held that the trial court did not have the discretion to grant expungement of arrest records when the arrestee failed to meet his burden of proving that he fell within the provisions of § 35-38-5-1.The court determined that § 35-38-5-1 did not unconstitutionally distinguish between persons who had been wrongfully arrested and persons who had been acquitted after trial. The court concluded that the arrestee's acquittal did not change the fact that there was probable cause for his arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order in favor of the state in the arrestee's action for expungement of his arrest record.

Regan v. State


No. 92A03-9111-CR-339


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


590 N.E.2d 640; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 551



April 21, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE WHITLEY SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James R. Fleck, Judge. Cause No. 92D01-9002-CF-115



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Whitley Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him pursuant to a jury trial of operating a vehicle while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's car went off the road, a police officer stopped to investigate. The officer noticed a strong odor of alcohol as he interviewed defendant in the patrol car and, thus, asked defendant to accompany him to the sheriff's department to submit to an Intoxilyzer test. Defendant consented to the test, which registered a .15 percent blood alcohol content. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in admitting statements that he made to the officer before the corpus delicti of the crime was established, but the court found that the evidence was sufficient to establish the corpus delicti of the crime. The court also rejected defendant's assertion that all the evidence gained as a result of his conversation with the officer was the product of an unlawful detention. Additionally, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction, that Ind. Code §§ 9-11-2-1 and 9-11-4-5 were constitutional, that admission of exhibits related to the testing procedure did not violate defendant's rights to confrontation and cross-examination, and that there was no error in the trial court's instructions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of operating a vehicle while intoxicated.

 

1011 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Garrod v. Garrod


No. 79A05-9106-CV-201


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


590 N.E.2d 163; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 492



April 15, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Vincent F. Grogg, Special Judge. Cause No. 79C01-8711-DR-735


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged an order from the Tippecanoe Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for modification of the child support he had been ordered to pay to appellee mother, who had been awarded custody of their only child.


OVERVIEW: When the marriage of the father and mother was dissolved, the mother was awarded custody of their child. The father was ordered to pay child support and to pay all reasonable and necessary uninsured medical expenses for the child. The father filed a petition for modification of support alleging a substantial and continuing change in circumstances made the support order unreasonable. The trial court denied the petition. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The record indicated that the father was not voluntarily unemployed and his decline in income was not purposely brought about to reduce support payments. The trial court erred by considering the father's potential income when it determined whether modification of the support order was appropriate. There was no evidence that the father's loss of employment was temporary. The trial court could consider the father's assets to determine whether he had an ability to pay child support above what his income indicated under the Indiana Child Support Guidelines. The court indicated that the record supported a deviation from the guideline amount because the child spent substantially more time with the father than in the average case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of the father's petition for modification of child support, and the action was remanded for a determination whether a substantial and continuing change in circumstances existed justifying a modification.

 

1012 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Coleman v. State


No. 20A05-9109-CR-304


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


588 N.E.2d 1335; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 468



March 31, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied July 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Gene R. Duffin, Judge. Cause No. 20C01-9102-CF-017



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the Elkhart Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of delivering more than three grams of cocaine, a Class A felony under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 35-48-4-1, on its face, was unconstitutionally vague, and violated the substantive due process and equal protection guarantees of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, as well as Ind. Const. art. I, § 16, the constitutional guarantee of proportionality in sentencing; and that it was reversible error to allow prosecution witnesses to testify about what defendant's girlfriend said when he was arrested. The court could not say that the Class A felony enhancement of § 35-48-4-1 was unconstitutionally vague. Ordinary people could understand that it was the overall rather than pure weight that counted, and there had been no showing that § 35-48-4-1 lent itself to arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. The court held that § 35-48-4-1 was not unconstitutionally vague and did not offend the rights of due process and equal protection. Defendant did not cite any case on the meaning of Indiana's proportionality guarantee, so he waived the issue. The girlfriend denied making a statement, testifying instead that she had said the police were arresting the wrong person. There was nothing unfair or surprising to the witness. There was no error in admitting the witnesses' testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

Warthen v. State


No. 60A01-9108-CR-256


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


588 N.E.2d 545; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 326



March 18, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE OWEN CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Frank M. Nardi, Judge. Cause No. 60C01-9009-CM-379



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is reversed and the cause is remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Own Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered judgment on a jury verdict and convicted him of operating a vehicle while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: When a deputy arrived at the scene of an accident, he found defendant trapped in the car, with the motor running and the wheels spinning, and noticed a strong odor of alcoholic beverages. After defendant was freed, a blood alcohol content (BAC) test, taken within three hours of the deputy's arrival at the accident scene, revealed a BAC of .116 percent and defendant was subsequently convicted. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and ordered a new trial. The court agreed with defendant that the trial court erred in instructing the jury that the BAC presumptively related back to the time defendant operated his vehicle if the jury found that the test was performed within three hours of after the deputy had probable cause to believe defendant committed an offense under Ind. Code § 9-30-5. The court noted that, although defendant had the burden to prove that the BAC results did not relate back to the time at which he had operated the vehicle, the jury should have been instructed that it was free to accept or reject the presumption even if defendant had not offered rebuttal evidence that he had consumed alcohol after the accident occurred and while waiting for help to arrive.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, convicting defendant of driving while intoxicated, and remanded the cause to the trial court for a new trial.

Campbell v. Criterion Group


No. 29A02-9103-CV-140


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


588 N.E.2d 511; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 270



March 12, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] On Petition to Transfer December 30, 1992, Reported at 1992 Ind. LEXIS 276.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Judith Profitt, Judge. Cause No. 29C01-8811-CP-759


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, indigent civil litigants, petitioned for review of the order of the Hamilton Circuit Court (Indiana) that denied their motion which requested leave to proceed on appeal in forma pauperis and requested preparation of the record on appeal at public expense.


OVERVIEW: Summary judgment was entered against an indigent civil litigant, who then moved to proceed on appeal in forma pauperis. Although the opposing side did not dispute his status as indigent, the trial court denied his motion to proceed in forma pauperis. On appeal from this denial, the trial court's order was reversed. The court held that Ind. Const. art. 7, § 6 and Ind. Const. art. I, § 12, together with Ind. Code § 34-1-1-3, entitled indigent civil appellants to records of the proceedings prepared without expense to them. The indigent civil litigants' petition to proceed on appeal in forma pauperis was granted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order below and granted the indigent civil litigants' petition to proceed on appeal in forma pauperis. All costs were waived, including the appellate filing fee. The parties were instructed to submit appellate briefs.

 

1015 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Klagiss v. State


No. 49A02-9008-CR-00478


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


585 N.E.2d 674; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 77



January 30, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Transfer Denied March 11, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John R. Barney, Judge. Cause No. 49G03-8903-CF-33013



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction for neglect of a dependent in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-1-4 entered on a jury verdict by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) after his mother died of a fractured neck while in defendant's care. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for neglect of a dependent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant presented hypothetical questions to two different expert witnesses at trial, to which the trial court sustained the state's objections because the hypothetical was based on facts not in evidence. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sustaining the objections to the hypothetical questions because although it was not necessary that the hypotheticals included all pertinent facts and defendant had a fundamental right to present exculpatory evidence, the hypotheticals were improper because they were based on facts not in evidence. Both of the questions asked the witnesses to assume that there had been no trauma to the deceased and on of the questions contained other facts not in evidence. The court ruled that it could not usurp the jury's prerogative and reweigh the evidence. The court found no ground for reversal, concluding that the evidence, and the inferences which it reasonably supported, was sufficient to sustain the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for neglect of a dependent.

 

1016 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Reeves v. Reeves


No. 49A02-9011-CV-6771


1 This case was assigned to this office on July 3, 1991.


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


584 N.E.2d 589; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 50



January 21, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied May 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT, ROOM 2. The Honorable Kenneth A. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. S275-632


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged the decision of the Marion County Superior Court (Indiana), which modified the father's child support obligation. The father contended that Ind. Code § 31-1-11.5-12(b)(1), under which the father was ordered to pay for half of his child's college costs, was unconstitutional, and that the trial court erred in making the modification retroactive and in awarding such a substantial increase in support.


OVERVIEW: Appellee wife filed a petition to modify child support. The trial court increased the support, made it retroactive, and ordered each party to pay half of the child's college expenses. The court affirmed the constitutionality of the law allowing the trial court to order the father to pay his daughter's college expenses. The law did not violate the equal protection or due process rights of the father. The father's liberty right was not absolute, but was tied to his right of control and legal custody of the child. A rational relationship existed between the law and the state's interest in seeing that the child was properly provided for within the father's financial means. The court remanded the issue of whether the father had to pay child support while the child lived on campus because the guidelines contemplated the avoidance of duplicative orders regarding a college student's living expenses. The trial court had the discretion to make a modification retroactive to the date of the petition. Also, the modification, while a substantial increase, was within the child support guidelines, and the father had made no showing that his standard of living would have been drastically reduced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the modification of child support by the father as modified by the court. The court remanded the issue of whether the father had to pay support while his child was living on a college campus. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in awarding the wife half of her appellate attorney's fees.

State v. Springer


No. 32A05-9104-CR-001211


1 This case has been diverted to this office by order of the Chief Judge.


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


585 N.E.2d 27; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 54



January 21, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Transfer March 19, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable J. V. Boles, Judge. Cause No. 32C01-9003-CF-071


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Indiana sought review of an order of the Hendricks County Circuit Court, which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment against him.


OVERVIEW: A nursing home resident was admitted to the hospital afflicted with conjunctivitis and tremors of undetermined origin. His eyes were matted shut and maggots were discovered under one of his toenails. A grand jury indicted defendant, the administrator of the nursing home, charging neglect of a dependent. The trial court dismissed the indictment. On review, the court reversed. The court held that Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4 clearly applied to defendant, as he was a "person having the care of a dependent." Defendant was not placed in a position of having to guess as to the conduct proscribed by the neglect statute. Reasonable persons of ordinary intelligence would have been able to determine that the neglect statute encompassed the failure to obtain necessary medical attention for a dependent, where the caregiver or custodian was not qualified to render medical services directly.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that had dismissed the indictment against defendant.

 

1018 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Deaton v. Greenwood


No. 41A01-9106-CV-182


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


582 N.E.2d 882; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 2150



December 17, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE JOHNSON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Jack Tandy, Special Judge. Cause No. 41C01-9003-CP-83


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two property owners and two City residents, filed an action against defendants, the City of Greenwood, several City officials, and others, challenging the City's annexation of land pursuant to annexation ordinances, Greenwood, Ind., Ordinance §§ 88-12, 89-5, 89-57. The Johnson Circuit Court (Indiana) granted the city's motion for summary judgment. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: In three "phases" under three separate ordinances, the City annexed certain property. Plaintiffs alleged that the ordinances were invalid as a matter of law because they did not contain a legal description of the corporate boundaries of the City, as required by Ind. Code § 36-4-3-3. Plaintiffs further alleged that two of the ordinances unconstitutionally deprived them, and others similarly situated, representation in local government by failing to assign the annexed areas to councilmanic districts. In affirming the Circuit court's judgment, the court ruled that: (1) the ordinances' failure to include a definition of the City's corporate boundaries, under § 36-4-3-3, was irrelevant because Ind. Code § 36-4-3-4 also permitted annexation, and it did not require a definition of the municipality's corporate boundaries; and (2) plaintiffs lacked standing to assert representational challenges to the ordinances because they were not residents of districts that were not councilmanic and their claims, whether based upon remonstrance or declaratory judgment, were time barred because no action was filed to challenge the ordinances within the 60-day limit proscribed by Ind. Code § 36-4-3-11(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

1019 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Reynolds/Herr v. State


No. 87A04-9008-CR-00394


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


582 N.E.2d 833; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 2116



December 11, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE WARRICK SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Edward A. Campbell, Judge. Cause No. 87D01-8910-CF-67


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Warrick Superior Court (Indiana) that, following a jury trial, convicted her of possession of cocaine within 1,000 feet of school property and dealing in cocaine within 1,000 feet of school property.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from convictions for possessing and dealing cocaine near a school. The court held that defendant waived any objection to the admission of evidence of prior drug activity by failing to raise an objection at trial and that the state presented sufficient chain of custody evidence showing that the location of the cocaine was verified at all times. The court also ruled that penalty enhancement for the drug offense due to the proximity to the school did not constitute a violation of the Equal Protection Clause. The classification for high punishment did not involve a "suspect class" or fundamental rights and rationally effectuated the legislature's desires to afford special protection to children from the perils of drug trafficking and to provide harsher penalties for drug peddlers near schools. The court agreed with defendant that possession of cocaine was a lesser included offense of dealing in cocaine and that there was insufficient evidence of a second baggie of cocaine to support the possession charge. The court reversed and remanded the cocaine possession conviction with instructions to vacate the judgment. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, in part, remanding with instructions to vacate defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine within 1,000 feet of school property. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

 

1020 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Casselman v. State


No. 35A04-9102-CR-36


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


582 N.E.2d 432; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 2115



December 10, 1991, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HUNTINGTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Mark A. McIntosh, Judge. Cause No. 35C01-9006-CF-15



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Huntington Circuit Court that convicted him of two counts of molesting a three-year-old child in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-4-3(c) and (d) and one count of sexually battering the child in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-4-8.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred by finding that the three-year-old victim was competent to testify and abused its discretion by refusing to strike all of her testimony, that the trial court erred by allowing the victim's inconsistent testimony to remain in evidence, and that the trial court erred by allowing the victim's videotaped testimony to be admitted because he was unable to cross-examine the victim and the tape was of such poor quality. The court determined that the trial court struck most of the victim's testimony, except that which stated that she talked to a caseworker and that defendant touched her genital area. The court held that it was not an abuse of discretion for the trial court to allow the remaining testimony. The court also held that pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-37-4-6 the videotape was admissible without the necessity of defendant cross-examining the victim because Ind. Code § 35-37-4-6 protected the victim from being subjected to cross-examination. The court concluded that the process was not unconstitutional. The court finally held that the quality of the videotape was a determination to be made within the discretion of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Low v. State


No. 29A04-9106-CR-1971


1 This case was diverted to this office by order of the Chief Judge.


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


580 N.E.2d 737; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1881



November 14, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Hamilton County Court Court; The Honorable Harry L. Sauce, Presiding Judge & Daniel Pfleging, Judge Pro-Tem; Cause No. 29E01-9003-CM-M0104.



DISPOSITION: Low's conviction for obscene performance is reversed and her conviction for refusing to aid an officer is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her convictions from the Hamilton County Court (Indiana) for obscene performance and refusing to assist a law enforcement officer after she accompanied an undercover officer to a hotel room as part of her job with an escort service.


OVERVIEW: A police department was investigating suspected prostitution activity. As part of the investigation, the undercover officer rented two adjoining rooms at a hotel. The officer telephoned the escort service and requested an escort. The officer met defendant and her driver later that evening. The driver made the officer sign a service agreement stating that defendant's services did not include sexual activity, massage, or lewd or obscene performances. The driver left defendant with the officer. Defendant performed a "bed dance" for the officer. Next, the officer watched defendant masturbate. The officer signaled other officers in the adjoining room, and defendant was arrested. The escort service called the room to check on defendant. The police told defendant not to alert the caller that they were present. Defendant's driver never came to pick her up. Defendant was convicted of obscene performance and refusing to assist a law enforcement officer. The court affirmed the conviction for refusing to assist a law enforcement officer on appeal. However, the court reversed the obscene performance conviction. The court reasoned that defendant's conduct occurred in a private setting.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for refusing to assist a law enforcement officer. However, the court reversed defendant's conviction for obscene performance.

 

1022 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Carr v. Carr


No. 79A04-9011-CV-536


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


580 N.E.2d 966; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1888



November 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Tippecanoe Superior Court 2; The Honorable George Heid, Judge Pro Tem; Cause No. S2-438-72.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the decision of the Tippecanoe Superior Court (Indiana), which ruled in favor of appellee mother and ordered the father to pay all reasonable and necessary tuition, room and board, fees, books, and supplies for his daughter's college education.


OVERVIEW: Following the parties' divorce, the mother was awarded custody of their daughter. The father was ordered to pay child support. When the daughter reached college age, the mother brought an action to modify the support provisions of the divorce decree. Pursuant to the Indiana Child Support Guidelines, the trial court ordered the father to pay all reasonable and necessary tuition, room and board, fees, books, and supplies for his daughter's college education. The mother was ordered to pay all of her miscellaneous college expenses. On appeal, the court affirmed the determination. The court held that a modification of a child support order was within the sound discretion of the trial court and that the trial court had the discretion of including educational expenses when calculating the basic child support obligation or in ordering the educational expenses as a separate award. In addition, providing the noncustodial parent a role in the child's education was also within the sound discretion of the trial court. The court further determined that Ind. Code § 31-1-11.5-12(b)(1) did not violate either the Due Process Clause or the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, which modified the support provisions of the divorce decree, requiring the father to pay his daughter's expenses for college.

Rossman v. Dunson


No. 29A02-9010-CV-6391


1 This case was diverted to this office by order of the Chief Judge.


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


580 N.E.2d 304; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1735



October 29, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Hamilton County Superior Court, Room No. 3; The Honorable William J. Hughes, Judge; Cause No. 29D03-8908-CP-478.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant purchasers sought review of a judgment of the Hamilton County Superior Court (Indiana) granting summary judgment for appellee alleged property owner and quieting title to property in his name, based on former Ind. Code § 6-1.1-25-4, which, prior to 1988 provided for a two-year redemption period.


OVERVIEW: The purchasers claimed that the trial court erred in applying a pre-1988 version of § 6-1.1-25-4. They claimed that the alleged property owner failed to redeem property sold at an October 8, 1987 tax sale within the period required by the amended statute. On review, the court agreed with the purchasers and reversed the grant of summary judgment. The 1988 amendment to the statute reduced the redemption period from two years to one year. A tax deed was issued to the purchasers on March 28, 1989. On May 17, 1989 they brought the quiet title action, and at that point, the alleged property owner attempted to redeem. The court found that the alleged property owner received sufficient notice of the tax sale, as required by Ind. Code § 6-1.1-25-6 (1988). Moreover, the court rejected the claim of the alleged property owner that the redemption period was unlawfully extended by a county auditor when considering which version of redemption statute to apply. The court found that any extension was not harmful and was not a basis for further extending any redemption rights. The court held that application of the statute as amended in 1988 did not violate any constitutional or contract rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment and quieting title in the alleged property owner.

 

1024 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


McCallip v. State


No. 41A04-9106-CR-1771


1 This case was diverted to this office by order of the Chief Judge.


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


580 N.E.2d 278; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1730



October 28, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Johnson Circuit Court; The Honorable Jeffrey C. Eggers, Judge; Cause No. 41C01-9001-CP-00010.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction for conspiracy to commit burglary, which was rendered in the Johnson Circuit Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his accomplice agreed to break into a residence. They walked to a residence and rang the doorbell. When the owner came to the door, the two men ran and were later apprehended. Defendant appealed from his conviction for conspiracy to commit burglary, and the court affirmed. The court held that Ind. Code § 35-36-4-1, which prescribed a time within which defendant had to allege the alibi defense, and Ind. Code § 35-34-1-2, which related to the particularity required of informations, did not violate due process. The court held that due process required reasonable notice, an opportunity for fair hearing, and the right to have a court of competent jurisdiction hear one's cause, and that the two statutes did not violate any of the enumerated requirements. The court held that the information sufficiently apprised defendant for alibi purposes that he was being tried for an offense occurring around a certain date. If defendant had raised an alibi defense, the prosecutor was required to provide a more specific date, and this was an adequate procedure by which defendant could raise an alibi defense. The court also found sufficient evidence to sustain the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1025 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Roddel v. Floro


No. 12A02-8907-CV-337


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


580 N.E.2d 255; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1710



October 21, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Transfer March 19, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Clinton Circuit Court; The Honorable Jack R. O'Neill, Judge; Cause No. 86-383.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen appealed an order of the Clinton Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed his claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and for personal injury against defendants, the county, town, and law enforcement officials, for failure to state a claim under Ind. R. Trial P. 12(B)(6). The citizen had also sought a declaration that Ind. Code §§ 9-4-1-25 and 36-8-3-6 were unconstitutional. The circuit court held that the statutes were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The citizen sought to recover for injuries sustained in a high-speed police chase. He alleged that a roadblock set up by police was unreasonable because the chase was unjustified. The circuit court held for defendants. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court properly dismissed the § 1983 complaint. Only roadblocks designed to cause death or serious bodily injury were sufficiently unreasonable to invoke § 1983 liability. The citizen did not allege that the roadblock was so designed. He merely claimed that any roadblock used to stop him was unreasonable because there was no reason for the stop. He also claimed that the town and county were liable for failing to adequately train the police to prevent a deprivation of his constitutional rights. Also, the trial court correctly dismissed the personal injury claim. The court rejected the citizen's contention that he was subject to false arrest or imprisonment and that, as a result, defendants' immunity was at issue. The citizen was guilty of resisting arrest, thus, he was not subject to false arrest or imprisonment, as a matter of law and defendants were immune. In addition, Ind. Code §§ 9-4-1-25 and 36-8-3-6 were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's dismissal of the citizen's complaint against the county, town, and law enforcement officials. The court also affirmed the circuit court's finding that the statutes were constitutional.

Jarrett v. State


No. 26A01-9104-PC-114


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


580 N.E.2d 245; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1675



October 17, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied January 23, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Gibson Circuit Court; The Honorable William H. Miller, Special Judge; Cause No. C-85-329.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order from the Gibson Circuit Court (Indiana) denying his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of child molesting. His conviction was affirmed on direct appeal. He then filed a petition for post-conviction relief, which was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that defendant failed to meet his burden of establishing grounds for relief. His trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to object to the trial court's proper determination that the victim was competent to testify at trial, failing to object when the trial court allowed cumulative testimony of four witnesses repeating allegations made by the victim against defendant, failing to object to a properly admitted testimony by a doctor, failing to object to prosecutorial remarks that drew logical conclusions from the evidence, failing to object to properly admitted evidence of defendant's prior sexual misconduct, failing to object to the trial court's jury instructions when as a whole they accurately described the law, and failing to object to aggravating factors that the trial court found justified an enhanced sentence. The other errors raised by defendant were waived because there was no apparent reason they could not have been raised at trial or in his direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

Gallagher v. Indiana State Election Bd.


No. 49A02-9007-CV-431


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


579 N.E.2d 649; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1668



October 16, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Petition for Transfer Granted August 28, 1992, Reported at 1992 Ind. LEXIS 201.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Marion Superior Court; Civil Division, Room 1; The Honorable Anthony M. Metz III, Judge; Cause No. 49D01-8810-CP-1489.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, representative of one subclass of voters and representative of a second subclass of voters, sought review of a decision of the Marion Superior Court, Civil Division (Indiana), which held that Ind. Code § 3-7-3-5 (1991) and Ind. Code § 3-7-4-1 et seq. (1988) did not violate the Indiana Constitution or the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellants brought an action to challenge voting provision of the Indiana Code. The challenged provisions allowed voters who moved to a new precinct within the same county who had filed a timely transfer request, to return to the former precinct and vote in the election. Those voters who moved to a new precinct within the same county and who failed to file a timely transfer request could only vote for President and Vice President. The trial court held that the challenged provisions did not violate either the state constitution or the federal constitution. On appeal, the court reversed and determined that the challenged provisions violated the Equal Protection Clause of the federal constitution. The court held that the proper standard of review was strict scrutiny because the right to vote was a fundamental right. The court found that there was no compelling state interest in limiting the franchise of the various subclasses of voters who moved to a new precinct within 30 days of an election.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision. The court held that the challenged voting provisions violated the Equal Protection Clause of the federal constitution.

 

1028 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


S.V. v. Estate of Bellamy


No. 18A02-9010-CV-570


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


579 N.E.2d 144; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1660



October 10, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Delaware Circuit Court; The Honorable Steven R. Caldemeyer, Judge; Cause No. 18C01-8905-JP-82.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother appealed the decision of the Delaware Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed her complaint for paternity filed against defendant, the estate of the alleged deceased father. The deceased was allegedly the unborn child's father.


OVERVIEW: The mother brought an action for paternity on behalf of her unborn child against the estate of the deceased. The trial court dismissed the action. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that, for inheritance purposes, Ind. Code § 29-1-2-7(b) required paternity actions to be filed within five months after the death of the putative father, notwithstanding the fact that the action was filed on behalf of a posthumous child. The court concluded that § 29-1-2-7(b) reflected a careful balance of the State's interest with the illegitimate child's interest and that the statute's five month limitation did not violate the equal protection clause. The court found that, in denying the paternity action, the trial court interpreted § 29-1-2-7(b) to prohibit all paternity actions for any purpose when they were commenced more than five months after the alleged father's death. The court concluded that trial court erred in dismissing the paternity complaint because the five-month limit affected an action only to the extent that it sought to establish a right of inheritance and did not effect the child's other possible claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the mother's action for paternity on behalf of her unborn child against the estate of the deceased and remanded.

Board of Trustees of Indiana Public Employees' Retirement Fund v. Grannan


No. 14A04-9101-CV-2


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


578 N.E.2d 371; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1573



September 25, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied February 26, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Daviess Circuit Court; The Honorable Robert L. Arthur, Judge; Cause No. 14C01-9003-CP-084.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for modification of the trial court's QDRO consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Trustees of Indiana Public Employees' Retirement Fund (PERF) sought review of the decision of the Daviess Circuit Court (Indiana), which found in favor of appellee ex-wife, requiring PERF to distribute appellee ex-husband's PERF retirement benefits to the ex-wife in her declaratory judgment action following the dissolution of their marriage. The trial court granted the motion for a stay of judgment pending appeal filed by PERF.


OVERVIEW: PERF refused to comply with the provisions of the Qualified Domestic Relations Order (QDRO), which had accompanied the parties decree in dissolution and related to the ex-husbands membership in PERF. The trial court granted a declaratory judgment in favor of the ex-wife, ordering PERF to accept and abide by the judgment and implement the QDRO. PERF appealed, and the trial court granted the motion by PERF for a stay of judgment. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for modification of the trial court's QDRO. The court found no supersedure or implied repeal of the PERF statutes. The court held that PERF was not obligated to comply with those portions of the trial court's order that were inconsistent with the PERF statutes. The court ordered the trial court to enter a conforming order because the PERF statutes and the marital dissolution statutes could be harmoniously construed. The court reasoned that the marital dissolution statute had offered the trial court a method of distribution, by setting aside a percentage of the payments either by assignment or in kind at the time of receipt, which was not in violation of the PERF statutes against assignment and attachment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, determining that the PERF statutes and the marital dissolution statutes could be construed harmoniously. The court remanded for modification of the trial court's QDRO.

The doctor filed a physician's statement. The trial court ordered the involuntary commitment of the patient. The court also determined that the trial court did not err in refusing to allow the patient to waive court-appointed counsel and in allowing the doctor access to the patient's medical records. 1032 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Southlake Limousine & Coach, Inc. v. Brock


No. 45A03-9007-CV-259


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


578 N.E.2d 677; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1515



September 16, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Lake Superior Court, Civil Division, Room 1; The Honorable Cordell C. Pinkerton, Judge; Cause No. 45D01-8903-CT-207.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee decedent's estate brought a wrongful death action, pursuant to Ind. Code § 34-1-1-2 (1988), against appellant tortfeasor after the decedent was killed in an automobile accident. The tortfeasor admitted liability, so the issue before the Lake Superior Court, Civil Division (Indiana) was solely the amount of damages due to the decedent's estate. The tortfeasor sought view of the damage award.


OVERVIEW: The parties did not dispute the testimony regarding the decedent's life expectancy, personal characteristics, future lost earnings, and future lost household services. The tortfeasor argued that the expert economist's testimony valuing the decedent's life should not have been admitted because it was not an aid to the jury in valuing the loss of affection and love to the husband and the loss of parental training and guidance to the children. The court agreed. The court found that Ind. Code § 34-1-1-2 (1988) limited the measure of damages for a wrongful death action to compensation for the pecuniary loss sustained by the plaintiffs in the action, and that damages for the estimated value of the life lost were not recoverable. The court concluded that because the jury was able to determine the loss of affection, love, parental training, and guidance from its own experiences and through the testimony of the survivors, the expert's testimony regarding these losses invaded the province of the jury. The court found that questions regarding annuities and the cost of annuities was relevant to determining the present value of damages and should have been admitted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.

Webb v. State


No. 49A02-8901-CR-00029


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


575 N.E.2d 1066; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1319



August 13, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Transfer Denied December 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion County Municipal Court; Room Number 4; The Honorable William S. Mercuri, Judge; Cause No. A487-3638.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Marion County Municipal Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of prostitution, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-45-4-2 (1988).


OVERVIEW: As part of a police investigation, the informant hired defendant for a $ 150 "fantasy session." During the session, defendant performed a "bed dance" while disrobing over the informant. For an additional $ 50, defendant inserted a flesh-colored penis-shaped object into her anus. Thereafter, defendant was convicted of prostitution, pursuant to § 35-45-4-2. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that § 35-45-4-2 was not void for vagueness because the statute placed defendant on notice that an agreement to perform deviate sexual conduct for money was prohibited. Moreover, Ind. Code § 35-41-1-9 (1988) specifically included anal insertion within the definition of "deviate sexual conduct." Further, § 35-45-4-2 was not unconstitutionally overbroad because it was the blatant commercialization of sexual conduct that was subject to legislative censure as opposed to the autoerotic conduct itself. Additionally, § 35-45-4-2 furthered the substantial governmental interest of protecting the public order, safety, and welfare. Thus, § 35-45-4-2 could constitutionally be applied to defendant's non-obscene performance. Finally, sufficient evidence supported defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for prostitution.

Hensley v. State


No. 49A02-9006-CR-320


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


575 N.E.2d 1053; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1291



August 8, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 1, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division One; The Honorable John T. Tranberg, Judge; Cause No. CR87-305A.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division One (Indiana), which convicted him of rape and confinement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape and confinement. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that defendant was competent to stand trial. The court held that Ind. Code § 35-36-3-1(1990) governing competency did not violate a defendant's right to due process because it provided for a hearing and the appointment of at least two disinterested doctors to evaluate defendant. The court concluded that defendant could not complain that instructions were incomplete when he failed to tender any instructions on the issue of guilty but mentally ill. The court held that even if the instruction, which defendant argued should have been given regarding the guilty but mentally ill verdict, had been tendered, it was not a correct statement of the law and refusal of the tendered instruction would not have been error. The court found that the jury was fully and fairly instructed regarding the insanity defense and the possible verdicts. The court held that the admission of mug shots because they were not unduly prejudicial and had substantial independent probative value.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for rape and confinement.

 

1035 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hobble by & Through Hobble v. Basham


No. 22A04-9006-CV-290


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


575 N.E.2d 693; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1289



August 5, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Floyd Superior Court; The Honorable Richard G. Striegel, Judge; Cause No. 22D01-8710-CP-154.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury action, plaintiff sought review of the judgment of the Floyd Superior Court (Indiana), which ruled that New Albany, Indiana, Ordinance § 116, relating to warning lights and devices on ice cream trucks was invalid because it was in conflict with Ind. Code § 9-8-6-29. The judgment complained of was rendered in plaintiff's action alleging defendants' ice cream truck was not in compliance with the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was struck by a car as she crossed the street to buy ice cream from defendants' truck. Plaintiff argued that defendants were negligent in that their truck failed to comply with the ordinance's requirements for warning lights and devices that would have warned defendant car driver to be alert for pedestrians. The trial court ruled that the ordinance was invalid because it conflicted with the state statute regulating vehicle warning lights. Plaintiff appealed. The court found that the city had authority to adopt the ordinance so long as the ordinance did not conflict with statutory provisions. The court found further that the ordinance's warning light provision requiring alternating flashing red lights on the front of ice cream trucks conflicted with the statute requiring that warning lights on the front of vehicles be white or amber, and permitting flashing red lights only on emergency vehicles. The court concluded, however, that the trial court erred in invalidating the entire ordinance because the ordinance also required safety measures other than the flashing lights, and the latter portion of the ordinance was severable, complete, and capable of execution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment that invalidated the entire ordinance relating to safety provisions, warning lights, and devices applicable to ice cream trucks. The court remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion that although the warning light provision of the ordinance was invalid, the remainder of the ordinance was severable, complete, and capable of execution.

 

1036 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Sturgeon v. State


No. 79A02-9007-CR-4131


1 This case was reassigned to this office on July 1, 1991.


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


575 N.E.2d 679; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1285



July 31, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Tippecanoe County Court 1; The Honorable Donald C. Johnson, Special Judge; Cause No. 79E01-8812-CF-479.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, Ind. Code § 9-11-2, from the Tippecanoe County Court (Indiana), alleging the jury instructions impermissibly shifted to him the burden of persuasion on the element of intoxication.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, Ind. Code § 9-11-2. On appeal, the court reviewed the challenged jury instruction concerning the evidentiary effect of defendant's blood alcohol content (BAC) test and concluding that the instruction was irrefutably mandatory in that it failed to inform the jury that they have a choice or might infer the desired conclusion. Nowhere in the challenged instruction or the charge as a whole did the trial court inform the jury that the presumption of BAC at the time of operation was rebuttable, therefore, the presumption created by the instruction was conclusive as well as mandatory. However, the erroneous instruction did not compare with the kinds of errors that automatically required the reversal of an otherwise valid conviction so the court first considered the entire record to determine if the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Because the record indicated conflicting evidence of defendant's intoxication, the erroneous instruction could not be considered harmless. The conviction was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction. Given the inconclusive nature of the evidence of appearance of intoxication and the conflicting opinion of the bartender that defendant did not appear intoxicated, the court was unable to conclude that the constitutionally infirm instruction was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

1037 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Chamness v. Carter


No. 34A02-9010-CV-5871


1 This case has been diverted to this office by order of the Chief Judge.


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fifth District


575 N.E.2d 317; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1228



July 23, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Howard Superior Court, Division No. 1; The Honorable Dennis H. Parry, Judge; Cause No. 34D01-9004-CT-00007.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father, a non-custodial parent, challenged the decision of the Howard Superior Court, Division No. 1 (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee tortfeasor in an action for the wrongful death of a minor child.


OVERVIEW: The child had been killed while the custodial parent was visiting the home of the tortfeasor and the child was negligently shot and killed by the tortfeasor's son. The issue was whether a divorced non-custodial parent had standing to bring an action for the wrongful death of a minor child under Ind. Code § 34-1-1-8. On review, the court reversed and remanded, holding that § 34-1-1-8 conferred standing upon a non-custodial parent. The court found that, when looked at as a whole, the statute clearly intended that a non-custodial parent be entitled to compensation for the wrongful death or injury of their child. The court also found that both parents were liable for the medical and funeral bills of a child because of their common law, and in some instances statutory, duty to support and maintain their children. The court determined that the apportionment of damages for loss of a child's services and a child's love and affection is a question of fact to be determined at trial or between the parents. The court concluded that there was no rational basis for denying a non-custodial parent standing to recover for loss occasioned by the injury or death of a child.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment in favor of the tortfeasor in an action for the wrongful death of a child was reversed and remanded.

 

1038 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


In re Grissom


No. 77A01-9008-CV-340


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


573 N.E.2d 440; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 939



June 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Sullivan Circuit Court; The Honorable David K. Johnson, Special Judge; Cause No. 77C01-8801-JP-001.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the order of the Sullivan Circuit Court (Indiana), which changed custody of the parties' daughter to appellee father as a result of the father's petition for custody.


OVERVIEW: The father filed a petition for custody of the daughter alleging that the mother left the state with the daughter without notifying him or the trial court and that his visitation rights were violated. The trial court entered an order changing custody to the father based on its finding that it was in the best interest of the daughter. On appeal by the mother, the court reversed the order because the wrong standard was used by the court. The court found that generally it was in a child's best interest to require a substantial and continuing change in circumstances before modifying a custody order. Therefore, in a custody modification proceeding arising out of a paternity action under Ind. Code § 31-6-6.1-11(e), the petitioning party had to have demonstrated a substantial and continuing change in circumstances so as to make the existing custody order unreasonable under Ind. Code § 31-1-11.5-22(d). Section § 31-1-11.5-22(d) applied to modification cases arising out of marriage dissolution. Because the mother was caring for the daughter with the help of the grandmother, a substantial and continuing change in circumstances warranting a change of custody did not exist.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that changed custody of the daughter from the mother to the father in the father's petition for custody.

Kerlin v. State


No. 32A01-9009-CR-370


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


573 N.E.2d 445; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 943



June 12, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 23, 1991. Rehearing Denied January 31, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal From the Hendricks Circuit Court; The Honorable Robert M. Hall, Special Judge; Cause No. 32C01-9003-CF-68.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Hendricks Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss the indictments charging defendant with neglect of a dependent in violation of Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a physician, was charged with violating the neglect of a dependent statute, Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4, by knowingly or intentionally placing dependents, patients who were under defendant's care, in situations that endangered the lives and the health of the dependents. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment denying defendant's motion to dismiss the indictments. The court held that § 35-46-1-4 was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad as applied to defendant because no reasonable person of ordinary intelligence would have difficulty determining that failure to give necessary or proper medical care was proscribed by the neglect statute. The court ruled that the indictments were sufficient to inform defendant of the charges against him because the indictments specified the date and place of the alleged offenses and identified defendant and the victims in language paralleling the words of § 35-46-1-4.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying defendant's motion to dismiss the indictments charging defendant with neglect of a dependent.

 

1040 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Metro Holding Co. v. Mitchell


No. 49A02-9004-CV-207


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


571 N.E.2d 580; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 800



 May 22, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 7, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Marion County Superior Court; Room No. 5; The Honorable James S. Kirsch, Judge; Cause No. 49D05-8906-CP-846.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is reversed and this cause remanded with instructions to enter judgment for Metro in its quiet title action and against Mitchell on his action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a buyer of real estate at a tax-sale, challenged a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which denied the buyer's motion for summary judgment in the buyer's action to quiet title in the property. The trial court granted the owner's motion for summary judgment summary judgment in the owner's counterclaim to declare the tax-sale void.


OVERVIEW: At the time of the tax-sale, Ind. Code § 6-1.1-25-4 (1982) provided a two-year period in which the owner could redeem the land. Pub. L. No. 89-1987, § 5 (Ind.) reduced the redemption period to one year. The owner received a notice of tax sale redemption but did not redeem the property, and the county auditor issued a tax deed to the buyer. In the buyer's action to quiet title, the trial court found that Ind. Code § 6-1.1-25-4 (1982) granted the owner a contract right to redeem the property for two years and the application of the reduced one-year redemption period was an unconstitutional impairment of the owner's contract rights. On appeal, the court disagreed and held that the 1987 amendment did not violate the contract clauses of U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10 and Ind. Const. art. I, § 24. The right of redemption did not create a contractual right but was a remedy accorded by the state as a matter of grace. Thus, the state legislature could constitutionally shorten the redemption period after the tax-sale occurred. Because the owner did not have a vested right in a two-year redemption period, there was no unconstitutional taking when the redemption period was shortened to one year.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the action with instructions to enter judgment for the buyer in its quiet title action and against the owner on his counterclaim to declare the tax-sale void.
