National Salvage & Service Corp. v. Commissioner of Indiana Dep't of Environmental Management


No. 49A04-8912-CV-554


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


571 N.E.2d 548; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 781



 May 15, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Transfer Denied March 5, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Circuit Court; The Honorable John M. Ryan, Judge; Cause No. 49C01-8910-M13752.



DISPOSITION: For all of the foregoing reasons, we affirm.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant solid waste transporter appealed the decision of the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted a preliminary injunction against it in the action of plaintiff Commissioner of the Indiana Department of Environmental Management (commissioner), seeking a preliminary and permanent injunction against the solid waste transporter's business.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner filed a complaint, which sought a preliminary and permanent injunction against the solid waste transporter's business that did not have a solid waste permit. The trial court granted a preliminary injunction, and the solid waste transporter appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the order granting the preliminary injunction. The solid waste transporter was required to get a solid waste permit under Ind. Admin. Code tit. 329, § 2-8-1 because it fell under the definition of a "waste processing facility" in Ind. Admin. Code tit. 329, § 2-2-1. It was transferring solid waste from one vehicle or container through its building to another vehicle or container for transportation. The court rejected the solid waste transporter's claim that Ind. Admin. Code § 2-8-1 was unconstitutionally vague because it gave fair notice of who needed a permit when interpreted. The public interest exception to the rule that estoppel did not ordinarily apply to the government was inapplicable because the public policy of protecting the citizenry by disallowing any facility which contributes to pollution without prior approval outweighed the solid waste transporter's economic interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting a preliminary injunction in the commissioner's action against the solid waste transporter's business, which was operating without a solid waste permit.

Everroad v. State


No. 03A01-9005-CR-179


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


570 N.E.2d 38; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 618



 April 15, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Bartholomew Superior Court; The Honorable John A. Westhafter, Special Judge; Cause No. SCR-1791.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a decision by the Bartholomew Superior Court (Indiana) that rendered judgment on a jury verdict against them, finding them guilty of several charges of dealing in controlled substances and sentencing them to consecutive terms.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were present at their mother's home when the police arrived to execute a search warrant for a stolen television. Although the television was not found, the police observed large quantities of drug and contraband throughout the home. As a result, all occupants were arrested. However, defendants' trial did not take place until approximately two years later due to several continuances by defendants. On appeal, defendants contended that the lower court erred in not discharging them pursuant to Ind. R. Crim. P. 4(c), when their trial was delayed for more than one year from their arrest, and in denying their motion to suppress. The court found no grounds for reversible error. The court held that: (1) any delays caused by defendants' acts extended the one-year time limitation by the length of such delays, including any failures to object to the delays; (2) defendants had no standing to challenge the search of their mother's home because they had no reasonable expectation of privacy in a home that they were merely visiting; and (3) absent bad faith on the part of police, the failure to preserve fingerprints or other evidence did not constitute a due process violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction in part, reversed in part, and remanded for resentencing.

 

1043 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Fordyce v. State


No. 48A02-8906-CR-00263


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


569 N.E.2d 357; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 450



March 28, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Madison County Court; The Honorable Larry W. Robbins, Judge; Cause Nos. 48E02-8711-CF-206, 48E02-8711-CF-208.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, book seller and corporation, appealed a decision of the Madison County Court (Indiana), which convicted them of distributing obscene matter that described sexual conduct involving a person under 16 years of age pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-49-3-1(2) (1988).


OVERVIEW: A police officer entered the corporation's bookstore and purchased two books from the seller. Both books were fictional, contained no photographs, and did not state the age of the characters. Based on the content of the books, defendants were convicted of distributing obscene matter that described sexual conduct involving a person under 16 years of age. On appeal, the court held that defendants failed to rebut the presumption that § 35-49-3-1(2) was constitutional. The trial court concluded that the content of a book proffered for comparison was substantially similar to the two books purchased. However, defendants failed to establish community acceptance of the comparative book or to show that they were prejudiced by its exclusion from evidence. The evidence was sufficient to support the conviction because the state was not required to submit expert testimony in an obscenity case. In affirming, the court held that an obscenity determination could be based solely on the jury's view of the allegedly offensive material. The enhancement portion of the statute applied even to fictional characters, and the jury could conclude that the books' characters were under 16 years of age.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions for distributing obscene matter that described sexual conduct involving a person under 16 years of age and upheld the constitutionality of the statute, including the enhancement aspect, even though the characters were fictional and their ages were never stated.

Whittaker v. Dail


No. 27A02-9007-CV-4241


1 This case has been diverted to this office by the order of the Chief Judge.


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fifth District


567 N.E.2d 816; 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 347



March 4, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Grant Circuit Court; The Honorable Thomas R. Hunt, Judge; Cause No. 27C01-8709-CP-783.



DISPOSITION: The judgment against plaintiff and the denial of the motion for relief from judgment are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee injured party brought an action against appellant tortfeasor for injuries he inflicted upon her in a battery. Even though aware of the trial date, as evident from a call from the trial judge, the tortfeasor failed to appear. The Grant Circuit Court (Indiana) entered a default judgment for the injured party and awarded her $ 98,423.90 in actual damages and $ 198,757.80 punitive damages. The tortfeasor sought review.


OVERVIEW: The tortfeasor had been represented by several attorneys, all of whom withdrew for one reason or another. After the tortfeasor failed to appear for the trial, the trial judge said he was going to enter a default judgment, but evidence was received on the merits as well. In rejecting the tortfeasor's argument that the trial judge was required to give him three days notice under Ind. R. Trial P. 55(B) before entering a default judgment, the court held that even though the trial judge had referred to it as a default judgment, it was in fact a judgment on the merits and the requirements of the rule did not apply. The court then concluded that the tortfeasor's failure to appear constituted a waiver of right to a jury trial under Ind. R. Trial P. 38(D). The award of damages was not so outrageous as to indicate that the trial judge was motivated by passion, prejudice, partiality, or the consideration of improper evidence. The court determined that the double jeopardy clause did not apply to a case between two private litigants, so it was irrelevant that the tortfeasor had pleaded guilty to a battery in connection with the tort and was fined $ 1 and given a 60-day suspended sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial judge who entered judgment for the injured party and awarded her $ 98,423.90 in actual damages and $ 198,757.80 punitive damages.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Shelby Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted her of murder and conspiracy to commit murder. The trial court admitted evidence of defendant's escape from custody after her arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and her lover murdered defendant's husband. Defendant later escaped from custody. Evidence of her escape and of her possession of a handgun were admitted as relevant to the consciousness of her guilt. The court found that no evidentiary rulings were abuses of discretion and that conspiracy, as well as murder, were proved by overwhelming evidence.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Fetner v. Maury Boyd & Assoc., Inc.

1050 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Chandley Enterprises, Inc. v. Evansville


No. 82A01-9009-CV-353


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


563 N.E.2d 672; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 1611



December 13, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied April 18, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Vanderburgh Circuit Court; The Honorable Richard L. Young, Judge; Cause No. 82C01-8905-CP-1902.



DISPOSITION: Chandley has not demonstrated that the trial court's judgment was contrary to law, and we therefore affirm the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord sought review of the judgment of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which ruled in favor of defendant city, in a declaratory judgment action that challenged two city ordinances that prohibited landlords from disconnecting a tenant's utilities.


OVERVIEW: The landlord leased property with a clause that provided that it could disconnect utilities if the tenant failed to pay rent. When the tenant failed to pay rent, the landlord disconnected the utilities. The city ordered the landlord to reconnect the utilities based upon city ordinances that prevented landlords from shutting off utilities. The landlord argued that the ordinances were unconstitutional. The court held that the prohibition against impairment of contracts had no application to the lease because the lease was entered after the ordinances were in force. The court also held that the ordinances were not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. Further, the prohibition against impairment of contracts did not restrict the exercise of the state's police power to protect the public health, safety, and welfare. The ordinances were necessary and reasonable and a proper exercise of the municipality's police power. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied the landlord declaratory relief.

 

1051 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Barco Beverage Corp. v. Indiana Alcoholic Beverage Com.


No. 49A02-8809-CV-343


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


563 N.E.2d 658; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 1603



December 11, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court; The Honorable Anthony J. Metz, Judge; Cause No. S187-1430.



DISPOSITION: The trial court's judgment as to the validity of Rule 28 as it pertains to distillers, rectifiers, and liquor and wholesalers is reversed, but in all other respects the trial court's judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, wholesaler and distributor, sought review of the judgment from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellees, commission, trade associations, and retailers, after determining that the commission did not exceed its statutory authority when it promulgated Ind. Admin. Code tit. 905, § 1-28-1(3) (1979) (Rule 28), prohibiting territorial restraints on the sale of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: The commission enacted Rule 28, which prohibited any person engaged in business as a distiller, brewer, rectifier, vintner, or other producer, importer, or as a wholesaler of liquor, wine, beer or malt beverages, directly or indirectly, or through an affiliate from entering into any agreement restricting sales to a designated area of primary responsibility. The wholesaler and the distributor challenged the validity of Rule 28. The court held that the commission could not enact any rule that exceeded its statutory authority. The court concluded that the commission had the authority to promulgate the rule as it related to brewers, vintners, and beer and wine wholesalers, but the commission exceeded its authority when it included distillers, rectifiers, and liquor wholesalers in the rule. The inclusion of these additional groups expanded the law as established by the legislature, and the agency was prohibited from enacting regulations that exceeded the authority that it was granted by the legislature. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and upheld that regulation as it pertained to brewers, vintners, and beer and wine wholesalers, but the court reversed the portion of the judgment regarding distillers, rectifiers, and liquor wholesalers in the rule.

 

1052 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Mallory v. State


No. 22A01-9003-CR-00104


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


563 N.E.2d 640; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 1610



December 10, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied March 25, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Floyd Superior Court; The Honorable Richard G. Striegel, Judge; Cause No. 22D01-8905-CR-64.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Floyd Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted her of neglect of a dependent as a class B felony, based upon the death of her six-year-old daughter. Defendant claimed she should not have been convicted of neglect of a dependent due to an absence of any evidence that an injury to her dependent was proximately caused by an act of neglect attributable to her.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's daughter showed signs of paralysis on her left side after she received a hit to the forehead when defendant's boyfriend was supposed to be caring for her. Defendant was told she should take her daughter to a doctor, but defendant did not want to take her child to the doctor because the bruises she had caused on the body of the daughter could still be seen. A doctor testified that the child's injury was treatable and, had it been promptly treated, she could have recovered. The trial court convicted defendant of neglect of a dependent as a class B felony. The court affirmed and held that the evidence was sufficient to support the conclusion that defendant had deprived her dependent daughter of support and that the deprivation of support resulted in the death of the dependent. The court held that defendant's act of deprivation of medical support resulted in a substantial risk of death, so substantial that death in fact occurred. The court concluded that the evidence sufficiently supported the element of serious bodily injury in this case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1053 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Myers v. State


No. 1804-9003-CR-1171


1 This case was diverted to this office by direction of the Chief Judge.


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


564 N.E.2d 287; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 1521



November 26, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Delaware Superior Court No. 1; The Honorable Robert L. Barnet, Judge; Cause No. 18D01-8910-CF-36.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is in all things affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Delaware Superior Court No. 1 (Indiana) reflecting a jury verdict finding him guilty of burglary, a Class B felony, and attempted rape, a Class A felony. The superior court denied defendant's motions to exclude evidence discovered in a search and to make an offer of proof of his past sexual activity with the victim pursuant to the rape shield statute, Ind. Code § 35-37-4-4(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant broke into a victim's home, took her pistol, and used it to force her onto her bed. In a struggle while they were undressed, defendant received a gunshot and left in a car that contained the pistol, blood stained gloves, and blood samples. The superior court correctly admitted the evidence from within the car. The court upheld the verdict because it was supported by substantial evidence of probative value. The court determined that the detective obtained valid consent to search the car as required by the U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court held that the detective reasonably believed that the employer possessed common authority over the car for two reasons. First, defendant stated that the car belonged to a company and its registration named his employer. Second, the detective obtained written consent from the employer to search the car and the employer failed to mention defendant's exclusive possession and control of the car. The superior court correctly denied defendant's motion to offer proof of his past sexual history with the victim because it was tendered on the day of trial and Ind. Code § 35-37-4-4(c)(1) required that it be tendered not less than 10 days before trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

 

1054 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. State


No. 49A02-8812-CR-00456


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


560 N.E.2d 561; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 1310



October 11, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion County Municipal Court; Criminal Division IX; The Honorable Charles Wiles, Judge; Cause No. 49F09-8802-CM-11773.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we reverse the judgment and remand for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Marion County Municipal Court (Indiana) for operating a motor vehicle with .10 percent or more by weight of alcohol in his blood.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for erratic driving and arrested after the officer smelled a strong odor of alcohol coming from defendant's car. A blood alcohol content (BAC) test conducted at 1:55 a.m., 25 minutes after the stop, revealed a BAC of .10 percent. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court's jury instruction that allowed the jury to presume that defendant had a .10 percent at the time he operated the vehicle created a mandatory presumption which was unconstitutional because it shifted to him the burden of proof upon an element of the crime, his BAC at the time of the offense. The court held that the instruction, which paralleled the language of Ind. Code § 9-11-4-15(b) (Cum. Supp. 1990), did not create a conclusive presumption or shift the burden of proof to defendant. It was not unconstitutional because it was permissible to place the burden on defendant to establish facts that would mitigate his culpability for a crime. The court reversed, however, because the instruction failed to advise the jury of its right to reject the presumption, and was thus subject to a mandatory interpretation which could have misled the jury with regard to its duty and prerogatives.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for a new trial.

 

1055 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hastings v. State


No. 61A01-9001-CR-13


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


560 N.E.2d 664; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 1313



October 9, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 12, 1990. Transfer Denied February 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Parke Circuit Court; The Honorable Earl M. Dowd, Judge; Cause No. 61C01-8805-CF-41.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction for neglect of a dependent under Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4, entered in the Parke Circuit Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's boyfriend had previously abused defendant's son and broke both of the boy's legs. The child was again injured by the boyfriend and suffered a broken arm when defendant left the child alone with the boyfriend, which she was not permitted to do. The county child services agency took steps to terminate defendant's parental rights, and she was convicted of neglect of a dependent. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction because it found that defendant's statements to the caseworker that the boyfriend abused the child were made only in response to threats made by the caseworker, indicating that defendant's parental rights could be terminated if she failed to cooperate. The totality of the circumstances suggested that defendant's statements were made under compulsion. The state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant's statements constituted a voluntary confession. The trial court erred in admitting evidence of defendant's comments concerning her suspicions of the boyfriend because such evidence violated defendant's Fifth Amendment right against self-incrimination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for neglect of a dependent.

 

1056 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Keyes v. State


No. 08A02-8911-CR-00577


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


559 N.E.2d 1216; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 1270



September 27, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Carroll Superior Court; The Honorable Jeffery R. Smith, Judge; Cause No. 08D01-8812-CM-259.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Carroll Superior Court (Indiana) convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle with a blood alcohol content greater than .10 percent in violation of Ind. Code § 9-11-2-1 (1988). He appealed and asserted that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction. He also argued that the statutory presumption of intoxication found in Ind. Code § 9-11-4-15(b) (1988) impermissibly shifted the burden of proof from the State.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped defendant for speeding. The officer administered a field sobriety test, which defendant failed. A breath test administered at the police station, within three hours of defendant's arrest, revealed a blood alcohol content of .13 percent. Based on that reading, defendant was presumed, pursuant to § 9-11-4-15(b), to have been driving with at least .10 percent alcohol in his blood. On appeal, defendant argued that § 9-11-4-15(b) was unconstitutional because it relieved the State from proving his blood alcohol content at the time of the offense and put the burden of proving a lower blood alcohol content on him. The court rejected defendant's error claims. Section 9-11-4-15(b) was constitutional; it merely shifted the burden of going forward. The State still had to prove all of the elements of the crime. The State had to prove all of the elements of § 9-11-4-15(b) in order to raise the presumption. The breath tests were properly admitted. The State had not only presented defendant's breath test results, but had shown that the test was properly administered. The evidence fully supported the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1057 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Indianapolis Convention & Visitors Ass'n v. Indianapolis Newspapers, Inc.


No. 30A04-8910-CV-441


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


559 N.E.2d 356; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 1187; 18 Media L. Rep. 1101



September 11, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 15, 1990. Reported at 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 1447.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Hancock Circuit Court; The Honorable Ronald L. Gottschalk, Judge; Cause No. 30C01-8908-CP-412.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant association sought review of the decision of the Hancock Circuit Court (Indiana), which held that the association was a governmental entity subject to the Indiana Access to Public Records Act and ordered it to produce, subject to a protective order, its expense records and vouchers for its officials for 1978-1989.


OVERVIEW: A corporation demanded that the association (ICVA) produce copies of internal expense vouchers for its officials for the years 1978-1989 and ICVA refused. ICVA sought a declaratory judgment against the corporation that it was not a public agency subject to the Indiana Access to Public Records Act. The lower court found that the association was a public entity and had to produce its records and vouchers and the court affirmed. The court found that the revenue that ICVA received from the Capital Improvement Board of Managers of Marion County, Indiana (CIB) was 60-70 percent of ICVA's total revenue. The court concluded that by virtue of the receipt of the CIB funds to support and maintain the ICVA, the ICVA became an entity subject to audit by the Indiana State Board of Accounts. Once it was subject to the audit, ICVA was considered a public agency and as such, the public had the right to access its records.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision and held that the association had to provide its records and vouchers.

 

1058 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Gainer v. Brown


No. 49A02-8812-CV-459


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


558 N.E.2d 867; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 1088



August 20, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court No. 1; Civil Division; The Honorable Anthony J. Metz, Judge; Cause No. S187-1739.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, purchasers under a recorded real estate contract, sought review of a judgment from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which ruled in favor of defendants, purchasers at a tax sale, county auditor, and county treasurer in an action to quiet title to real estate.


OVERVIEW: The purchasers filed an action against defendants to quiet title to real estate. The superior court ruled in favor of defendants. On appeal, the purchasers claimed that the tax sale and tax deed were void as to them because they were not given notice of the tax sale or notice of intent to issue a tax deed. The court reversed the judgment ruling in favor of defendants and remanded for entry of a judgment that the purchasers had the right to redeem their interest. The court held that the superior court erred in enforcing the tax sale against the purchasers' interest under a recorded contract of sale, because the county auditor's failure to provide the purchasers with notice of the tax sale proceedings violated the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. Therefore, the tax sale and subsequent deed did not terminate the purchasers' interest in the subject real estate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's judgment ruling in favor of defendants and remanded for entry of a judgment that the purchasers had the right to redeem their interest in the subject real estate.

Minder v. Martin Luther Home Foundation


No. 61A04-8908-CV-00341


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


558 N.E.2d 833; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 1051



August 13, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Parke Circuit Court; The Honorable Earl M. Dowd, Judge; Cause No. 61C01-8706-CP-120.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners appealed a decision from the Parke Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered a summary judgment in favor of defendant, an adult group home. The homeowners sought a declaratory judgment that would have prohibited, as a violation of restrictive deed covenants, the presence of the adult group home in their subdivision.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners contended that the trial court erred in entering a summary judgment and in improperly converting the adult group home's motion to dismiss into a summary judgment. The court disagreed. The court's majority agreed with a dissent in a cited case which, under similar facts, held that group homes did not violate the restrictive covenants contained in the deeds, a group home was the type of building, single family dwelling, permitted by the covenants, and the uses were residential, not the business uses prohibited by the covenants. Ind. Code § 16-13-21-14.1, authorizing the location of group homes for developmentally disabled and mentally ill persons in single family residential subdivisions, did not violate due process and did not unconstitutionally impair the homeowners' contracts because it was a legitimate and narrowly drawn exercise of police power. Finally, the homeowners' failure to present a complete record to the court waived any alleged error based on absent material.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1060 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Brownlee v. State


No. 49A04-8904-CR-123


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


555 N.E.2d 505; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 713



June 19, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion County Superior Court; The Honorable David McNamar, Judge; Cause No. 49G01-8801-CF-07163.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of attempted murder and attempted robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered an oil station and pulled a pistol out of his pants. The store manager, who was not paying attention and did not realize what was going on, started to walk to the back room, and defendant shot him in the head. Defendant was convicted of attempted murder and attempted robbery. During deliberations, the jury sent a note to the trial court which indicated that two jurors were unable to hear the tape of the alibi witness's testimony and requested that the tape be replayed. Without consulting the parties, the trial court said no. Neither party was aware of the communication. When defendant's counsel discovered the communication, she filed a belated motion to correct error, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the action. There was no indication that defendant knew or could have known of the communication until his appellate counsel received the transcript. Thus, a crucial issue was, in effect, concealed from defendant and thereby not raised in his original motion. Under the facts, the trial court erred in not permitting defendant to raise the issue by way of belated motion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the action.

 

1061 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Ulrich v. State


No. 46A03-9002-CV-48


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


555 N.E.2d 172; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 677



June 11, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 23, 1990. Transfer Denied December 3, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Laporte Superior Court; Room Three; The Honorable Paul J. Baldoni, Judge; Cause No. 46D03 8901 MI024.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pro se appellant, a former high school special education teacher, sought review of a judgment of the Laporte Superior Court (Indiana), which affirmed the revocation of his Indiana teacher's license by appellee, the State Board of Education. On appeal, he contended that the initial hearing notice failed to comply with Ind. Code. § 4-21.5-3-20(c) (1988) and that the revocation was not supported by substantial evidence.


OVERVIEW: The teacher was convicted of raping a student. His conviction was reversed on the ground that the trial court had erred in allowing a State's expert witness to testify that the victim was credible. He was acquitted of a rape charge against another student. At the hearing on the revocation of the teacher's license, the State introduced a transcript of the victim's trial testimony describing the rape. The Board revoked his license, and the trial court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The transcript was sufficient evidence of the teacher's immorality and misconduct in office to revoke his license under Ind. Code. § 4-21.5-3. Ind. Code. § 20-6.1-3-7(a) (1), (2), Also, the complaint and notice of hearing complied with Ind. Code. § 4-21.5-3-20(c)(2) (1988) where it was signed by the attorney who appeared before the Board. Further, the State was not required, under § 4-21.5-3-20(c)(2)(6) (1988), to include the name, title, address and phone number of an administrative law judge when the Board acted as such. It was entitled to do so by Ind. Code. § 4-21.5-3-9(a)(1) (1988) as the ultimate authority for teacher licensing under Ind. Code. §§ 20-6.1-3-1, 7 and 4-21.5-1-15 (1988).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1062 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Harts v. Caylor-Nickel Hosp., Inc.


No. 05A02-8907-CV-323


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


553 N.E.2d 874; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 572



May 10, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 7, 1990. Transfer Denied April 23, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Blackford Circuit Court; The Honorable Bruce C. Bade, Judge; Cause No. 05C01-8703-CP-032.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of a judgment from the Blackford Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted defendant hospital's motion for judgment on the evidence in the patient's action against the hospital for negligence.


OVERVIEW: The patient, an elderly man, fell from his hospital bed because the rails on the bed had been lowered. He broke his hip and brought an action against the hospital for negligence. He did not initially present his case to a medical review panel in accordance with the Medical Malpractice Act (Act), Ind. Code §§ 16-9.5-1-1 through 16-9.5-10-5 (1988). The jury found the patient 25 percent at fault and the hospital 75 percent at fault. The trial court granted the hospital's motion for judgment on the evidence on the ground that the action fell within the Act. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded with instructions to the trial court to reinstate the jury's verdict. The patient's complaint supported an allegation of ordinary negligence. He did not allege any breach of duty directly associated with medical negligence that was integral to the rendering of medical treatment. Because the patient's claim was not subject to a medical panel's review, the trial court had erred in granting the hospital's motion for judgment on the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision that had granted the hospital's motion for judgment on the evidence in the patient's action against the hospital for negligence. The court remanded with instructions that the jury's verdict that had found the patient 25 percent at fault and the hospital 75 percent at fault be reinstated.

 

1063 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Golden v. State


No. 19A01-8911-PC-474


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


553 N.E.2d 1219; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 571



May 7, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied July 6, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Dubois Circuit Court; The Honorable Hugo C. Songer, Judge; Cause Nos. CR-83-72 and CR-83-73.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Dubois Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief following his convictions for forgery and his sentence as an habitual offender. Defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to find that he was an habitual offender and that the sentencing scheme subjected him to double jeopardy in violation of the Fifth Amendment and Ind. Const. art. I, § 14.


OVERVIEW: Defendant received two checks for his repair services. Each check was for $ 50, but defendant added an extra zero to the sums so they appeared to be for $ 500 apiece. Defendant was found guilty of two counts of forgery and was found to be an habitual offender. Defendant was sentenced to a five year sentence for each conviction, and each conviction was enhanced by 30 years under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8. The trial court accepted a plea agreement and set aside a conviction but did not alter the sentence. Defendant's appeals were denied, and his petition for post-conviction relief was denied. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed but sua sponte reversed the sentence. The evidence was sufficient to find defendant an habitual offender. However, the forgeries stemmed from a single transaction and were intimately related, so the trial court erred in fixing both forgery sentences with additional habitual offender sentences. The sentences were unconstitutional violations of defendant's double jeopardy rights and were prohibited by § 35-50-2-8. It was proper to give defendant concurrent presumptive sentences but only one of those sentences could be enhanced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of post-conviction relief, it remanded the cause for resentencing with instructions to enhance one forgery sentence by 30 years for a total sentence of 35 years, and it instructed the trial court to specify which sentence it enhanced, to vacate the additional habitual offender sentence on the remaining underlying felony conviction, and to give defendant credit for time served.

 

1064 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


McKinney v. State


No. 71A03-8902-CR-45


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


553 N.E.2d 860; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 502



May 3, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the St. Joseph Superior Court, The Honorable Jeanne J. Swartz, Judge, Cause No. 71D05-8803-CF-00134.



DISPOSITION:  We therefore, reverse and remand for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana) for homicide.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with homicide after he admitted to several people that he had killed a man, and the man's body and his truck, which defendant had used, were found.On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court found that the jury should have been instructed on the necessity of establishing territorial jurisdiction, and that the trial court had failed to do so. The court reasoned in part that defendant had preserved the issue for review when he tendered his proposed instruction on territorial jurisdiction, although the tendered instruction did not correctly state the law. The court further reasoned that the prosecution must prove territorial jurisdiction, and the issue must be submitted to the jury unless the trial court had determined no reasonable jury could have failed to find territorial jurisdiction beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found that there was conflicting evidence on the issue because defendant had told different stories about where and who had committed the homicide. The court also found that the conflicting evidence as to where the homicide occurred was not sufficient to grant a motion to dismiss for lack of territorial jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's homicide conviction, and remanded for a new trial.

 

1065 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hammond v. Doody


No. 45A03-8904-CV-144


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


553 N.E.2d 196; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 482



April 26, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Lake Circuit Court, The Honorable Lorenzo Arredondo, Judge, Cause No. C87-2447.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the City of Hammond, sought review of a judgment entered by the Lake Circuit Court (Indiana), which permanently enjoined it from enforcing an ordinance against appellee proprietor. The trial court also denied the City's motion to correct errors in that judgment.


OVERVIEW: The City enacted Hammond, Ind., Ordinance 6045 (Apr. 28, 1987), which prohibited outdoor retail sales in commercially zoned districts. The proprietor challenged the ordinance. His complaint alleged that the ordinance was unconstitutional and that his business was a lawful nonconforming use. The trial court entered a judgment that enjoined the City from enforcing the ordinance against the proprietor and declared that he had a valid nonconforming use. After its post-trial motion, which alleged bias and prejudice, was denied, the City appealed from the trial court's judgment. On appeal, that judgment was affirmed. The City maintained that it did not learn that the trial court's law clerk and the proprietor's attorney had filed suit against it in an unrelated action until after the judgment was rendered. In that regard, Ind. R. Trial P. 59(H)(1) provided that a motion to correct an error that was based upon evidence outside the record had to be supported by affidavits and the City had filed no affidavits. Moreover, the City should have made the law clerk's employment with the trial court part of the record instead of asking the court to take judicial notice of her employment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1066 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. Chatfield


No. 49A04-8812-CV-00416


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


553 N.E.2d 490; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 487



April 24, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, Juvenile Division, Room No. 1, The Honorable James W. Payne, Judge, Cause No. PT81-1602.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the judgment of the Marion Superior Court, Juvenile Division (Indiana), that modified the initial custody determination and awarded appellee father custody of her child.


OVERVIEW: The initial custody determination, which gave the mother custody was decided under the paternity statute, Ind. Code § 31-6-6.1-11. Several years later, the father filed a petition for temporary custody, restraining order and a vacation of wage assignment alleging that the child had been "abandoned" by the mother. The trial court granted the petition, and the father was given temporary custody, although the child was actually staying with the her paternal grandmother. The change separated the child not only from her mother, but also her siblings. Thereafter, the father was awarded permanent custody. On appeal, the court held that the trial court had abused its discretion and reversed the trial court's judgment, finding that the change in custody was not in the child's best interest. There was no evidence of abandonment, and no showing of a substantial and continuing changed circumstances in the mother's home. The father did not show that: (1) the child was abandoned; (2) the mother was unfit; (3) a substantial change in mother's home occurred which was detrimental to the child's welfare; or (4) that the original custody order was unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that granted the father permanent custody and remanded the action to the trial court for entry of an appropriate support order.

 

1067 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Willis


No. 64A03-8905-PC-175


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


552 N.E.2d 512; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 448



April 11, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 12, 1990. Transfer Denied April 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Porter Superior Court, The Honorable John L. Richert, Special Judge, Cause No. 85-PSCr-49.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State and cross-appellant inmate, an attorney, challenged a judgment of the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), which granted the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief on two grounds and denied relief on three grounds, set aside the jury verdict, vacated the inmate's conviction of theft, and ordered a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a petition for post-conviction relief from his theft conviction, which the trial court granted on two of the five grounds raised. The court reversed the granting of relief. A jury instruction given at trial regarding inconsistent statements was not fundamental error. The same argument was made and rejected in another case, which was decisive on the issue even though one word was different between the instruction in the prior case and the instant case. Moreover, post-conviction review of the allegedly improper admission of disciplinary complaints was foreclosed by the doctrine of res judicata because the issue was decided on direct appeal. The court affirmed the denial of relief on the other grounds raised by the inmate. A jury instruction given informing the jury that it was the judge of the law and facts did not deny him basic constitutional rights and due process. The instruction clearly stated that the jury did not have the right to make, repeal, disregard, or ignore the law as it existed. Also, the other jury instructions given provided the jury with all the information necessary on the law applicable to this case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment as to the two grounds on which the trial court granted the petition and ordered the trial court to reinstate the jury verdict, reinstate the judgment of conviction and sentence, and vacate its order granting a new trial. The court otherwise affirmed.

 

1068 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hunt v. State


No. 71A03-8906-CR-267


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


550 N.E.2d 838; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 267



March 8, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied January 14, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the St. Joseph Superior Court, The Honorable Jeanne J. Swartz, Judge, Cause No. 23666.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of murder and class C robbery and imposed enhanced consecutive sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his friend demanded the victims' wallets. After the victims produced their wallets, the friend pushed one victim off a wall and defendant shot and killed the other. Thereafter, defendant was arrested at his girlfriend's residence. At the police station, defendant signed a rights waiver form and a statement allegedly prepared from defendant's own words. Defendant was convicted of murder and class C robbery. The trial court imposed enhanced consecutive sentences. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant's arrest was not illegal because the girlfriend's consent to the officers' entry was sufficient to overcome defendant's Fourth Amendment claim. Further, the statement was properly admitted because defendant had a sufficient understanding of his rights to silence and to the assistance of counsel. Thus, defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied. Moreover, although the irrelevant testimony regarding defendant's willingness to kill might be presumed prejudicial, the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt rebutted any such presumption. Finally, the court could not say that no reasonable person could find the sentence appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision convicting defendant of murder and class C robbery and imposing enhanced consecutive sentences.

 

1069 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Superior Constr. Co. v. Carr


No. 45A04-8908-CV-345


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


550 N.E.2d 805; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 223



February 28, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Lake Superior Court, The Honorable Paul D. Stanko, Judge, Cause No. 45D08-8904-CT-01148-0.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant company sought review after the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) denied its motion for change of venue from Lake County and its alternative motion to limit the trial court's monetary jurisdiction in a personal injury action filed by plaintiff victims.


OVERVIEW: The victims filed a personal injury action in the Lake Superior Court, County Division. They sought damages in excess of $ 10,000. The company filed a motion to change venue from the county, and an alternative motion to limit the trial court's jurisdiction to $ 10,000, or in the alternative, to transfer the cause to the Lake Superior Court, Civil Division, so that it could obtain a change of venue from Lake County under Ind. R. Trial P. 76. The trial court denied the motions. The court affirmed. When the victims filed their complaint in 1989, no Lake County Court existed. The Lake Superior Court, County Division, handled all matters assigned to county courts in other counties, including matters assigned to the plenary docket. Thus, the trial court correctly overruled the motion for change of venue from Lake County because no substantive right to such change existed at the time. Lake Superior Court Act § 16(4) was not a local or special law that violated Ind. Const. art. 4, § 22. As the County Division's jurisdiction was not limited by dollar amount, the County Division had subject matter jurisdiction of cases filed on its plenary docket that sought damages in excess of $ 10,000.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1070 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Collins v. State


No. 84A01-8906-CR-210


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


549 N.E.2d 89; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 92



January 31, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 20, 1990. Transfer Denied July 6, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Vigo Circuit Court, The Honorable Robert H. Brown, Judge, Cause No. C CR 86-65.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Vigo Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of possession of cocaine in the amount of more than three grams.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in an automobile accident. A passerby found defendant and took him to a friend's house, where he called for help. When a deputy arrived, he took defendant to the jail for a breath test, which defendant refused. The jail authorities conducted an inventory search of defendant's jacket, which yielded 26.5 grams of cocaine. Defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine, and he appealed. On appeal the court affirmed. It held that 1) the arrest of defendant was valid under Ind. Code § 9-4-1-134, 2) the search of defendant's jacket was a valid inventory search, 3) there was no discovery misconduct by the state because defendant's admissions to the police, alleged to have been withheld from him, were not in the police report, 4) Miranda warnings were unnecessary because the deputy's questions to defendant were not to obtain a confession, 5) exigent circumstances existed for the deputy's entry into the house because defendant may have been injured in the accident, and 6) the jury could have concluded that defendant "knowingly" possessed the cocaine because he picked up the jacket and twice acknowledged that it was his.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of possession of cocaine in the amount of more than three grams.

Sims v. State


No. 18A02-8908-CR-378


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


549 N.E.2d 53; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 33

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who had been convicted of theft and granted a suspended sentence, sought review of an order of the Delaware County Superior (Indiana), which revoked his probation.


OVERVIEW: While on probation, defendant was convicted for public intoxication. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in revoking his probation because the docket sheet for the public intoxication conviction did not show that he had properly waived his right to counsel. Affirming the trial court, the court held that the trial court could revoke probation based upon defendant's commission of a criminal act whether or not defendant was convicted of the act. Therefore, defendant's guilty plea to public intoxication was grounds for revoking his probation even if the plea was uncounseled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1072 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Clem v. Christole, Inc.


Consolidated Cause No. 53A04-8712-CV-393


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


548 N.E.2d 1180; 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 32



January 17, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Monroe Superior Court III, The Honorable John G. Baker, Judge, Cause No. 53D038609CP0297 and Appeal from the Madison Superior Court Division III, The Honorable Robert L. Barnet, Special Judge, Cause No. 48D03-8805-CP-307.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners, in a consolidated appeal of two lawsuits, challenged the judgments of the Monroe Superior Court III (Indiana) that permitted appellee developers to operate group homes for developmentally disabled persons in the property owners' single family residential subdivisions.


OVERVIEW: In the midst of litigation between the property owners and the developers concerning the operation of group homes for the developmentally disabled in residential subdivisions, the Indiana legislature amended Ind. Code § 16-13-21-14 to permit the group homes. As a result, the trial court granted summary judgment to the developers and the property owners appealed. The court reversed, observing that the state had the inherent police power to enact laws to promote the order, safety, health, morals, and general welfare of society. The court also observed that property rights were not absolute and could be restricted by governmental action that constituted a proper exercise of the state's police power. In this case, however, the court determined that the statute, which invalidated restrictive covenants in the property owners' deeds, did not benefit the general public but, instead, benefited the developers as private parties. Accordingly, the court found that the statute was not a valid exercise of police power, both as to the Fifth Amendment of the U.S. Constitution and Ind. Const. art. I, § 21.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the causes were remanded for further proceedings.

 

1073 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Miller Reeder Co. v. Farmers State Bank


No. 71A03-8905-CV-178


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


545 N.E.2d 593; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 1018



October 30, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 10, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the St. Joseph Circuit Court, The Honorable John W. Montgomery, Judge, Cause No. R-4300.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee mortgagee filed a complaint in the St. Joseph Circuit Court (Indiana) on a promissory note and for foreclosure of a real estate mortgage, naming appellant buyer as defendant. The buyer filed an answer and counterclaim to quiet tile on the basis of its tax sale purchase of the realty and filed a motion for summary judgment. The trial court granted summary judgment to the mortgagee. The buyer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county sold the property to the buyer at a tax sale. Notice of the tax sale was published in a newspaper of general circulation and posted on the courthouse wall. The mortgagee did not receive actual notice of the tax sale. The buyer argued that the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment did not require the county auditor to mail to the mortgagee notice of an impending tax sale when the mortgagee did not make the proper requests on the forms available in the auditor's office pursuant to Ind. Code § 6-1.1-24-4.2 (amended 1986; repealed 1989). The mortgagee responded that the failure to make a reasonable attempt to notify it of the tax sale amounted to an unconstitutional deprivation of property without due process of law. The court held that because the mortgagee's address was readily identifiable, actual notice by mail or personal service was required. Lack of that notice violated the mortgagee's due process rights as a mortgagee. Accordingly, the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the mortgagee was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment rendered by the trial court in favor of the mortgagee.

 

1074 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Chilcutt v. State


No. 25A03-8811-CR-363


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


544 N.E.2d 856; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 974



October 16, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied March 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Fulton County Court, The Honorable John J. Delworth, Jr., Judge, Cause No. 25E01-8707-CF-018.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Fulton County Court (Indiana) that convicted him for operating a vehicle with a .10 percent, or more, blood alcohol level in violation of Ind. Code § 9-11-2-1 (1988).


OVERVIEW: An emergency worker and an officer dispatched to the scene of an accident observed an overturned pickup truck lying in a field and defendant lying beside it. They noticed an odor of alcohol about defendant. He was taken to the hospital after falling down. A blood test revealed a blood alcohol content of .17 percent. Defendant contended that Ind. Code § 9-11-4-15 unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof away from the state, effectively requiring him to prove his innocence. The court held that the state proved each element of the offense through the test results and the testimony of the officer. Defendant had the burden of establishing his defense and none of his constitutional rights were destroyed thereby. Defendant argued that an offense under Ind. Code § 9-11-2-1 could not be committed if the person was operating a vehicle solely on private property. The court held that the state had a strong interest in protecting the health and safety of its citizens from intoxicated drivers, and thus the statute applied. Because there was sufficient probative evidence to support the verdict, the conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for operating a vehicle with a .10 percent, or more, blood alcohol level was affirmed.

 

1075 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Ayers v. Porter County Plan Com.


No. 64A04-8701-CV-22


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


544 N.E.2d 213; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 926



October 5, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Porter Superior Court, The Honorable Raymond D. Kickbush, Judge, Cause No. 86-PSC-2408-K.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a group home and its lessors, challenged the judgment of the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), which granted appellee plan commission's petition for a permanent injunction against the home, which prohibited it from operating in a single-family residential area.


OVERVIEW: The zoning ordinance contained no special exception for group homes, but the trial court required the home to qualify for a general special exception under language requiring such exceptions for dormitories, fraternities, and orphanages. The court reversed, because defendants claimed that the home was created under Ind. Code §§ 16-13-21-1 to -18, and as such, was a permitted use in a single-family residential area. The court held that the home was not required to administratively appeal the plan commission's order that it apply for a special exception, because its use of the property was a permitted use. The court held that Ind. Code §§ 16-13-21-1 to -18 did not prohibit a local planning authority from requiring a group home to obtain a special exception, within limits imposed by statute. However, the court noted that zoning laws which limited the use of real property were to be strictly construed. Because the home's use of the property was a permitted residential use and met the zoning ordinance's definition of single-family dwelling, and because the ordinance did not require a special exception for group homes, the plan commission had improperly imposed the requirement.


OUTCOME: Because the record did not establish whether the group home was in fact a residential facility for the developmentally disabled as defined and regulated by the statute, the court remanded to the trial court with instructions to grant a hearing on that issue.

Beck v. State


No. 48A02-8811-JV-00447


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


544 N.E.2d 204; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 925



October 4, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Madison County Superior Court, Division II, The Honorable Jack L. Brinkman, Judge, Cause No. JD-987-87-4.



DISPOSITION: We reverse and remand for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent minor sought review of a judgment of the Madison County Superior Court (Indiana), which adjudged the minor to be a delinquent child and remanded him to the custody of the Indiana Boys School.


OVERVIEW: The minor was charged with molesting a child. The trial court conducted a hearing to determine whether a videotaped statement given by the child contained sufficient indicia of reliability to be introduced as evidence and also to consider whether the child was available to testify. The trial court determined that the child was unavailable and, over the minor's objection, that the tape was admissible. The minor was thereafter adjudged to be a delinquent child. The minor appealed, claiming that the admission of the videotape violated his Sixth Amendment right to confront and cross-examine the child. The court reversed, holding that the trial court violated the minor's Sixth Amendment rights by failing to give his attorney an opportunity to cross-examine the child about the substance of her videotaped statement. The trial court's error was not harmless because the videotaped statement constituted the only direct evidence linking the minor to the molestation. The trial court abused its discretion in admitting the videotape because there was insufficient corroborative evidence of the act to satisfy the admissibility requirements of Ind. Code § 35-37-4-6(d).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision adjudging the minor to be a delinquent child, and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

1077 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Casada v. State


No. 47A01-8903-CR-96


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


544 N.E.2d 189; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 919



September 28, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied March 5, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Lawrence Circuit Court. The Honorable Linda L. Chezem, Judge, Cause No. 47C01-8710-CF-076.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Lawrence Circuit Court (Indiana) for attempted child molesting.


OVERVIEW: Before his arrest, after defendant agreed to allow his polygraph test results to be admissible in court, he waived his right to counsel. During his trial, the victim, who was more than 10 years old, was unable to testify until a chalkboard was placed between her and defendant. The board was removed during cross-examination. The court held that the placement of the board violated defendant's Confrontation Clause rights because he was entitled to face-to-face confrontation in the absence of overwhelming circumstances. The board was not justified by the victim's mere inability to testify because there was no evidence, such as psychiatric reports or the victim's trauma, or particularized findings to support the placement of the board. The error was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because the other evidence against defendant was purely circumstantial and the victim's testimony was the key to the prosecution. The admission of the polygraph test was proper because defendant was not entitled to an attorney when he signed the stipulation to allow the polygraph to be admitted because it was not a critical stage of the proceedings. Also, defendant waived his rights to counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction.

Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District

OVERVIEW: The mortgagee sold property to the mortgagors. The mortgagors were provided notice of a tax delinquency at their last known address. The mortgagees received no such notice of the sale. The court noted that the mortgagee's address was reasonably available and, therefore, the mortgagee should have been given notice of the tax sale.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Adams v. State


No. 71A03-8903-CR-84


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


542 N.E.2d 1362; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 833



August 29, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the St. Joseph Superior Court, The Honorable Sanford M. Brook, Judge, Cause No. 71D02-8805-CF-220.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of automobile theft under Ind. Code § 35-43-4-2.5(b) (supp. 1988) and resisting law enforcement under Ind. Code § 35-44-3-3 (supp. 1988).


OVERVIEW: Working on an anonymous tip that defendant was driving a stolen vehicle, police attempted to stop defendant, and a chase ensued. Defendant's was ultimately arrested and convicted for automobile theft and resisting law enforcement. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and found that: (1) though police did not have probable cause to arrest defendant when they attempted to stop him, they did have sufficient cause to perform an investigatory stop based on the anonymous tip and the verification of information supplied by the informant; (2) evidence that defendant drove at 80 miles an hour, crossed the centerline, and ran stop signs during the chase was sufficient to support the trial court's determination that defendant's driving constituted a substantial risk of bodily injury; (3) though the trial court erred in barring defendant from offering impeachment evidence of a prosecution witness's conviction for attempted rape the error was harmless; and (4) where there was direct evidence of defendant's culpability, the trial court did not err in refusing to charge the jury that cases based on circumstantial evidence had to rule out every reasonable hypothesis except guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for automobile theft and resisting law enforcement.

Bailey v. Menzie


No. 20A03-8806-CV-195


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


542 N.E.2d 1015; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 815



August 24, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Elkhart Circuit Court, The Honorable Gene R. Duffin, Judge, Cause No. 20C01-8708-DR-285.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions to set Bailey's petition for a hearing on the merits.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandmother sought review of the judgment from the Elkhart Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed her petition for visitation rights with her granddaughter, the child of her deceased daughter, pursuant to the Grandparent's Visitation Act (Act), Ind. Code § 31-1-11.7-1 et seq. Appellees, natural father and adoptive mother, contested the petition. The adoptive mother was the child's stepmother.


OVERVIEW: The grandmother was initially granted visitation rights. The father and the adoptive mother successfully sought to have the grandmother's visitation rights terminated. In that proceeding, a trial court found that the grandmother had no rights under the Act. The legislature amended the Act to provide that a grandparent's visitation rights survived the adoption of the child by a stepparent. The grandmother filed a petition for visitation, which the trial court dismissed. On appeal, the court reversed and instructed the trial court to set the petition for a hearing on the merits. The court concluded that the Act's amendment could be applied to the grandmother. The court determined that the grandmother's petition did not seek a revival of her initial visitation rights, but rather a hearing on her rights under the Act. The court found that such a hearing would not deprive appellees of their prior judgment against the grandmother. The court noted that the Act interfered with a parent's liberty interests only to observe its duty under the parens patriae doctrine and only upon a finding that it would be in the best interest of the child.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed the grandmother's petition and instructed the trial court to set her petition for a hearing on the merits.

Kinder v. Doe


No. 47A04-8802-CV-00054


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


540 N.E.2d 111; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 503



June 28, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Lawrence Circuit Court, The Honorable Linda L. Chezem, Judge, Cause No. 47C01-8706-CP-00476.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of an order from the Lawrence Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied the parents' motion to compel a county welfare department to produce a letter from appellee unknown authors that precipitated an investigation of possible child abuse.


OVERVIEW: The parents filed an action against the unknown authors for allegedly making false statements in a letter that caused the county welfare department to investigate the parents for possible child abuse. The trial court denied the parents' motion to compel the county welfare department to produce the original letter that precipitated the investigation. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's order and remanded the case with instructions to hold an evidentiary hearing. The court determined that the records in question were necessary to resolve the issue of whether the unknown authors were not immune from civil liability because the report was made maliciously or in bad faith. The court concluded that the trial court properly interpreted Ind. Code §§ 31-6-11-7, 31-6-11-18 to require the parents to present evidence to rebut the presumption that the unknown authors acted in good faith. The court found, however, that nothing in the record indicated that the parents were not informed of the need to present evidence to rebut the presumption of good faith before the denial of their motion and that they were entitled to an opportunity to present such evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied the motion to compel the county welfare department to produce the letter that precipitated the investigation of possible child abuse. The court remanded the case with instructions for the trial court to hold an evidentiary hearing to determine if the parents were able to rebut the presumption that the unknown authors acted in good faith.
