Brady v. State


No. 71A03-8809-CR-266


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


540 N.E.2d 59; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 475



June 21, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Granted June 28, 1991, Reported at: 1991 Ind. LEXIS 128.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the St. Joseph Superior Court, The Honorable Jerome Frese, Judge, Cause No. 25820.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana), which, upon the jury's verdict, entered a conviction of felony child molesting, Ind. Code § 35-42-4-3(b), and sentenced him to seven years in prison with a fine of $ 1,000, Ind. Code § 35-50-2-6.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of molesting his three-year-old daughter. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding, inter alia, that: 1) Ind. Code § 35-50-2-6, which authorized and outlined the procedures used to videotape a child witness' testimony did not violated defendant's right to confront his accusers under U.S. Const. amend. VI because, unlike an Iowa statute that was found to be unconstitutional, the Indiana statute did not create a presumption of trauma to the child victims but required that the need for the extraordinary measure of videotaping child witness testimony be determined on a case-by-case basis, § 35-37-4-8(d)(1)(C); 2) the trial court properly denied a motion for mistrial because its admonishment was sufficient to overcome any potential prejudice stemming from the State's opening remarks; 3) the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction, notwithstanding inconsistencies in the child's testimony as to who caused her injuries; and 4) in light of the offense and the relationship of the defendant to his daughter, the sentence imposed, although enhanced, was within the statutory sentencing range and not manifestly unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of child molesting and sentence of seven years entered against defendant.

 

1084 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Woods v. Thompson


No. 49A02-8804-CV-143


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


539 N.E.2d 976; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 480



June 19, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Madison Circuit Court, The Honorable Robert C. Barnet, Judge, Cause No. 48A01-8702-CV-65.



DISPOSITION: This cause is reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer appealed the judgment from the Madison Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed his amended complaint against defendants, a sheriff, individually and as the county sheriff, and the county Board of Commissioners. The complaint sought reinstatement, back pay, and damages.


OVERVIEW: The County Sheriff's Merit Board held a hearing on two charges filed against the police officer. The Merit Board found him guilty of one charge but issued no penalties. The sheriff dismissed the officer based upon the Merit Board's findings. The officer then filed a complaint against defendants, claiming that his termination was wrongful because it did not comply with Ind. Code § 36-8-10-11 in that it was not preceded by a decision of the Merit Board that cause for termination existed. The trial court dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court found that in order to provide the constitutionally required judicial review of the cause and discipline determinations within § 36-8-10-11, the Merit Board's "decision" had to include a determination that cause existed for the particular disciplinary action. Therefore, the court held that before an officer could be dismissed, demoted or suspended the Merit Board had to determine the factual basis of the charge and the discipline for which that conduct constituted cause. Because failure to comply with that statutory procedure would render the officer's dismissal unlawful, the court found that he had stated a claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

1085 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


National City Bank v. Oldham


No. 82A01-8811-CV-361


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


537 N.E.2d 1193; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 307



May 9, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied February 8, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Vanderburgh Superior Court, The Honorable J. Douglas Knight, Judge, Cause No. 83-CV-2185.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank challenged the decision of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) denying its motion for proceedings supplemental which it filed seeking to satisfy its judgment against appellee heir from the heir's interest in the assets of appellee estate.


OVERVIEW: The bank had an unpaid judgment lien against the heir. After the heir's father died, the bank filed a motion for proceedings supplemental against the father's estate as garnishee. The trial court denied the bank's motion, finding that the heir had disclaimed his interest in the estate under Ind. Code § 32-3-2-3, precluding the bank from executing upon the estate assets. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision, ruling that the heir's disclaimer related back to a time before the decedent's death and his interest devolved as if he had predeceased his father. The court found that the lien did not attach to the heir's interest when it passed to him by operation of law at his father's death because the disclaimer's effect was that no interest was created in the heir to which a lien could have attached. The court ruled that the heir was not barred from disclaiming his interest because Ind. Code § 32-3-2-10 did not apply where the judgment lien arose before the heir had any interest in the estate. The court concluded that executing an affidavit for transfer of real estate did not constitute acceptance of the interest that barred him from disclaiming it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding that the heir's disclaimer of his interest in the estate precluded the bank from reaching the assets of the estate to satisfy its judgment against the heir.

 

1086 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Schilling v. Lafayette School Corp., Bd. of Trustees


No. 79A02-8710-CV-00420


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


537 N.E.2d 69; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 279



April 27, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Tippecanoe Circuit Court, The Honorable Ronald E. Melichar, Judge, Cause No. C-182-87.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township trustee challenged an order of the Tippecanoe Circuit Court (Indiana) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee school corporation in the school corporation's action to quiet title to a tract of real estate.


OVERVIEW: A township reorganized its school districts, and a former school corporation was given to the school corporation. The school corporation brought an action to quiet title to real estate owned by the former school corporation, and the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the school corporation. The township trustee sought review, and the court affirmed. The court held that it was the legislature's intent that real property pass under the reorganization plan when Ind. Code Ann. § 20-4-5-8 (Repl. 1985) was enacted. Also, because the title passed as a matter of law under § 20-4-5-8, no approval by the fiscal body was necessary and the township board was not required to be joined. Finally, the trial court did not commit error by granting summary judgment while the township trustee's discovery motion was pending because the motion was not likely to lead to the development of a genuine issue of material fact.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the school corporation in their quiet title action.

 

1087 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Buckley v. Standard Inv. Co.


No. 41A01-8809-CV-282


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


536 N.E.2d 311; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 249



April 10, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Granted November 22, 1991, Reported at 1991 Ind. LEXIS 225.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal form the Johnson Circuit Court, The Honorable Jeffrey C. Eggers, Judge, Cause No. 36,490.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant customer sought review of a decision by the Johnson Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee gas company on the customer's suit to recover for personal injuries and property damages she sustained in a gas explosion and fire that destroyed her apartment.


OVERVIEW: Three successive small fires ignited in the customer's kitchen within hours, and a gas inspector checked the lines downstream from her meter, but detected no leaks and restored the gas service. Two days later, a fourth fire totally destroyed the apartment, and a cracked gas line was found. The customer filed suit, claiming negligent inspection of her gas lines, but the gas company obtained summary judgment under the Indiana Tort Claims Act based on the immunity provided by Ind. Code § 34-4-16.5-3(11). On review, the court found that the gas company qualified as a political subdivision under Ind. Code § 34-4-16.5-2(5)(iii) or (x), that it satisfied all other prerequisites to immunity under Ind. Code § 34-4-16.5-3(11), and that state and federal regulations governing the handling of gas did not change the result, either because the gas lines inspected were located downstream of the consumer's meter or because the regulations on which she relied were otherwise inapplicable to the facts. The court found distinctions between governmental and proprietary activities of no consequence because the common law immunity to which such distinctions were applied had been abrogated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

James v. State


No. 62A01-8811-CR-368


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


534 N.E.2d 1113; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 153



February 27, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal form the Perry Circuit Court, The Honorable David Evrard, Judge, Cause No. 86-CR-22.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Perry Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for permission to file a belated motion to correct error after he was convicted in absentia of battery, disorderly conduct, and two counts of resisting law enforcement and was sentenced in absentia to consecutive sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried by a jury and convicted in absentia of battery, disorderly conduct and two counts of resisting law enforcement. He was sentenced in absentia and received consecutive sentences on all counts. Defendant was later apprehended and filed a petition for post-conviction relief and an untimely motion to correct error. The trial court denied the motion, and defendant appealed. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. Defendant did not include the portion of the record dealing with his absence from trial in the transcript and he did not argue the sufficiency of the evidence offered at trial on voluntariness. Because both the allegations of the petition and a factual basis were lacking, the court affirmed the post-conviction court's determination that no error occurred in sentencing. Neither the court nor the trial court was shown by a preponderance of the evidence that defendant's absence was anything but knowing and voluntary. Defendant did not meet the procedural requirements for maintaining an appeal. He did not demonstrate that the failure to comply with the procedural prerequisites was not a consequence of his own volitional acts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court denying defendant's untimely motion to correct error after his conviction and sentencing in absentia.

 

1089 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Cloyd


No. 83A01-8808-CV-264


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


534 N.E.2d 257; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 109



February 21, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Vermillion Circuit Court, The Honorable Don R. Darnell, Judge, Cause No. 83C01-8803-CP-0035.



DISPOSITION: JUDGEMENT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant dentist sought review of a decision of the Vermillion Circuit Court (Indiana), which found for plaintiff patient on the dentist's motion for summary judgment in an action that alleged malpractice.


OVERVIEW: The dentist last saw the patient on February 10, 1977. The patient was displeased with the appearance of her teeth and began consulting another dentist. On July 23 or 24, 1986 the patient consulted an orthodontist, who advised her that he would not be able to put braces on her teeth until she had work done to her gums above two teeth. The patient alleged that it was at this time that she learned that a post placed by the dentist had apparently created other dental problems. The patient's relationship with the dentist ended either on February 10, 1977 or March 7, 1977. The patient filed her complaint on August 13, 1987. In reversing the decision, the court found that the patient's complaint was untimely under the applicable two-year statute of limitations found in Ind. Code § 16-9.5-3-1. The patient's assertion that she continued to rely upon the root canal work performed by the dentist was insufficient to create a genuine factual issue. As a matter of law, the dentist's duty to disclose and the patient's reliance upon him ended with the termination of their dentist-patient relationship. Actual discovery did not trigger the commencement of the limitation period.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

Leuteritz v. State


No. 32A04-8810-CR-356


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


534 N.E.2d 265; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 107



February 21, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Hendricks Superior Court # 2, The Honorable Larry R. Hesson, Judge, Cause No. 32D02-8803-CM-266.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions to enter a judgment of not guilty.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Hendricks Superior Court, Division 2 (Indiana), which convicted him of harassment based one phone call to his former employer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his employer had a dispute over money allegedly owned for labor he performed. The complainant, the employer's wife, stated defendant called their home and ask to speak to her husband by referring to him as "Diaper Rash Face Charlie." The complainant also received a number of other calls in which the caller hung up or played weird music, however, the State stipulated there was no evidence defendant many any of those calls. Defendant contended that there was insufficient he intended to harass. The court held under Ind. Code § 35-45-2-2 a person violated the harassment statute if they with intent to harass, annoy, or alarm another person but with no intent of legitimate communication makes a telephone call, whether or not conversation ensues. The court held that intent could not be inferred from the complainant's perception and the standard to be used was that of a reasonable man. The court held that defendant's request to speak to the complainant's husband, although discourteous, was itself a legitimate communication.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment with instructions to enter a judgment of not guilty.

 

1091 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Mareska v. State


No. 75A03-8805-CR-134


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


534 N.E.2d 246; 1989 Ind. App. LEXIS 105



February 20, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied September 26, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Starke Circuit Court, The Honorable Marvin D. McLaughlin, Judge, Cause No. 75C01-8801-CM001.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Starke Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of disorderly conduct, a Class B misdemeanor, Ind. Code § 35-45-1-3 (1982).


OVERVIEW: The charge of disorderly conduct, a misdemeanor, stemmed from defendant's loud, belligerent, and vulgar conduct at a meeting regarding the cancellation of his school bus driving contract. He was initially tried by the Knox city court. After he was found guilty, defendant appealed to the circuit court. After a jury trial de novo, defendant was again found guilty. The court affirmed, holding that the city court had subject-matter jurisdiction over the charges, even though the crime occurred outside of the city limits. In so ruling, the court held that the statute defining the criminal jurisdiction of the city court, Ind. Code § 33-10.1-2-2 (1982), was simply a reiteration of the former statute, which clearly gave the city court county-wide misdemeanor jurisdiction. Section 33-10.1-2-2 did not evince any legislative intent to reduce the city court's territorial jurisdiction. Further, even though the city court violated defendant's Sixth Amendment rights when it tried him before a jury that specifically and systematically excluded jurors from the area where the crime occurred, the error was cured by his trial de novo in the circuit court, which jury was drawn from the entire county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

State v. Pease


No. 82A01-8804-CR-129


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


531 N.E.2d 1207; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 1039



December 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Vanderburgh Superior Court, The Honorable Thomas Lockyear, Judge, Cause No. 87-CR-442.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the judgment of the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence after defendant was charged with possession of a schedule II controlled substance, amphetamines.


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed that the windshield of defendant's vehicle was badly cracked. The officer stopped the vehicle and asked defendant to exit the vehicle. The officer conducted a pat down search on defendant and felt a hard object in defendant's shirt pocket. The officer asked defendant what it was, and defendant reached for his pocket, turned, and ran. Defendant threw the object, and the officer recovered it and reported that it was amphetamines. Defendant was charged with possession of a controlled substance. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the evidence. The trial court granted the motion. The state appealed. The court affirmed, finding that the officer's pat down search of defendant was illegal. Although the court held that the officer acted reasonably in stopping defendant to investigate whether the vehicle was being operating in an unsafe condition under Ind. Code § 9-8-6-2 due to the cracked windshield, the frisk that followed was impermissible because the officer did not hold a reasonable belief that defendant was armed and dangerous. The court also held that the search was not a search incident to arrest because the officer did not subject defendant to arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of defendant's motion to suppress evidence.

Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


530 N.E.2d 750; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 925

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant under the Indiana Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act, Ind. Code § 35-45-6-2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violation of the Indiana Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act, Ind. Code, § 35-45-6-2, predicated upon Ind. Code § 35-49-3-3. The trial court permitted the prosecution to amend the indictment and convicted defendant under Ind. Code § 35-45-6-2(a)(3). On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment against defendant. The court concluded that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to dismiss the amended indictment on the grounds that it was not resubmitted to the grand jury. The court determined that Ind. Code § 35-34-1-5(a) did not require the amended indictment to be resubmitted to the grand jury after the amendment for an immaterial defect. The court also concluded that the trial court correctly applied Ind. Code § 35-49-3-3(3) regarding the appropriate method of determining the distance between the two points.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant under the Indiana Racketeer Influenced & Corrupt Organizations Act.

 

1094 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Frank v. Trustees of Orange County Hospital


No. 88A01-8805-CV-149


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


530 N.E.2d 135; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 921



November 14, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Washington Superior Court, The Honorable William Thompson, Judge, Cause No. 59C01-CP-283.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff physician filed suit for breach of contract against defendants, the trustees of a hospital. He appealed from the order of the Washington Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his motion to compel certain deponents to disclose what transpired at the various meetings of administrators and medical staff held pursuant to the peer review process or any statements concerning the physician made during private, informal conversations.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the trial court's order. It held that the information was not relevant to the issues raised by the pleadings. The physician argued that the information would establish that the medical staff's decision to terminate him was based on nonprofessional grounds thereby defeating the defense of justification. However, the complaint sought damages for breach of contract and the hospital did not raise the issue of justification in its answer. Also, even if the information was relevant, it was privileged under the state's peer review statute, Ind. Code §§ 34-4-12.6-1 to -5. This statute prohibited the disclosure of any content of communications to or the determination of a peer review committee. It was irrelevant that some of the discovery requests sought disclosure of statements made during private conversations. Those statements might have shaped the opinions of the participating physicians. Further, there was no requirement that the communications be offered in good faith or be related to professional qualifications in order to qualify for the peer review privilege. The privilege did not deprive the physician of his due process right to judicial review of state action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying the physician's motion to compel discovery.

Terpstra v. State


No. 25A04-8802-IF-68


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


529 N.E.2d 839; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 793



October 20, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 15, 1988; Transfer denied March 31, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Fulton County Court, The Honorable John J. Delworth, Jr., Judge, Cause Nos. 1759, 1760, 1761 & 1762.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged a decision of the Fulton County Court (Indiana), which, upon charges filed by appellee state, convicted him of violating Ind. Code § 9-1-4-5 for failure to display a certificate of registration, § 9-1-4-7 for failure to display a registration plate, § 9-1-4-20 for display of a false or fictitious registration plate, and § 9-1-4-40 for failure to have a driver's license in possession.


OVERVIEW: A police officer pulled the driver over and asked him to produce a valid driver's license and vehicle registration. The driver could not produce either item and was cited for driving without a driver's license and a vehicle registration. The driver was then formally charged with four different infractions and, following a bench trial, was found guilty of all four charges. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: (1) although the driver should have been served with a complaint and summons, the fact that the charges were brought by an information and criminal summons did not constitute reversible error, because the driver was aware of the charges against him and did not show that he was misled, in any manner, in the preparation of his defense; (2) the driver's failure to comply with Ind. R. Trial P. 38(B) waived his right to a trial by jury; (3) the driver's religious beliefs did not constitute a legal defense to the charges; and (4) the collective benefit to the general public of traffic safety laws outweighed any infringement on the driver's free exercise of the right to travel and the right to freedom of religion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which found the driver guilty of (1) failure to display a certificate of registration, (2) failure to display a registration plate, (3) display of a false or fictitious registration plate, and (4) failure to have a driver's license in possession.

 

1096 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Lilley v. Carmel


No. 06A01-8802-CV-45


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


527 N.E.2d 224; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 611



August 29, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Boone Circuit Court, The Honorable Ronald E. Drury, Judge, Cause No. C85-303.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former fireman challenged a decision from the Boone Circuit Court (Indiana), which affirmed his dismissal from appellee fire department by the Board of Public Works and Safety. The fireman challenged his dismissal for violation of Ind. Code § 36-8-3-4.


OVERVIEW: The department discharged the fireman for engaging in conduct unbecoming an officer. He was intoxicated one evening when he appeared at the station while he was off duty. On the second occasion, he committed theft of gasoline from one of the emergency vehicles and of meat stored in the department's freezer. The court found that the department relied on off duty firefighters often and that the chief had warned the fireman that he did not want the fireman at the station when he was off duty and had been drinking. The Board was not required to find that the fireman had been drinking to the extent that he was unfit for duty. The court found it necessary to address the issue of theft because the evidence of the fireman's intoxication was sufficient to support the Board's decision to dismiss the fireman. Other issues raised by the fireman were not preserved for review and as such, he could not complain of error as to those issues. Finally, because the department relied on off-duty officers and because the fireman held a position of authority, the requirement that he not engage in conduct that might impair his ability to respond in an emergency was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner wife sought review of the judgment of the Shelby Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted a temporary injunction in favor of respondent husband that enjoined the wife from obtaining an abortion.


OVERVIEW: The wife, age 19, was married to the husband, but there was a pending petition for dissolution of marriage filed by the wife. The wife was pregnant and was preparing to have an abortion. The husband filed a petition for injunction in the dissolution proceedings that sought to prevent the wife from obtaining the abortion. Van Sant v. State


No. 11A01-8711-CR-281


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


523 N.E.2d 229; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 388

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Clay Superior Court The Honorable John P. Stelle, Judge Cause No. SCR-86-480.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Clay County Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted her of distribution or exhibition of obscene matter in violation of Ind. Code § 35-49-3-1.


OVERVIEW: Two police officers purchased pornographic magazines at an adult bookstore. Defendant, who was employed at the adult bookstore as a cashier, picked up the magazines to determine the price, rang up the sale, and placed the magazines in a paper bag. Defendant was charged by information with two counts of offer, distribution, and exhibition of obscene material. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the Indiana Obscenity Statute, Ind. The trial court properly excluded defendant's evidence relating to the availability of comparable sexually explicit materials in the county. Additionally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by refusing to send exhibits and instructions to the jury room. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for distribution or exhibition of obscene matter.

K-Mart Corp. v. Novak


No. 93A02-8708-EX-330


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


521 N.E.2d 1346; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 336



April 27, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 8, 1988; Transfer denied December 7, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Industrial Board of Indiana Cause No. 99846.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded with instructions to order payment over five hundred (500) weeks and to increase the award by five percent (5%).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged a decision of the Industrial Board of Indiana that awarded workmen's compensation death benefits to appellee surviving widower of an employee after a maniacal gunman shot and killed an employee while she was at work.


OVERVIEW: Appellee's wife was a cashier at appellant's store when she was killed by a maniacal gunman who had gone on a shooting spree and entered the store where she worked. Appellee was awarded workmen's compensation death benefits as a surviving widower and appellant challenged that award. Appellant contended that the risk to decedent was not increased above that of the general public and therefore the award was improper. The court held that the "positional risk" test applied to a cashier and likened her situation to a traveler who might have been assaulted while traveling for work to find that the decedent had been killed in the course and scope of employment. The court therefore affirmed the board's award of survivor's workmen's compensation benefits to appellee. The court also held that appellee was entitled to an increase of the award of five percent due to its affirmation on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Industrial Board decision that awarded survivor's death benefits to the widower of an employee shot and killed while at work.

Rodgers v. Martinsville School Corp.


No. 06A01-8710-CV-261


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


521 N.E.2d 1322; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 335



April 25, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied December 2, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Boone Superior Court The Honorable Ora Kincaid, III, Judge Cause No. S-86-287.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an order of the Boone Superior Court (Indiana), which granted two motions for summary judgment in favor of defendant school in plaintiff's action against the school to recover damages for injuries sustained as a result of the school's alleged negligence in failing to supervise its male students.


OVERVIEW: When plaintiff was changing clothes in the girls' locker room in the school, a male student, while committing an act of voyeurism, fell through a false ceiling landing on the plaintiff, injuring her shoulder. Plaintiff was 13 years old at the time. Seven years later, plaintiff filed a complaint for damages against the school. The school set forth as an affirmative defense plaintiff's failure to comply with the notice requirements of the Indiana Tort Claims Act. The trial court granted summary judgment for the school. Prior to the summary judgment hearing, plaintiff had filed a second cause of action against the school, alleging the same facts, but also alleging that notice had been timely filed. The trial court granted summary judgment for the school in the second action. Plaintiff's appeals were consolidated. The court held that plaintiff was barred from maintaining her claim because she failed to file timely notice with the school. The school was not estopped from asserting non-compliance with the notice provisions, even though it had actual notice that the incident occurred. Plaintiff was barred by res judicata from relitigating the same claim in her second cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment for the school.

Mishler v. County of Elkhart


No. 50A03-8706-CV-164


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


521 N.E.2d 693; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 298



April 11, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 16, 1988. Reported at 521 N.E.2d 693 at 698.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marshall County Circuit Court, The Honorable Michael D. Cook, Judge, Cause No. CTC 84-201.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Marshall Circuit Court (Indiana) entered summary judgment denying appellant landowners a collateral attack on a judgment ordering appellee Elkhart Board of County Commissioners to rezone appellee property owner's land. The landowners appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: The owner had property that was zoned for residential purposes. The landowners owned property contiguous to the owner's property. The owner applied to the Commissioners for rezoning for commercial purposes. The Elkhart County Plan Commission recommended rezoning but the Commissioners rejected the owner's application. The owner filed a complaint for declaratory judgment, alleging an unconstitutional taking of his property by the Commissioners. A lower court directed the Commissioners to grant the rezoning. The landowners filed a complaint for declaratory judgment and injunction seeking to set aside the lower court's judgment. The trial court entered summary judgment against the landowners. On appeal, the court found that the lower court had jurisdiction to review the constitutionality of the Commissioners' decision. However, the court also found that the lower court exceeded its authority by ordering the Commissioners to rezone the owner's property. Therefore, the court determined that the lower court's judgment was void for lack of jurisdiction to render the particular judgment and could be collaterally attacked. The court concluded that the landowners could amend their complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's order.

 

1102 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Walters v. Rinker


No. 71A03-8706-CV-153


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


520 N.E.2d 468; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 209



March 29, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 1, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the St. Joseph Superior Court, The Honorable Sanford M. Brook, Judge, Cause No. R-7626.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pathologist appealed from the judgment of the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana), which denied the pathologist's motion for preliminary determination of his affirmative defense in a medical malpractice action brought by appellees, patient and his wife.


OVERVIEW: The patient and his wife filed a malpractice complaint alleging that the pathologist who examined the patient's tumor negligently failed to diagnose lymphoma. The trial court denied the pathologist's motion for preliminary determination of his affirmative defense which was based upon the two year statute of limitations, Ind. Code § 16-9.5-3-1(a) (1982 & Supp. 1986), but granted a motion for certification of an interlocutory appeal. The pathologist argued that the doctrines of continuing wrong and fraudulent concealment were not applicable because no physician-patient relationship existed or, if one did exist, it terminated when he diagnosed the tumor. The court reversed, holding that: (1) the trial court erred in denying the pathologist's motion because the physician-patient relationship terminated with the last act of health care the pathologist provided on the patient's behalf and the statute of limitations was not tolled under the doctrine of continuing wrong or fraudulent concealment and (2) the statute of limitations did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 12 because the alleged concealment did not preclude the patient and his wife from bringing suit in a timely fashion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order denying the pathologist's motion for preliminary determination of his affirmative defense and remanded the case with instructions to grant judgment on the motion.

 

1103 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. White


No. 27A02-8704-CV-154


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


520 N.E.2d 475; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 211



March 29, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Grant Circuit Court The Honorable Alan Brubaker, Special Judge Cause No CA-86-2.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Grant Circuit Court (Indiana) entered an order vacating appellant grandparents' adoption of a child on a motion filed by appellees, an aunt and her husband, to vacate a decree of adoption. The grandparents appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: After murdering the child's mother, the father left the child with the grandparents. Thereafter, a New Jersey court entered an order giving the child to the aunt and her husband. The aunt and her husband filed for custody and the grandparents filed for adoption. As a result of the petitions, the New Jersey court declared the child to be a ward of the court. Subsequently, the trial court entered its decree of adoption. Neither the aunt and her husband nor the New Jersey court were aware that a petition for adoption had been pending in Indiana. When the aunt and her husband learned of the adoption, they filed a motion to vacate the adoption. The trial court specifically found that the adoption decree was invalid due to lack of consent from the aunt and her husband and the New Jersey court. On appeal, the court determined that in addition to the father's consent, the consent of the aunt and her husband and the New Jersey court were required. Since the grandparents failed to obtain all of the required consents, the court found the judgment of adoption was voidable. The court concluded that the trial court did not err in setting the adoption aside.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

Bozarth v. State


No. 49A02-8701-CR-00009


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


520 N.E.2d 460; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 180



March 24, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 21, 1988; Transfer Denied August 11, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court Criminal Division Two, The Honorable Webster L. Brewer, Judge, Cause No. CR86-025B.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division Two (Indiana), of rape, a class B felony, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-4-1(a)(3) (1987). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant has sexual intercourse with the victim, a 21-year-old deaf and mentally retarded woman. The State contended that the victim was incapable of consent and that therefore defendant's sexual intercourse with her constituted rape under Ind. Code § 35-42-4-1(a). On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant waived his claim that § 35-42-4-1(a) was unconstitutional where he failed to file a motion to dismiss challenging the constitutionality of the statute. There was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction where the evidence indicated that the victim's understanding of sexual matters was that of a child of six or seven years old and defendant was aware of the victims' mental deficiency. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in striking defense counsel's remarks attacking the State's psychiatric expert where the remarks were not in reference to any fact in evidence and were improper. Defendant's claim that his sentence was excessive did not present a justiciable question where the trial court reduced defendant's sentence from 10 years to six years in prison, the minimum allowed under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-5.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Communications Workers of America, Local 5714 v. Reeb


No. 49A02-8707-CV-270


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


520 N.E.2d 111; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 162; 128 L.R.R.M. 3019; 122 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P56,912



March 15, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Municipal Court, Room No. 8, The Honorable Richard H. Huston, Judge, Cause Nos. M886-1424 and M886-381.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two locals of a communications workers union, sought review of decisions of the Marion Municipal Court (Indiana), which ruled in favor of defendant workers in plaintiffs' actions to collect fines from the workers for crossing picket lines. The trial court granted summary judgment to the worker in the first union's action and entered judgment in favor of the worker in the action of the second union.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought actions against workers to collect fines pursuant to the union's constitution for crossing picket lines after a nationwide strike was commenced against a telephone system. The trial court ruled that the union's strike and fine violated Indiana's Public Utility Anti-Strike Act, Ind. Code § 22-6-2-1 et seq. On appeal of the judgments for the workers, the court reversed both decisions and remanded for a trial on the merits of the first union's claim and ordered judgment in favor of the second union. The court held that the National Labor Relations Act, 29 U.S.C.S. § 151 et seq., pre-empted Ind. Code § 22-6-2-1 et seq. and that the latter Act was void and unconstitutional under the Supremacy Clause, U.S. Const. art. VI, cl. 2. The court ruled that the right to collect fines was an integral part of the union's right to strike and that the formula for imposing fines was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed both decisions and remanded for a trial on the merits of the first union's claim and ordered judgment in favor of the second union.

Werblo v. Board of School Trustees

Frum v. Little Calumet River Basin Dev. Com.


No. 64A03-8611-CV-312


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


518 N.E.2d 809; 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 35



January 28, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied August 29, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Porter Circuit Court, The Honorable Raymond D. Kickbush, Judge, Cause No. 86-PCC51K.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners sought review of a judgment of the Porter Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered in favor of appellee Little Calumet River Basin Development Commission (Indiana), in the taking phase of an eminent domain action brought by the Commission to condemn property owned by the owners. The owners argued that the Commission's taking was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that pursuant to Ind. Code § 14-6-29.5-2(a) (Supp. 1986), the Commission had the power of eminent domain and the power to lease improvements made upon land to private persons. The Commission developed a plan to acquire land to construct a marina. The legislature subsequently passed a bill prohibiting the Commission from taking by eminent domain land owned by steel companies. The Commission selected the owners' property as a site for the marina and commenced taking proceedings. On appeal, the court determined that the Commission had the authority to lease property to private purposes only for purposes in furtherance of § 14-6-29.5-2(a). Thus, the court held, the Commission's limited authority did not convert the use for which the owners' property was taken from a public purpose to an unconstitutional private one. The court also ruled that the Commission's taking was not unconstitutional based on the fact that the steel companies' land was excluded from its taking power. The court concluded that the legislature could have reasonably determined that taking such land was economically impractical thus, there was a rational basis for the distinction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1108 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Robb v. Matthews Buick-Pontiac, Inc.


No. 27A02-8704-CV-172


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


516 N.E.2d 1110; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 3401



December 28, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Grant County Court, The Honorable John P. Porter, Judge, Cause No. CCS-86-822.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car owner appealed an adverse decision in the small claims court action that she filed in the Grant County Court (Indiana) against defendant car dealer for damages to her car that was stored on the dealers lot. She claimed that the trial court erred in denying her demand for a jury trial because of Ind. Code § 33-10.5-7-5(a) (1984 Supp.), and that the judgment was contrary to law, in part because it violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 20.


OVERVIEW: The owner's car was towed to the dealer's lot where it was vandalized, and she filed a small claims action for damages. She also filed a demand for a jury trial, which was rejected, and judgment was entered for the dealer. On appeal she claimed that her right to a jury trial was denied in violation of art. I, § 20. The court affirmed the judgment, ruling that Ind. Code § 33-10.5-7-5(a) (1984 Supp.) did not extinguish her right to a jury trial. She could have filed her claim in a court where her jury trial right would have been preserved. The court rejected her argument that she should have received notice of her right to seek a jury trial elsewhere. Section § 33-10.5-7-5 did not apply to her as plaintiff. The court also ruled that the automatic waiver of a jury trial that was effectuated by filing a small claims action was not unconstitutional because § 33-10.5-7-5(a) altered the right to a jury trial only in small claims courts. With regard to the bailment claim, the court concluded that the dealer had stored the vehicle in a lighted, locked, and fenced area. Accordingly, the evidence supported the trial court's finding that the dealer had exercised the required degree of care.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which ruled for the dealer in the owner's action for damages to her car while it was stored on the dealer's lot.

Meeks v. Shettle


No. 29A02-8609-CV-327


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


514 N.E.2d 1272; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 3203



November 12, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Hamilton Circuit Court, The Honorable Judith Proffitt, Judge, Cause No. C85-073.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer challenged a judgment of the Hamilton Circuit Court (Indiana), affirming the disciplinary action taken against him by appellees, the Indiana State Police Board and the Indiana Police Superintendent. The Board partially sustained a decision of the Superintendent to the extent that it found the officer guilty of one of three charges, demoted him, and suspended him for five days without pay.


OVERVIEW: The officer's state police vehicle collided with a horse-drawn buggy when he attempted to pass a car. The Board only found the officer guilty of causing the negligent destruction of state property and the property of another. The circuit court correctly upheld the Board's decision. The court rejected as meritless the officer's contention that the Superintendent's disciplinary action was contrary to the Administrative Adjudication Act (AAA), Ind. Code Ann. § 4-22-1-1 et seq. (1986). The court determined that the AAA did not apply because the Superintendent conducted an intradepartmental prehearing under the State Police Act, Ind. Code Ann. § 4-22-1-11 (1982), the court ruled that only the Board, as the ultimate authority, was required to conduct a hearing and determination in compliance with the AAA. The court decided that the officer failed to preserve an issue for appellate review, that a delay between his appearance before the Superintendent and the Board's proceedings violated due process, because that issue was not raised in a motion to correct error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

In re Paternity of King


No. 49A02-8704-JV-174


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


514 N.E.2d 325; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 3169



October 26, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, Juvenile Division, 1 The Honorable James Payne, Judge, Cause No. PT-86-120.


1 This case was diverted from the Second District by order of the Chief Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a summary judgment from the Marion Superior Court, Juvenile Division (Indiana), holding that his paternity suit against appellee mother was barred by the paternity statute of limitations in Ind. Code Ann. § 31-6-6.1-6. The father contended that § 31-6-6.1-6 violated the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and Indiana Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The parties' relationship produced a child who moved with the mother to Indiana after their separation. The mother's second husband prohibited the father from visiting the child. The superior court properly disposed of the father's suit. The court determined that a condition in Ind. Code Ann. § 31-6-6.1-6(a)(6) applied and required that the father's action must have been filed within two years after the child was born unless the mother could not have been served with summons during that period. The court found from the evidence that the condition set out in § 31-6-6.1-6(a)(6) did not arise within the child's first two-years of life and continue until two years before the father filed suit. The court decided that, although that condition would have applied in the child's first year, the condition ended as soon as he was moved to Indiana, when the father had to file suit in the next two years. The court concluded that the intermediate level of judicial review did not apply to the different period of limitation for the father under Ind. Code Ann. § 31-6-6.1-6, which did not violate the Equal Protection guarantees of the United States and Indiana Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

Gossett v. Auburn Nat'l Bank


No. 49A04-8612-CV-00379


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


514 N.E.2d 309; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 3127



October 19, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 7, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, Room No. Two, The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Cause No. S284-1409.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and remanded with instruction to vacate the judgment quieting title in Sanda and enter judgment quieting title in Gossett.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant purchaser challenged a judgment from the Marion County Superior Court (Indiana) that was entered for appellees, a mortgagee and its mortgagor. The superior court denied the purchaser relief of quieting title in him. The superior court granted relief to the mortgagee in its action to set aside a tax deed that was issued to the purchaser, divested him of his interest in real estate from a tax sale, and quieted title in the mortgagor.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagor guaranteed a non-party corporation's mortgage for a loan from a non-party savings and loan association. The corporation conveyed title to the real estate to the mortgagor by quitclaim deed. The mortgagee's action named both the purchaser and the mortgagor as co-defendants and they each counterclaimed to quiet title. The court held that the mortgagee lacked standing to contend that Ind. Code § 6-1.1-24-4.2 violated the association's right of due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV to receive notice of a tax sale of the real estate on which it had a mortgage. Although the court lacked jurisdiction of that issue, the mortgagee, in a post-tax sale position, could not demonstrate any direct pecuniary loss resulting from the operation of § 6-1.1-24-4.2. The court decided that the mortgagee lacked any right to notice of the proposed issuance of the tax deed. The superior court improperly quieted title in the mortgagor because the tax sale involved no irregularities and, pursuant to Ind. Code § 6-1.1-25-4(d), the mortgagor's title was divested upon issuance of the tax deed. Therefore, the purchaser owned fee simple absolute title that was not encumbered by the mortgage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the superior court with directions to vacate the judgment quieting title in the mortgagor and to enter judgment quieting title in the purchaser.

Kaminsky v. Medical Licensing Bd.


No. 1-785-A-188


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


511 N.E.2d 492; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2953



August 11, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Petition Denied September 23, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated Appeals from the Shelby Superior Court The Honorable Jonathan E. Palmer, Judge, Cause No. SUPC 81-252. Marion Superior Court, Civil Division, Room 3, The Honorable Betty Barteau, Judge, Cause No. S384-848. Tippecanoe Circuit Court, The Honorable Warren B. Thompson, Judge, Cause No. C-323-84.



DISPOSITION: Tippecanoe Circuit Court's order affirmed. Shelby and Marion Superior Courts' appeals dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, chiropractor and medical licensing board (MLB), challenged the judgment of the Shelby Superior Court (Indiana) upholding the MLB's suspension of the chiropractor's license, of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) upholding appellee chiropractic review board's (IBCE) revocation of the chiropractor's license, and of the Tippecanoe Circuit Court (Indiana) holding in favor of appellee assistant in an unauthorized practice claim.


OVERVIEW: The chiropractor's license was suspended by the MLB and later revoked by the IBCE after the chiropractor used the title "M.D." while he was not licensed to practice medicine, and for exceeding the scope of his license. The assistant was then enjoined from engaging in the practice of medicine. The chiropractor challenged the lower courts' judgments upholding both actions against him and the MLB challenged the vacating of the judgment against the assistant. The court held that: (1) the Shelby Superior Court properly struck the chiropractor's claims under various state and federal laws in his petition for judicial review because review pursuant to the Administrative Adjudication Act was an exclusive remedy; (2) the chiropractor's challenge of his license suspension was moot because the IBCE subsequently relicensed him; (3) The Marion Superior Court was without jurisdiction to hear the chiropractor's appeal because his complaint was not properly verified; and (4) the circuit court properly vacated its injunction against the assistant after Ind. Code § 25-22.5-1-2 was amended to exempt the assistant from the prohibition of the unauthorized practice of medicine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment striking the chiropractor's state and federal law claims in his petition for judicial review, dismissed the chiropractor's appeals of the orders of the MLB and the IBCE, and affirmed the judgment vacating the injunction against the assistant.

Burdine v. State


No. 73A01-8609-CR-249


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


510 N.E.2d 1385; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2906



July 30, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 17, 1987; Transfer Denied August 4, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Shelby County Court, The Honorable Jack A. Tandy, Judge, Cause No. SCCR85-787.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions for operating a motor vehicle while his driving privileges were suspended under Ind. Code § 9-12-2, a violation of Ind. Code § 9-12-3-1 (Supp. 1986), and leaving the scene of an accident involving serious bodily injury, a violation of Ind. Code § 9-4-1-40 (Supp. 1986), from the Shelby County Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions. The court noted that proof of actual knowledge of an injury was not required in a prosecution under Ind. Code § 9-4-1-40 and held that there was substantial evidence from which the jury could have inferred that defendant reasonably should have anticipated serious bodily injury to the occupant of the other vehicle. As to the habitual offender charge under Ind. Code § 9-12-3-1, the court held that the State had to prove that defendant knew or reasonably could have known that his driving privileges had been suspended as a result of his having been determined to be a habitual traffic offender. The court held that evidence was insufficient to permit the inference that when defendant drove on the morning of the accident at issue, while his driving privileges had been suspended under the habitual offender statute, he was aware of a high probability that he was engaging in the conduct prohibited by § 9-12-3-1. Given defendant's acquiescence in the jury's composition, the court concluded that no error occurred as a result of the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for change of venue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for leaving the scene of an accident but reversed his conviction for driving after having been adjudged a habitual traffic offender.

Lincoln v. Board of Comm'rs


No. 79A04-8610-CV-315


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


510 N.E.2d 716; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2890



July 22, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Tippecanoe Circuit Court, The Honorable Ronald E. Melichar, Cause No. C-813-85.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the trial court is reversed and remanded with instructions to reinstate Lincoln's appeal of the Board's decision to discharge her.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee sought review of a decision from the Tippecanoe Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed her appeal of an executive decision of appellee, the Board of Commissioners of Tippecanoe County (Indiana), to discharge her from her employment as a courthouse custodian. The trial court had dismissed the appeal as not timely filed within the 30-day period specified by Ind. Code § 36-2-2-27.


OVERVIEW: On review, the employee contended that the decision terminating her employment was judicial in nature and not ministerial; therefore, she had the right of appeal. The employee also asserted that Ind. R. Trial P. 6(A), (E) should be applied to determine when the statute of limitations began and ended. The court agreed with the employee that the Board's decision was quasi-judicial in nature; the board provided notice to the parties, permitted the parties to be represented by counsel, convened a formal hearing, took evidence, judged the credibility of the witnesses and weighed the evidence, and then made a decision to affirmed the discharge decision. Thus, the employee did have a right to appeal. The court further found that because Ind. Code § 36-2-2-27 did not specify the method of computing the 30-day statute of limitations, Ind. R. Trial P. 6(A), (E) applied and the statute was not therefore unconstitutionally value. Furthermore, the "date the executive decision was made" was the date on which the Board posted notice to the employee. In reversing, the court concluded that under the facts of the case, the appeal was timely filed and that notice by ordinary mail was adequate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision to dismiss the appeal of the decision to discharge appellant and remanded the case with instructions to reinstate the appeal.

Jackson v. State


No. 21A01-8612-PC-337


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


509 N.E.2d 885; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2814



July 2, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 21, 1987; Transfer Denied October 29, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Fayette Circuit Court, The Honorable Daniel L. Pflum, Judge. Cause No. C-83-18.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the decision of the Fayette Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief following his guilty plea to attempted murder.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pleaded guilty to attempted murder and was sentenced to a prison term of 20 years per the plea agreement. In his petition for post-conviction relief, petitioner claimed that the convicting court's failure to advise him that his sentence could be increased based on his prior convictions was error. The trial court disagreed, and the court affirmed. The court held that because the convicting court sentenced petitioner to the least possible sentence for attempted murder, 20 years, pursuant to the written plea agreement, the error was harmless. The court noted that petitioner did not allege that the omission affected his decision to enter a guilty plea. The court held that petitioner waived his objection to the trial court judge hearing the petition because he failed to raise the issue at trial. The court held that petitioner waived his complaint that he was compelled to testify before the trial court, and it held that the trial court's decision to require petitioner to testify under oath at the post-conviction hearing was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1119 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


B.G. v. H.S.


No. 45A03-8608-JV-243


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


509 N.E.2d 214; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2776



June 24, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 10, 1987; Rehearing Denied March 24, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Lake Superior Court, Juvenile Division, City of Gary, Lake County, Indiana. The Honorable Darlene Wanda Mears, Judge, Peter Caras, Referee, Cause No. J84-2972.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment of the Lake Superior Court, Juvenile Division, City of Gary (Indiana) that denied her pre-trial motion to dismiss appellee alleged father's paternity action.


OVERVIEW: In her motion to dismiss the mother asserted that the paternity action was not within the juvenile court's jurisdiction because the child had been adopted. On appeal, the court reversed the juvenile court's denial of the motion. The court held that paternity action should have been dismissed because the adoption was valid. The court considered the state's paternity action and adoption statutes, specifically Ind. Code §§ 31-6-6.1-1, 31-6-6.1-2(a)(2), 31-3-1-8, and held that the state had sufficiently protected the alleged father's opportunity, as an unwed father, to establish a responsible parental relationship with his child. The court held that requiring an unwed father to take an extra step toward establishing a relationship with the child and toward accepting responsibility was not unreasonable. Due process did not require that every possible biological father be given notice of adoption proceedings, but only that the notice scheme not omit many responsible fathers. The court concluded that requiring unwed fathers to initiate a paternity action in order to ensure that they received notice of adoption proceedings was not an onerous burden.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that denied the mother's motion to dismiss.

 

1120 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Payne v. Grant County Court


No. 27A02-8609-CV-317


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


508 N.E.2d 1331; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2750



June 15, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied April 19, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Grant Circuit Court, Cause No. C-83-675, The Honorable Dennis C. Carroll, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fee payers sought review of a judgment of the Grant Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered judgment in favor of appellees, a court and its judge, a county, and an attorney general, in the fee payers' action to recover administrative fees retained by the county court when the fee payers posted cash bail bonds.


OVERVIEW: The fee payers brought an action to recover administrative fees retained by the county court when the fee payers posted cash bail bonds. The fee payers claimed they were denied the opportunity to post full cash bail, and that the charging of an administrative fee pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-33-8-3(2) (1986) was unconstitutional. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellees. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held the orders in no way denied the accused the opportunity to post full cash bail. Somewhat ambiguously, the bail schedule merely suggested two viable alternatives to posting bail, but did not preclude any other statutorily recognized bail options. An administrative fee could be charged when an accused posted a cash bail bond. Further, there was no unlawful taking of property of the fee payers to which they were entitled to compensation. Rather, the fee payers voluntarily parted with 10 percent of the amount deposited in exchange for benefits received from not having to deal with a bail bondsman and thereby forfeiting, in all likelihood, the full 10 percent bail amount. Further, the percentage method to determine the fee had considerable precedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1121 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Speckman v. Indianapolis


No. 49A04-8605-CV-155


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


508 N.E.2d 1336; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2755



June 15, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 30, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, Civil Div., Room 4, The Honorable Richard L. Milan, Judge, Cause No. S483-1208.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana) granted defendant city's motion to dismiss and to strike plaintiff employee's complaint that alleged claims of a discharge in breach of an employment contract, deprivation of a property interest in continued employed, and deprivation of a liberty interest in the employee's name and reputation. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after the employee was hired by the city, he was discharged. The employee sued the city, and they settled the dispute by entering into an agreement that released the city from any further tort liability and provided for the employee's reinstatement. Several months later, the employee was again terminated after he paid a facility rental fee to the city on behalf of his assistant after the assistant wrongfully withheld the payment. The employee sued the city claiming his discharge was in breach of an employment agreement and deprived him of a property interest in continued employment and of a liberty interest in his name and reputation. The trial court granted the city's motion to dismiss and to strike, and the employee appealed. The court reversed and remanded. The employee was not an at-will employee. The settlement agreement entered into between the employee and the city constituted an employment contract, even though no definite term of employment was specified, because the employee's release of tort liability was sufficient independent consideration to convert the agreement into a contract. Therefore, the employee could only be discharged with good cause shown.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting the city's motion to dismiss and to strike the employee's complaint that alleged breach of an employment contract, deprivation of a property interest in continued employment, and deprivation of a liberty interest in the employee's name and reputation was reversed and remanded.

Whitewater Valley Canoe Rental, Inc. v. Board of Franklin County Comm'rs


No. 81A01-8603-CV-66


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


507 N.E.2d 1001; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2676



May 21, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 30, 1987; Transfer Denied December 10, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Union Circuit Court The Honorable Gary K. McCarty, Judge, Cause No. 9670.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant canoe livery sought review of a decision by the Union Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered a default judgment against the livery pursuant to Ind. R. Trial P. 37(B) for its obstreperous conduct relating to compliance with discovery, contending a lesser sanction was warranted. The livery also challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance enacted by appellee county under which the action was initiated.


OVERVIEW: The county brought an action to impose a civil penalty against the livery for violation of its ordinance that regulated the operation of watercraft for hire, lease, or rental. The trial court entered default judgment against the livery pursuant to Rule 37(B) for abusing, resisting, and obstructing discovery in bad faith by either destroying documents material to the case or refusing to produce them. The livery appealed, challenging not only the default judgment but also the constitutionality of the ordinance. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing the sanction for discovery misconduct and that a lesser sanction was not adequate. The court held that the livery failed to overcome the strong presumption in favor of the constitutionality of the ordinance, finding that it did not violate due process because it was not so vague or overbroad that a person of ordinary intelligence would not be aware of the proscribed conduct. The court determined that the ordinance did not violate equal protection principles because there was a rational basis for imposing regulations upon the hiring, leasing, or renting of watercraft.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the default judgment entered against the livery and concluded that the county's ordinance, under which the action was initiated, was constitutional.

DISPOSITION: The jury verdict is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the judgment of the Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana), which found in favor of appellees, a railroad, engineer and brakeman, in her action against them for the wrongful death of her minor child. The trial court denied the mother's motion to correct errors that challenged the trial court's grant of the railroad's motion in limine to exclude two city ordinances.


OVERVIEW: The mother filed an action against the railroad, the engineer, and the brakeman for the death of her daughter who was struck by the train when her shoe was caught on the railroad track. The trial court granted the railroad's motion in limine to exclude evidence of two city ordinances and denied the mother's motion to correct errors. The mother then appealed the jury verdict. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the trial court properly excluded the two city ordinances. The court found that the city speed ordinance was preempted by the Federal Railroad Safety Act of 1970, 45 U.S.C.S. § 434, and by the Federal Railroad Administration regulations in 49 C.F.R. § 213.9. Additionally, the court held that the city crossing safety gate ordinance was invalid as the Indiana legislature had vested exclusive authority pursuant in Ind. Code Ann. §§ 8-6-3-1, 8-6-7.7-2 to the Public Service Commission to declare as dangerous any grade crossing in the state which required installation of crossing safety devices. The court concluded that the mother failed to preserve error on appeal regarding the final jury instruction on the measure of damages for the wrongful death of a child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jury verdict in favor of the railroad, the engineer and the brakeman in the mother's wrongful death action for her minor child.

State v. Sappenfield


No. 34A02-8603-CR-74


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


505 N.E.2d 504; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2529



March 31, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 15, 1987; Transfer Denied August 17, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Howard Superior Court Division I Cause No. 2630 The Honorable Dennis H. Parry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We therefore reverse the judgment and remand for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Indiana sought review of a judgment of the Howard Superior Court, Division I (Indiana), which dismissed two informations charging defendants with violating the Indiana Corrupt Business Influence statute (RICO), Ind. Code § 35-45-6-2.


OVERVIEW: Law enforcement officers purchased several magazines containing graphic photographs of heterosexual and homosexual activity at two stores allegedly owned or operated by defendants. The State thereafter charged defendants with violating Indiana's obscenity statute, Ind. Code § 35-49-1-1 et seq., and alleged a pattern of criminal activity arising out of the distribution of the same obscene matter pursuant to RICO. Defendants moved to dismiss the RICO counts on the ground that RICO was unconstitutionally vague and violative of the 14th Amendment, and the trial court found that RICO could not be constitutionally applied to violations of Indiana's obscenity statute. The court held that the trial court erred in granting defendants' motion to dismiss regarding the counts based on the RICO statute because the Indiana Supreme Court had recently held, in a factually similar case, that: (1) the Indiana RICO statute included obscenity violations as a predicate offense; and (2) the RICO statute, as it pertained to the predicate offense of obscenity, did not violate the First and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

Andrews v. State


No. 1-1185 A 295


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


505 N.E.2d 815; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2554



March 31, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Monroe Superior Court, The Honorable Raymond Kern, Judge, Cause No. MO8411-007.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with recklessly remaining in a voting booth longer than one minute in violation of Ind. Code § 3-1-23-28, and the jury found him guilty. The Monroe Superior Court (Indiana) entered judgment and found defendant in contempt for certain statements made in court and for leaving the courtroom in violation of the judge's order, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went into a voting booth. Later he asked for a write-in ballot and was told that none was available. Defendant refused to leave and was arrested. At his trial, he made statements expressing his opinion that the trial judge was biased. He also left the courtroom in violation of an order to remain. He claimed that § 3-1-23-28 was applied in a discriminatory manner so as to deny him equal protection of the law and that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. He claimed that there was insufficient evidence to support a finding that he acted recklessly and that the findings of contempt were improper. The court held that (1) the fact that defendant was motivated by a desire to protest the unavailability of write-in voting was irrelevant; (2) there was sufficient evidence to support the finding that defendant acted with the requisite intent; (3) enforcement of § 3-1-23-28 did not violate defendant's equal protection rights and the statute was not vague; and (4) the contempt order with respect to the statements was insufficient because it did not contain specific findings, but the contempt order with respect to defendant's leaving the courtroom met the specificity requirement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the finding of contempt with respect to defendant's conduct in leaving the courtroom, but reversed the finding of contempt with respect to defendant's statements.

Adult Group Properties, Ltd. v. Imler


No. 48A02-8604-CV-124


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer sought review of the decision from the Madison Superior Court, Division III (Indiana), which, after a hearing, granted a permanent injunction that enjoined the developer from building a structure for the developmentally disabled in a residential subdivision. Appellee family had brought a suit for an injunction against the developer.


OVERVIEW: The developer argued that the trial court erred by finding a residential subdivision's restrictive covenants could be invoked to prohibit construction of a residential facility for developmentally disabled or mentally ill persons, which was to be operated as a commercial enterprise in violation of the covenants. The court interpreted Ind. Code § 16-13-21-14 as making the restrictive covenants enforceable against the developer and its proposal to operate a business in violation of the subdivision's covenants. The court held that the covenants did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. The court held that the word "family" as used in the restrictive covenants meant "father, mother and children, immediate blood relatives."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which granted a permanent injunction against the developer.

Bailey v. Menzie


No. 92A03-8607-CV-206


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


505 N.E.2d 126; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2498



March 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Whitley Circuit Court, The Honorable Edward J. Meyers, Judge, Cause No. C-86-11.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On a second appeal, petitioner maternal grandmother challenged a judgment from the Whitley Circuit Court (Indiana) in favor of respondents, a natural father and a stepmother. The trial court denied the grandmother's petition for visitation pursuant to Ind. Code § 31-1-11.7(d) of the Indiana Grandparent's Visitation Statute (Act), Ind. Code § 31-1-11 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The father was married to the grandmother's daughter, and one child was born to them. The child's natural mother died, and the father married the stepmother. Shortly after the grandmother was granted visitation rights, the stepmother adopted the child, and a petition for modification and termination of the visitation order was filed. The trial court denied the petition. However, in an initial appeal, the court reversed on the ground that the stepmother's adoption of the child cut off the grandmother's visitation rights under the Act. On appeal, the question for resolution was whether Ind. Code § 31-1-11.7(d) of the Act, which provided that grandparent visitation rights survived the adoption of the child by a stepparent, preserved such rights for the grandparents of children who had been adopted before subsection (d) was added. The court held that: (1) under the original Act, visitation rights did not survive adoption by a stepparent; (2) the legislature's subsequent amendment did not change that interpretation; and (3) since prospective application was sufficient to carry out the purpose of the Act, the grandmother was not entitled to the benefit of retroactive application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court.
