Ridenour v. Furness


No. 06A01-8610-CV-267


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


504 N.E.2d 336; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2427



February 26, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 25, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Boone Circuit Court, The Honorable Ronald E. Drury, Judge, Cause No. C86-361.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Director of the Indiana Department of Natural Resources (DNR) and boat association, brought this interlocutory appeal from an order of the Boone Circuit Court (Indiana) requiring appellees, fishermen and restaurant, to post a bond, and denying the DNR's request to dissolve a preliminary injunction prohibiting DNR enforcement of its emergency order temporarily banning the use of gill net fishing or to grant a stay pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellees claimed they would suffer financially from the ban on gill fishing nets. As the parties seeking the preliminary injunction, appellees were required to show an irreparable injury to a legally recognized right. Because appellees had no legally recognized right to claim as harmed, the court held that the trial court abused its discretion in granting the injunction. The court noted that appellees could not assert any property interest in the fish harvested from the state's waters. Moreover, commercial fishermen's license to fish in the state's waters was a revocable privilege, not a right. The trial court further abused its discretion because appellees failed to establish even a prima facie case that the DNR acted improperly by enacting its emergency order and failed to prove that the order was arbitrary and capricious. The court held that the issue on appeal was not moot where potential liability existed under the bond posted by appellees. The public interest exception to mootness was also triggered because the issue was one of great importance that would likely recur and it would evade review if appellees obtained an injunction before the ban.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that granted a preliminary injunction to the fishermen and restaurant because a review of the trial court's findings and conclusions revealed a clear abuse of discretion.

Hewell v. State


No. 82A04-8609-CR-269


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


507 N.E.2d 241; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2629



February 11, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Vanderburgh Superior Court, The Honorable Terry D. Dietsch, Judge, Cause No. 83-CR-21.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of corrupt business influence. On appeal, the appellate court had found that an unconstitutional seizure of evidence had occurred, evidence which was subsequently admitted. The appellate court ordered a new trial. A new trial was held without the unconstitutionally seized items in evidence. Again, in the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), defendant was convicted of corrupt business influence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant presented four issues for review: (1) whether the trial court properly followed the law of the case; (2) whether defendant's double jeopardy rights were violated; (3) whether the trial court erred in failing to dismiss the prosecution's second amended information; and (4) whether the jury verdict was contrary to law and not sustained by sufficient evidence in view of the charging information. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The law of the case was correctly applied by the trial court on remand. Defendant's first conviction was reversed to rectify trial error, namely the admission of improperly seized evidence. The appellate court did not rule upon the sufficiency of the evidence. Therefore, there was no double jeopardy violation. The second amended complaint was sufficient to inform defendant he was being charged with attempted receipt of stolen property. The prosecution proved the offense of attempted receipt of stolen property. Defendant could be convicted of attempted receipt of stolen property, which was a predicate crime for the racketeering offense. Attempting to receive stolen property was a substantial step towards the commission of theft.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1132 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Beasley


No. 49A04-8609-CV-279


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


504 N.E.2d 1028; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2447



February 10, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, Civil Division, Room Four The Honorable Richard L. Milan, Judge Cause No. S486-318.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed from an order of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed his claim for increased salary benefits.


OVERVIEW: The employee brought suit for back pay, affirmative injunctive relief, and attorney fees, arguing that he was improperly denied a salary increase under the new Career Development Merit Increase Program. The trial court granted defendant police department's motion to dismiss the employee's amended complaint based on the fact that suit was not brought within the statute of limitations. On appeal, the employee contended that his reduced earnings were a continuing wrong and that the statute of limitations should have run from when each paycheck was received. The court disagreed and affirmed the dismissal. Although the state did follow the general rule that where an obligation was payable in installments the statute of limitations ran as to each installment as it became due, there was no continuing wrong in this case. The case involved a one time paid percentage increase to employees. Although the alleged wrong may have had a present impact on the employee's salary, it was not a continuing wrong. Accordingly, the statute of limitations began to run at the time the merit program was placed into effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the employee's claim for increased salary benefits.

State v. Monticello Developers, Inc.


No. 2-985-A-277


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


502 N.E.2d 927; 1987 Ind. App. LEXIS 2292



January 20, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 19, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Delaware Superior Court, Court 3, No. CS3-83/15, The Honorable Betty Shelton Cole, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order from the Delaware Superior Court (Indiana), which granted corporate defendant's motion for judgment on the evidence under Ind. R. Civ. P. 50, claiming that the trial court erred in finding there was a lack of sufficient evidence to support a conviction of criminal recklessness, Ind. Code § 35-42-2-2 (1982).


OVERVIEW: The state filed a charge of neglect of a dependent, Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4(a)(1982), against a corporation which ran a care facility for the developmentally disabled, as well as against the corporate president and two of its employees. After a jury found the corporate defendant not guilty, the trial court granted the corporate defendant's motion for judgment on the evidence under Ind. R. Civ. P. 50, concluding that the evidence was insufficient to support a finding of criminal recklessness. On the state's appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in granted the motion for judgment on the evidence. The court concluded that the state provided more than enough evidence to present a prima facie case of criminal recklessness, which was a lesser included offense of neglect of a dependent under Ind. Code § 35-41-1-16(1), because the offense was "factually included" due to the manner in which the greater offense was committed. The court further held that the trial court properly found that Ind. Code § 35-41-2-3, which provided that a corporate defendant could be held culpable for the actions of its employees when acting with the "scope of authority" was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, concluding that there was a factual basis for the jury's verdict of criminal recklessness, and that the trial court erred in granting the corporate defendant's motion for judgment on the evidence. The court then remanded with directions to the trial court to enter a judgment of guilty and to determine defendant's penalty for the crime of criminal recklessness.

Felix v. Indiana Dep't of State Revenue


No. 41A01-8601-CV-9


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


502 N.E.2d 119; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 3306



December 30, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Johnson Circuit Court, The Honorable Larry J. McKinney, Judge, Cause No. 36,074.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment by the Johnson Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed his suit against appellees, Indiana Department of Revenue, the Indiana Revenue Board, and officials, that challenged a provision of the Indiana Intangible Tax Act of 1933, Ind. Code § 6-5.1-1-1, et seq.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed suit alleging that the Indiana Intangible Tax Act of 1933 violated the constitutions of the United States and Indiana. In the complaint, the taxpayer sought refunds of the tax paid by himself as well as other similarly situated persons who were subjected to the tax. He also sought injunctive relief. The Department filed a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and lack of standing. Thereafter, the taxpayer submitted for the first time a claim for refund with the Department. The trial court dismissed the complaint without prejudice for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. On appeal, the taxpayer argued that the exhaustion requirement was inapplicable because pursuing the refund procedure was futile and the administrative remedy would have been ineffective. The court determined that the taxpayer was still required to go through the refund procedure because exhaustion was still required in constitutional challenges to tax statutes. Additionally, the court decided that requiring the filing of a claim for refund was appropriate because it afforded the Department the opportunity to resolve the matter on nonconstitutional grounds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Albright v. State


No. 4-785 A 181


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


501 N.E.2d 488; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 3274



December 23, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Elkhart Superior Court, No. 2, The Honorable Stephen E. Platt, Judge, Cause Nos. 1776 & 1777.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana), which entered convictions after a jury found defendant, who was the owner of an adult store, guilty of four counts of selling obscene matter for the sale of sexually explicit movies and magazines.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed and held that defendant failed to show that her "expert" had the training, education, or experience in identifying contemporary community standards to establish professional acceptance and reliability of the basis for her opinion on the ultimate issue of the standards in the community. Because the witness was not present as required for an offer of proof, the court held that defendant's offer of proof as to the witness was inadmissible as hearsay. The court found that the prosecution of defendant was prejudicial and met the requirements for establishing the defense of selective prosecution, but that defendant waived the argument by failing to properly assert and establish her argument for selective prosecution. The court held that defendant failed to preserve as error the comments made by the prosecutor in closing arguments because defendant failed to request a mistrial, admonition to the jury or object to the remarks. The court held that the obscenity statute was not defective and did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the rulings of the trial court in favor of the state.

McClanahan v. Remington Freight Lines


No. 2-685-A-184

In re Guardianship of Thompson


No. 4-785 A 207


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


502 N.E.2d 916; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 3356



October 27, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Lake Superior Court, Room two, East Chicago, The Honorable Morton B. Kanz, Judge Presiding, Cause No. EG84-124.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Texas couple sought review of a judgment from the Lake Superior Court, Room two, East Chicago (Indiana), which appointed appellee Indiana couple as Indiana resident guardians, pursuant to Ind. Code § 29-1-18, over the person of the Texas couple's minor child.


OVERVIEW: On review, the Texas couple argued that guardianship proceedings were inappropriate to determine whether out-of-state parents or in-state strangers should have the care and custody of the minor child because Ind. Code § 31-6-2-1 of the state's juvenile code preempted the guardianship statute when the potential effect of the proceedings was to terminate parental rights and authority over the child. The court found that the proceeding was in reality a Child in Need of Services proceeding for which the juvenile court had exclusive jurisdiction under Ind. Code § 31-6-2-1(a)(2), particularly as the Indiana couple alleged that the Texas couple were not fit and proper parents to have care and custody of the minor child. Thus, the state's juvenile code preempted the state's guardianship code under the instant circumstances. The issue of a parent's performance as a parent, including both natural and adoptive parents, was only to be litigated under the juvenile law, which preempted the guardianship provisions and provided the exclusive means to determine parental fitness. The court accordingly reversed the judgment under review and remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment appointing Indiana resident guardians over the person of the minor child, and remanded with instructions to enter an order transferring the case to a juvenile court of appropriate jurisdiction.

 

1138 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. State


No. 1-1285 A 327


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


498 N.E.2d 1008; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 3047



October 23, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 4, 1986; As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Pike Circuit Court, The Honorable Marvin D. Stratton, Judge, Cause No. 84-CR-27.



DISPOSITION: For the above reasons, this cause is affirmed. Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Pike Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted her of two counts of attempted child molestation in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-4-3 and two counts of confinement in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-3-3. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred when it admitted a videotaped statement made by the victim under Ind. Code § 35-37-4-6 (1984). She also asserted that the State failed to prove venue.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of attempted child molestation in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-4-3 and two counts of confinement in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-3-3. The court affirmed her conviction and found that a videotaped statement made by the victim was properly admitted under Ind. Code § 35-37-4-6 (1984). Under § 35-37-4-6, which the court noted was constitutional, statements made by young children who may have been abused could be admitted at trial even where they were not normally admissible if there were sufficient indications of reliability. No set formula existed to gauge reliability in this context, but the child's age, condition, and circumstances were all factors to be considered. Although at the time of the proceeding § 35-37-4-6 did not specifically define videotapes as "statements," the court noted that statements remained such no matter how they were recorded. This videotape constituted substantial evidence of defendant's guilt. Defendant claimed that the State failed to prove venue, but the court found that it had satisfied its burden by a preponderance of the evidence. Circumstantial evidence was correctly used to meet that burden.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Shortridge v. Review Bd. of Indiana Employment Sec. Div.


No. 2-1085 A 330


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


498 N.E.2d 82; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 3010



October 8, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from a Decision of the Review Board of The Indiana Employment Security Division, Case No. 84-R-2558.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged the judgment of the Review Board of the Indiana Employment Security Division (Review Board), which refused to reopen a claim she filed for unemployment benefits when she was pregnant on the grounds that she was not entitled to benefits because she applied for and/or accepted a leave of absence from her employer.


OVERVIEW: Employee applied for unemployment benefits during her pregnancy, and her application was denied by the Review Board on the grounds that she was not eligible because she did not apply for a leave of absence. Thereafter, a federal appellate court held that all pregnant women who were denied unemployment benefits were sexually discriminated against. Employee then filed another claim for benefits on the basis of the federal court judgment. The Review Board again denied the claim because she had applied for and/or accepted a leave of absence from her employer. Employee appealed the ruling by claiming that the Review Board was barred by collateral estoppel from review the facts in its earlier decision. The court held that the doctrines of collateral estoppel and res judicata applied to administrative hearings, including the hearings conducted by the Review Board. The court stated that the Review Board was barred from ignoring its early facts that employee had not applied for a leave of absence, and therefore its second decision denying benefits was reversed. The court remanded for the Review Board to conduct a new hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the Review Board by holding that the Review Board's decision that employee was not entitled to unemployment benefits was erroneous. The cause was remanded for further proceedings.

Sturgill v. State


No. 36A01-8602-CR-25


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


497 N.E.2d 1070; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2973



September 29, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Jackson Circuit Court. The Honorable Robert R. Brown, Judge. Cause No. 85 CR 34.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Jackson Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied defendant's motion to compel production of documents from the county welfare department. Defendant had been charged by appellee state with child molesting and incest involving his stepdaughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the trial court's refusal to allow him to inspect statements made to the county welfare department by the 17 year old alleged victim of child molestation. The welfare department denied the request and the trial court affirmed apparently upon the authority of Ind. Code § 31-6-11-18 that limited access to information gathered by a county welfare department during its investigations of child molestations. The court reversed the judgment because the trial court abused its discretion. In so ruling, the court determined that § 31-6-11-18 was unconstitutional as applied to the facts of defendant's case. The court held that defendant had an interest in discovering the child's statements made to the welfare department because the statements were material evidence that might have contradicted the child's trial testimony and police statements, and could have influenced the trier of fact to render defendant not guilty. Further, the court determined that the state failed to show that it had a paramount interest in non-disclosure where the child's explicit testimony at trial greatly diminished the state's interest in confidentiality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that denied defendant's motion to compel production of documents from the county welfare department in the state's criminal prosecution of defendant for child molestation and incest.

Taylor Drug Stores, Inc. v. Indiana Alcoholic Beverage Com.


No. 41A01-8601-CV-17


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


497 N.E.2d 932; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2961



September 25, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 21, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Johnson Circuit Court, The Honorable Larry J. McKinney, Judge, Cause No. 35,222.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of the decision of the Johnson Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted the summary judgment motion of appellee, Indiana Alcoholic Beverage Commission, in an action challenging the Commission's refusal to issue the applicant a license to sell alcoholic beverages.


OVERVIEW: The applicant, a drug store, filed an application with the Commission seeking a "Type 208 drug store permit" to enable it to sell alcoholic beverages. An excise officer measured the distance from the outside kitchen wall of a neighboring church in a straight line to the nearest point on the back wall of the applicant's store as 185 feet. Ind. Code § 7.1-3-21-11 prohibited the issuance of a liquor permit for premises within 200 feet of a church. Thereafter, the local board and the Commission denied the application. The trial court granted the Commission summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that, under the plain meaning of § 7.1-3-21-11, the excise officer used the appropriate terminal points when measuring the distance between the applicant's store and the church. Further, measurements by local boards did not violate Ind. Const. art. IV, § 23 because § 7.1-3-21-11 was mandatory and applied to all applicants, even if its operation was not uniform in achieving the same result in all respects. Finally, neither § 7.1-3-21-11 nor the proceedings before the local board or Commission delegated a governmental power to a religious institution in violation of the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision granting the Commission's summary judgment motion in the action challenging the Commission's refusal to issue the applicant a license to sell alcoholic beverages.

 

1142 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Palmer


No. 49A04-8605-CR-132


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


496 N.E.2d 1337; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2901



September 3, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Municipal Court, Criminal Div., Room No. 9, The Honorable Charles A. Wiles, Judge, Cause No. A & B 0985-5232.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from the decision of the Marion Municipal Court, Criminal Div. (Indiana), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charges against him for unlawful possession and illegal sale of fireworks. Defendant had been issued a summons to appear at an initial hearing after the charging informations were filed by the prosecutor without a probable cause affidavit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was issued a summons to appear in court on charges of unlawful possession and illegal sale of fireworks. He had not been arrested or detained. On appeal of the dismissal, the court held that the motion to dismiss for a lack of probable cause was not included in the statutory grounds for a dismissal of an information or an indictment. Ind. Code Ann. § 35-34-1-4(a) provided the grounds for which an indictment or an information could be dismissed. The grounds included defective indictments or informations. Ind. Code Ann. § 35-34-1-6(a) described when an indictment or an information was defective. There was no provision in either statute for a dismissal of an information or indictment due to a lack of probable cause. Probable cause was constitutionally required if an arrest was to be made based on an information. The probable cause requirement did not pertain to the filing of the information. Ind. Code Ann. § 35-33-4-1(a) also provided that a trial court could issue a summons in lieu of an arrest warrant if a person was charged in an information or indictment with a misdemeanor. The fireworks violations were misdemeanors, and defendant was served with an appropriate summons.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal and remanded for trial.

Altmeyer v. State


No. 1-1285 A 308


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


496 N.E.2d 1328; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2904



September 2, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing denied February 9, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Pike Circuit Court, The Honorable Marvin D. Stratton, Judge, Cause No. 84CR7.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Pike Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of three counts of child molesting and one count of attempted child molesting. He contended that one of his victim's was available to testify at trial and that her videotaped statement was not admissible under Ind. Code § 35-37-4-6.


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that the victim was unavailable to testify at trial because her participation would have been a traumatic experience for her and that her videotaped statement was admissible in lieu of her testimony. The trial court found that her statements bore sufficient indications of reliability. No transcription of the victim's statement appeared in the record. After the State presented evidence that corroborated the acts of which defendant was charged, including the testimony of two other victims, the jury viewed the videotape. Upon review, the court found that the trial court's determination that the victim was unavailable under § 35-37-4-6 was not error. However, the court found that upon the record, meaningful review of whether the victim's videotaped statement provided sufficient indications of reliability was impossible. The record did not show what guarantees of trustworthiness formed the basis of the trial court's decision to admit the videotape. Thus, the case had to be returned to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the action to the trial court with instructions to enter specific findings of fact and conclusions of law that concerned the reliability of the victim's videotaped statement.

Ashland Oil, Inc. v. Arnett


No. 3-885 A 216


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


496 N.E.2d 1313; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2897



August 28, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 7, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Jasper Circuit Court, Honorable E. Duane Daugherty, Judge, Cause No. C-404-84, Appeal from the Newton Superior Court, Honorable George Vann, Special Judge, Cause No. SPR 84 164. Appeal from the Marshall Circuit Court, Honorable Michael D. Cook, Judge, Cause No. CTC-84-212. Appeal from the Lake Superior Court, Honorable James J. Richards, Judge, Cause No. 584-905.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the attachment plaintiffs, challenged decisions of the Jasper Circuit Court (Indiana), the Newton Superior Court (Indiana), and the Marshall Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered damage awards in favor of appellees, the attachment defendants, for wrongful and oppressive attachment. The attachment defendants challenged a decision of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed a motion for such damages.


OVERVIEW: The attachment plaintiffs first filed an underlying suit against the attachment defendants in federal court. The attachment plaintiffs then filed attachment proceedings in the circuit courts, which entered attachment orders. Those orders were dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. On appeal, the attachment plaintiffs alleged error in the assessing of damages against the attachment bonds because the elements of wrongful attachment were not satisfied, and the attachment plaintiffs had a good faith defense to the proceedings upon the bonds. The court upheld the damage awards and reversed the Marshall Circuit Court's refusal to award damages to all of the attachment defendants covered by the bond. The court held that there was no good faith defense to the proceedings on the bonds. Further, even though the merits were not determined, the attachment defendants still had a right of recovery upon a finding of wrongful and oppressive attachment. Also, the Marshall Circuit Court's ruling that some of the attachment defendants were not entitled to damages because they had no property attached was erroneous; they were entitled to damages for challenging the attachment proceeding.


OUTCOME: The Marshall Circuit Court's order denying a damage award to all of the attachment defendants covered by the attachment bond was reversed. That action was remanded for a determination of damages. The remaining judgments were affirmed.

Conn v. State


No. 4-1083 A 342


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


496 N.E.2d 604; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2852



August 19, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 8, 1986; Transfer Denied January 22, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Franklin Circuit Court, The Honorable Eugene A. Stewart, Judge, Cause No. 9266.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we reverse the judgment and remand this cause for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the Franklin Circuit Court (Indiana) for nine counts of receiving stolen property, which was a Class D felony under Ind. Code § 35-43-4-2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on multiple charges based on evidence obtained from a search performed of his mobile home and storage shed pursuant to a search warrant. Defendant appealed challenging the legitimacy of such search. On appeal, the court reversed the convictions and remanded for a new trial. The court found that the omission of the state and county in the text of the affidavit for search created no discretion in the execution of the warrant and therefore was not fatal to the validity of the warrant. The deviation from the statutory form did not amount to substantial noncompliance with Ind. Code § 35-33-5-3. The court found that the police officers performed an unlawful general search because their warrant specified 9 items and they seized approximately 245 items. Because the discovery of the additional items was anticipated during the search, the plain view doctrine was inapplicable to the case. The plain view doctrine could not have been used to extend a general exploratory search from one object to another until something incriminating emerged. The state also improperly failed to return seized property not shown to be stolen as required by Ind. Code § 35-33-5-5.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of nine counts of receiving stolen property and remanded the cause for a new trial. The court instructed the trial court upon remand to conduct such hearing if necessary to enforce its order as to any property not yet returned to defendant.

Miller v. State


No. 24A01-8602-CR-29


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


496 N.E.2d 592; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2853



August 19, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 19, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Franklin Circuit Court, The Honorable Eugene A. Stewart, Judge, Cause No. 8861.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Franklin Circuit Court (Indiana), of receiving payment while indebted under Ind. Code § 32-8-3-15.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contracted to build a house, and during construction accepted installment payments from the buyers, but did not inform them that he had not yet paid for all the materials used. Defendant declared bankruptcy prior to completing the building of the house, one of his suppliers perfected a mechanic's lien on the property, and defendant was charged and convicted of receiving payment while indebted. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction. The court held that in light of the fact that § 32-8-3-15 omitted language of culpability, knowledge and intent were to be construed as statutory elements of the offense, because § 32-8-3-15 was a criminal statute derived from the common law offense of fraud and that the requirement of a mens rea in offenses from common law derivations was favored. The court found that no evidence of criminal intent on the part of defendant was adduced, and that intent to defraud could not be inferred from defendant's conduct in accepting payments for the work he was providing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for receiving payment while indebted.

Orr v. Turco Mfg. Co.


No. 4-1084 A 292


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee manufacturer filed a notice of exhaustion of appellate proceedings and request for ruling on motion for attorney's fees in appellant claimant's appeal of the decision of the Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana), after the court affirmed the trial court's ruling in favor of the manufacturer in the claimant's product liability action on behalf of her child.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer sought an award of attorney fees on appeal before the court issued its opinion. After the decision, the manufacturer filed a request for ruling on its motion. The claimant argued the manufacturer waived its claim by not seeking rehearing of the decision, claiming that the court implicitly denied the motion by not addressing it. The court remanded the case to the trial court to take evidence and make a recommendation as to the amount of attorney's fees due to the manufacturer and file it with the court for its review and decision.


OUTCOME: The court granted the manufacturer's motion to assess attorney fees, retained jurisdiction of the appeal, and appointed the trial court as commissioner to determine the reasonable value of the services rendered to the manufacturer by its attorneys in the appeal.

Ray v. State


Nos. 4-1083 A 353, 4-883 A 292 CONSOLIDATED


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


496 N.E.2d 93; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2791



July 30, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 25, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Lawrence County Court The Honorable Raymond L. Kern, Judge, Cause Nos. 79-CL-992 and 74 CL 2850.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a decision from the Lawrence County Court (Indiana), which denied their petitions for post-conviction relief after separate trials. The court consolidated the cases to determine whether knowing acquiescence was shown by a guilty plea and whether a lost record entitled the defendants to new trials if they could not reconstruct it.


OVERVIEW: The defendants pled guilty to driving while intoxicated in separate trials and later filed petitions under Ind. Post Conviction Remedies 1 for post-conviction relief. The trial court denied relief on the basis of laches, finding that the defendants' guilty pleas put them on constructive notice of their right to seek post-conviction relief. The defendants appealed. Although the court held that the trial court improperly applied the doctrine of laches to bar the defendants' claims because laches could not be predicated on constructive knowledge, the court affirmed on other grounds. The court held that the failure to prove that a destroyed trial record was impossible to reconstruct barred one defendant from seeking a new trial based on alleged violations of his constitutional rights because there was no evidence from which the court could conclude that his rights had been violated. The court held that the other defendant could not seek post-conviction relief based on newly discovered evidence when he had failed to attack the reliability of breathalyzer equipment at trial, thus showing a lack of due diligence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court.

Indiana & Michigan Electric Co. v. Public Service Com.


No. 2-1284-A-390


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


495 N.E.2d 779; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 3150



July 29, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied November 19, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Public Service Commission of the State of Indiana, Cause No. 37494. Original Opinion of May 7, 1986, Reported at: 492 N.E.2d 323.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant electric utility companies petitioned the court to grant rehearing of its decision dismissing their appeal of a decision of the Public Service Commission of the state of Indiana. The court considered the petition for the limited purposed of addressing the utility companies misconceptions regarding the court's original decision.


OVERVIEW: The electric utility companies argued that the court's previous decision dismissing their appeal was erroneous and conflicted with ruling precedent that the court may assert jurisdiction to review Public Service Commission orders entered in rulemaking proceedings. The court disagreed, finding that the order the companies appealed from was not one contemplated under Ind. Code Ann. § 8-1-3-1 or § 8-1-3-7. Both provisions clearly indicated that to be reviewable, an order must be based upon findings of fact supported by sufficient probative evidence. The commission could only issue such an order after receipt of evidence or factual data and a decision resolving the factual controversy. The order the companies appealed from was one that stated the obvious -- that the commission, after due deliberation and hearing as provided for in Ind. Code Ann. § 4-22-4, had determined that its draft of the proposed rules was ready for submissions to the attorney general and governor for approval. This was not a reviewable order and the companies sought to bypass the administrative procedure governing attempted enforcement or application of rules by seeking review of it.


OUTCOME: The court denied the utility companies' petition for rehearing after addressing misconceptions the companies had regarding the court's earlier dismissal of their appeal of the commission decision.

Board of School Trustees v. Commission on General Education of Indiana State Bd. of Education


No. 2-1283 A 454


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


493 N.E.2d 1262; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2646



June 6, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Circuit Court, The Honorable John M. Ryan, Judge, Cause No. C-83-2471. This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of May 13, 1986, Reported at: 492 N.E.2d 697.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded for further proceedings. Sullivan, J., concurs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In its action for judicial review of a determination made by the Commission on General Education of the Indiana Board of Education, plaintiff school board appealed a judgment of the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied its motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court considered the issue of the school district's right to judicial review of the Commission's decision to certify various plans for selecting the members of the school district's school board. The court found that the key issue was whether the Commission's determination was an administrative adjudication and held that it was not. The court found that the Commission's determination was not an administrative adjudication and that the proceedings before the Commission were not final, and were ministerial and not judicial. The court further found that under the statutory scheme involved in the litigation, plans were submitted to the Commission for review, revision, approval, and certification pursuant to Ind. Code Ann. § 20-4-10.1-9 (1975) and that the review and revision were to insure conformity with statutory guidelines. The court concluded that the procedure did not involve the Administrative Adjudication Act, Ind. Code Ann. § 4-22-1-1 et seq. (1982) because it did not constitute an administrative adjudication, that there was no right to judicial review, and that the trial court properly denied the school district's motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

1151 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Board of School Trustees v. Commission on General Education of Indiana State Bd. of Education


No. 2-1283 A 454


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


492 N.E.2d 697; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2577



May 13, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn June 6, 1986; Substituted Opinion Reported at: 493 N.E.2d 1262.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION CIRCUIT COURT, THE HONORABLE JOHN M. RYAN, JUDGE, CAUSE NO. C83-2471



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners board of school trustees and the school (schools) challenged the decision of the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied its motion for summary judgment in the schools' action, filed pursuant to Indiana's Administrative Adjudication Act (AAA), seeking judicial review of a determination made by respondent Commission on General Education of the State Board of Education.


OVERVIEW: A petition plan to change the method of selecting members of the board of trustees was presented to the school board. The school board disapproved the petition plan on the grounds that it violated the 14th Amendment and Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. The school board then initiated two additional plans. In accordance with Ind. Code § 20-4-10.1-9, all three plans were submitted to the commission for review. The commission determined that all three plans met the statutory limitations of Ind. Code 20-4-10.1-9 and certified the plans to the school board. Thereafter, the schools petitioned for judicial review of the commission's decision and filed a motion for summary judgment. After the trial court denied its motion for summary judgment, the schools appealed. On appeal, the schools argued that the commission's decision was erroneous because it was not supported by the required findings of fact. The court held that the schools' action seeking judicial review of the commission's decision did not involve the AAA because the decision did not constitute an administrative adjudication. Hence, the court held that there was no right to judicial review pursuant to the AAA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

1152 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Indiana & Michigan Electric Co. v. Public Service Com.


No. 2-1284-A-390


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


492 N.E.2d 323; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2550



May 7, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 29, 1986, Reported at: 495 N.E.2d 779.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Public Service Commission of the State of Indiana, Cause No. 37494.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant electric utilities sought review of a refusal by the Public Service Commission of the State of Indiana to stay and suspend enforcement of its rules, and an order that amended the rules to clarify them in reference to federal law. Appellees, public service commission (commission), state agency, and customer, filed a motion to dismiss the appeal on the basis that the there was no subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The commission claimed that that two documents designated as "orders" did not trigger judicial review pursuant to Ind. Code § 8-1-3-7 because the electric utilities' challenge was to the rule-making process itself which was not directly reviewable. The court granted the appellees' motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Direct review under § 8-1-3-7 was appropriate only upon the commission's decisions, rulings, or orders which were rendered to resolve factual issues in a given circumstance. In contrast the "orders" at issue were rendered under the commission's rulemaking function because they operated in general upon a class of utilities. Accordingly, the commission's "orders" which addressed the electric utilities' challenge to the commission's authority to promulgate rules, and the clarifying "order", which operated prospectively upon the class were rulemaking actions and were not subject to direct review. The court also concurred in the commission's refusal to declare portions of its rules unconstitutional or preempted by federal law because it lacked authority to issue declaratory rulings, and there could no appeal from its refusal to do so.


OUTCOME: The court granted the appellees' motion to dismiss the electric utilities' appeal to the commission's refusal to stay and suspend enforcement of its rules, and as to an order that amended the rules to clarify a reference to federal law. The dismissal was without prejudice to the electric utilities' right to seek relief in the appropriate forum.

 

1153 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Finney v. State


No. 1-1185 A 289


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


491 N.E.2d 1029; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2536



April 30, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Vanderburgh Circuit Court; The Honorable Robert S. Matthews, Judge, Cause No. 4641.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of driving a motor vehicle when his blood alcohol content was .10 percent or greater as a class D felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended the statute under which he was charged was unconstitutional, and that the class C misdemeanor charges was an insufficient basis for enhancement to a class D felony. An officer stopped defendant after he crossed the centerline of highway and drove erratically. An intoxilyzer test was administered that revealed defendant's blood alcohol was .10 percent. The court held that Ind. Code Ann. § 9-11-2-1 (Supp. 1985), which prohibited a person from driving a motor vehicle with .10 percent or more by weight of alcohol in his blood, was not unconstitutional. The court held that the legislature had authority to regulate traffic upon public highways and had authority to prohibit a person having a blood alcohol of .10 percent or more to drive a motor vehicle upon the highways. The court also held § 9-11-2-1 was not violative of the constitutional protection against double jeopardy because defendant was neither subjected to nor could he have been subjected to multiple punishment for the same offense. The court also held his conviction of a class C felony properly formed the basis for enhancement of the offense to a class D felony under Ind. Code Ann. § 9-11-2-3 (Supp. 1985).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1154 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Medical Licensing Bd. v. Brady


No. 1-985 A 223


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


492 N.E.2d 34; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2534



April 28, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Monroe Circuit Court, The Honorable James M. Dixon, Judge, Cause No. CV8503 047A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state and Medical Licensing Board of Indiana (collectively board), sought review of orders of the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana) denying the board's verified petition for injunction and granting appellee tattoo artist's request for an injunction against the board. The board alleged that the tattoo artist was engaged in the unlawful practice of medicine in violation of Ind. Code Ann. § 25-22.5-8-1 (amended 1985).


OVERVIEW: The board claimed that the tattooing of individuals was the practice of medicine or osteopathic medicine under § 25-22.5-8-1. The trial court granted the tattoo artist's request under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for an injunction to enjoin the board from enforcing Ind. Code Ann. § 25-22.5-8-1 (amended 1985), claiming that such violated his rights under the First Amendment. The court disagreed with the trial court's interpretation of the subject statute and reversed the judgment. The court held that the statutory definition of the practice of medicine in Ind. Code Ann. § 25-22.5-8-1 (amended 1985) encompassed the tattooing of individuals for any purpose. The phrase for the intended palliation, relief, cure or prevention of an ailment was intended to modify "the penetration of the skin or body orifice," because the statute's definition would otherwise have been redundant and nonsensical. The court held that tattooing for artistic purposes was not protected by the First Amendment and that the application of § 25-22.5-8-1 to tattooing was not unconstitutionally arbitrary or capricious. The court remanded the case with instructions to grant the board's petition for an injunction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which granted the tattoo artist's request for an injunction against the board and denied the board's verified petition for an injunction. The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions for the trial court to enter judgment in favor of the board on its verified petition.

Haverstock v. State Public Employees Retirement Fund


No. 2-585 A 1601


1 This case was diverted from the Second District to the First District by order of the Chief Judge.


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


490 N.E.2d 357; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2427



March 20, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 12, 1986; Transfer Denied August 29, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Marion Superior Court Civil Division, Room 7, The Honorable Gerald Zore, Judge, (Cause No. S780-1601).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a class of police officers and firefighters, sought review of a grant of summary judgment by the Marion Superior Court Civil Division (Indiana) in favor of appellee public employees' retirement fund (PERF) in appellants' complaint seeking a declaratory judgment determining that a new pension plan could not be applied retroactively to those police officers and firefighters hired prior to the date of its enactment.


OVERVIEW: At the time appellants were hired, the pension plan would have permitted them to collect benefits after 20 years of service. However, a new pension plan was adopted by legislation that provided that a member was eligible for retirement after completing 20 years of service or reaching age 55, whichever came later. This new plan was made effective retroactively to appellants who had been employed for less than 25 days. Appellants filed a class action seeking a declaratory judgment that the new pension plan could not be applied retroactively. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of PERF. On appeal, the court affirmed. Because appellants' participation in the pension plan was compulsory, they had no contractual rights in the plan that was operating at the time they were hired. Therefore, the retroactive effect of the new pension plan did not result in an unconstitutional impairment of contractual rights under either U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 or Ind. Const. art. I, § 24. Retroactive application of the new pension plan did not violate appellants' equal protection rights. The legislature had a rational basis for determining the effective date of the new pension plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee in appellants' complaint seeking a declaratory judgment that a new pension plan could not be applied retroactively.

Indiana State Bd. of Registration of Architects v. Meier


No. 4-885 A 216


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


489 N.E.2d 966; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2394



March 10, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, Room No. 7, The Honorable Gerald S. Zore, Judge, Cause No. S783-1386



DISPOSITION: The court below is affirmed and this cause is remanded to the Board for further determination consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Indiana State Board of Registration of Architects sought review of a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which set aside the Board's denial of appellee architect's application for certification as a landscape architect.


OVERVIEW: The architect applied for waiver of the college degree and examination requirements for certification on the basis that his landscape architectural experience exceeded the statutory requirement under the Indiana Landscape Architects' Certification Act (the Act), Ind. Code § 25-4-2-1 to -12 (1982). The Board denied the application, and the architect sought review in the trial court. The trial court set aside the Board's denial as arbitrary, capricious, and in excess of the Board's statutory authority. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court, holding that the Board ignored the standard governing the exercise of its discretion. Specifically, the Board failed to demonstrate any relationship between its finding that the architect did not have 12 years of full-time experience and its ultimate conclusion that the architect was not qualified for certification under the Act. The Board heard no evidence and made no finding that 12 years of full-time experience was necessary to render the applicant competent in the eight categories of landscape architectural services under Ind. Code § 25-4-2-1(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed trial court's judgment and remanded the cause to the Board for further determination.

Gibraltar Mut. Ins. Co. v. Hoosier Ins. Co.

DISPOSITION: Our opinion dated December 11, 1985, is hereby modified as expressed herein, and the petition for rehearing is denied in all other respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an appeal from a judgement of the Marion Circuit Court (Indianapolis) in which the court affirmed the circuit court's entry of summary judgment in favor of defendants, an insurer and an individual, in an action for libel brought by plaintiff insurance company, the insurance company filed a petition for a rehearing.


OVERVIEW: In the court's original opinion it held that Ind. Code § 27-1-6-15 (1986) did not eliminate truth as a defense to libel and was applicable on its fact to insurers. The court held that inasmuch as the subject letter to the state life and health guaranty association merely stated that the insurance company was not in compliance with that statute the letter was not libelous. The insurance company claimed that the opinion erred by failing to recognize the existence of two separate guaranty associations and by refusing to hold that Ind. Code § 27-4-1-4 (1986) created a new private right of action. On review, the court held that the insurance company had not convinced it that its decision should have been otherwise. The insurance company argued that because the individual's letter was directed at the "wrong" guaranty association that the court committed error. The court held because it concluded that the contents of the letter were true and not otherwise prohibited, it did not reach the question of whether the communication was privileged. Thus, the preceding discussion of the separate associations had no impact on its original conclusion.


OUTCOME: The court modified the modified its prior order and denied the petition for rehearing.

Smith v. State


No. 4-985 A 250


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


489 N.E.2d 140; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2341



February 24, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 5, 1986; Transfer denied November 6, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Marion County Municipal Court, Room No. 9, The Honorable Charles A. Wiles, Judge, Cause No. A984-07525.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for battery by the Marion County Municipal Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: The evidence supporting the judgment indicated that defendant repeatedly hit his daughter with a belt for approximately 10 minutes after she received a report card with failing grades. Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support conviction and that his due process rights were violated in that he was convicted of battering his child despite the parental authority afforded by Ind. Code § 35-41-3-1 or , in the alternative, because the misdemeanor battery statute and the statute recognizing parental authority to punish a child were unconstitutionally vague in failing to fairly advise him of the limits of authorized punishment. The court found that the duration and intensity of the beating, together with the numerous wounds evident in photographs of the victim contained in the record, sufficiently supported the trial court's determination that defendant's parental discipline was unreasonable and therefore beyond the bounds of his legal authority. No reasonable person of ordinary intelligence would have difficulty determining that the beating defendant inflicted on his daughter was excessive and not protected parental discipline.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for battery.

 

1161 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Gary v. Redmond


No. 3-485 A 101


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


489 N.E.2d 543; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2362



February 18, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Lake Superior Court, Room No. Four, The Honorable Gerald Svetanoff, Judge, Cause No. 484-14.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision from the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which awarded attorney fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 in a cause of action under the Indiana Tort Claims Act, Ind. Code § 34-4-16.5-1 et seq., for damages resulting from the demolition of appellee property owner's building located in Gary, Indiana.


OVERVIEW: The city presented only one issue for review: whether the property owner was entitled to attorney fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 as the prevailing party in a case amounting to a common law tort claim and properly resolved pursuant to the Indiana Tort Claims Act. On appeal, the court held that the Indiana Tort Claims Act gave the property owner the opportunity for an ultimate judicial determination of liability. The court held that, since the facts of this case did not present a claim for relief under 42 U.S.C.S. Section 1983, the property owner was not entitled to an award of attorney's fees as a prevailing party on a federal claim under § 1988. The court also held that the property owner's claim was not pendent to a substantial federal constitutional issue which would warrant an award of attorney's fees under § 1988. The court held that since the property owner had not prevailed on a claim enumerated under § 1988 and had not presented a substantial constitutional claim pendent to his successful tort claim, an award of attorney's fees based on § 1988 was not authorized. Accordingly, the court reversed the trial court's award of attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's award of attorney fees. The court held that, since the facts of this case did not present a claim for relief under federal civil rights statutes, the property owner was not entitled to an award of attorney's fees as a prevailing party on a federal claim under the applicable federal statute authorizing attorney fees.

 

1162 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hunt v. State


No. 2-1084 A 325


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


487 N.E.2d 1330; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 2260



January 23, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion County Municipal Court, Room No. 10, The Honorable A. Toni Cordingly, Judge, Cause No. M1083-8473.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded with instructions to vacate the guilty plea.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the judgment of the Marion County Municipal Court (Indiana) which refused to vacate a guilty plea entered by petitioner to the offense of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor. Petitioner alleged he did not knowingly and intelligently relinquish his constitutional rights when he entered the guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner signed a prepared form that listed the constitutional rights of Ind. Code Ann. § 35-35-1-2 (Supp. 1983) and pleaded guilty to driving under the influence. The judge asked petitioner if he signed the bottom of the form but asked no further questions concerning whether petitioner understood the constitutional rights he was waiving. Petitioner contended that the post-conviction court erred in concluding he knowingly and intelligently waived his constitutional rights. The court reversed and vacated the plea. The failure of the trial court to ask any questions concerning petitioner's understanding of the rights he was waiving, whether petitioner had read the form he signed, or whether petitioner was literate in reading the English language evidenced the fact that the trial judge could not have made an independent determination of petitioner's understanding of the rights he was waiving at the time of the guilty plea hearing. Although the trial judge did not have to personally advise petitioner of his constitutional rights, the judge was required to make an independent determination, based on the record, that petitioner's plea was entered voluntarily and knowingly.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the cause remanded with instructions to vacate the guilty plea.

Baesler's Super-Valu v. Indiana Comm'r of Labor


No. 84A01-8603-CV-73


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


500 N.E.2d 243; 1986 Ind. App. LEXIS 3158; 27 Wage & Hour Cas. (BNA) 1562



November, 26, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Vigo County Court Small Claims Division, Division No. 4, The Honorable John C. Kite, Judge, Cause No. CO-SC-85-1684.



DISPOSITION:  Judgment affirmed in its entirety.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed a judgment of the Vigo County Court, Small Claims Division (Indiana) in favor of plaintiff labor commissioner, in an action on behalf of a former employee for unpaid vacation pay. The employer contended the trial court erred in finding that the employee, whose employment terminated after a union negotiated employment contract expired, was entitled to accrued vacation pay.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff labor commissioner filed suit against defendant employer, on behalf of a former employee, for unpaid vacation pay. The trial court awarded enhanced damages to the employee pursuant to Ind. Code §§ 22-2-5-1 and 2, and attorney's fees. On review, the employer contended the trial court erred in finding that the employee, whose employment terminated after a union negotiated employment contract expired, was entitled to accrued vacation pay. The appeals court stated that under the common law, once a trial court finds that an agreement to give vacation pay was made, and the services are rendered by the employee as promised, the trial court must find, as a matter of law, that the right to receive compensation is "vested." Thus, because there was nothing in the contract indicating that the parties intended their relationship to vary from the common law, the employee was entitled to compensation as a matter of law, even after the expiration of the negotiated union contract. The court noted that it would be coercive to condition the receipt of the benefits accruing under the old contract on the ratification of a new contract.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment in favor of the labor commissioner because the trial court's conclusion that the employer failed to pay the employee's accrued vacation pay, as required by statute, was well supported by the evidence. The failure to pay the employee in this manner activated the statutory penalty provision without any further showing.

No. 2-1284-A-362


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


502 N.E.2d 490; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 3132



December 30, 1985, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff real estate developer appealed the judgment of the Huntington Circuit Court (Indiana) in favor of defendants, county health officer, members of the county board of health (collectively the county), and the Indiana State Board of Health (state), upon the developer's complaint for a declaratory judgment. The developer sought a permit to install a subsurface sand filter sewage disposal system on a lot in a subdivision he was developing.


OVERVIEW: Huntington County, Ind., Ordinance No. 1-1965 prohibited the installation of sand filter disposal systems in Huntington County. The developer sought a permit to install a subsurface sand filter disposal system on a lot in his development. The county denied his request. The developer sought a declaratory judgment that the denial of the permit was a taking. The trial court found in favor of the county and the state. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The trial court's finding of fact that multiple contagious diseases could filter through a sand filter sewage disposal system was not contrary to the weight of the evidence. The denial of a sewage permit for the lot was a proper exercise of police power and not clearly erroneous. Sand filter systems could contribute to the spread of disease in the county. The denial of a sewage permit was not arbitrary and capricious, or an abuse of discretion. There was no unconstitutional taking of property without just compensation contrary to law. The developer was not denied any vested right. The lot was not exempt from state residential sewage disposal regulations by virtue of Ind. Admin. Code tit. 410, § 6-8-12(C).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Bergmann v. State


No. 4-585 A 140


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


486 N.E.2d 653; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 3026



December 26, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Noble Superior Court, The Honorable Roger B. Cosbey, Judge, Cause No. SCR-84-17.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged an order from the Noble Superior Court (Indiana) that convicted them of reckless homicide and neglect of a dependant, violation of Ind. Code §§ 35-42-1-5, 35-46-1-4.


OVERVIEW: When defendants' child became ill, they treated her with prayer, fasting, and reading. After her death, they were convicted of reckless homicide and neglect of a dependant, and on appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err in refusing to dismiss the jury panel after a panelist stated that he had already formed an opinion because he did not prejudice the other jurors and the trial court gave an admonition to the jury. The trial court properly admitted expert testimony as to the cause of the child's death because it was probative, even though the expert was not absolutely certain as to his conclusion. Defendants were not entitled to a Miranda warning when they spoke to police and a coroner at their home because they were not in custody, nor were they deprived of freedom of action in any way. It was not error for the state to rely on its case-in-chief to rebut defendants' mistake of fact defense, nor was it required to negate defendants' religious practice affirmative defense. The reckless homicide convictions were not contrary to the law because the evidence was clearly sufficient to show the voluntary nature of defendants' failure to seek medical attention.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order convicting defendants of reckless homicide and neglect of a dependant.

Indiana Hospital Licensing Council v. Women's Pavilion of South Bend


No. 3-783 A 219


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


486 N.E.2d 1070; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 3017



December 23, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the St. Joseph Circuit Court The Honorable John W. Montgomery, Judge, Cause No. K-1521.



DISPOSITION: Therefore, we hold the trial court was in error in applying a multiplier to the lodestar figure, as well as in awarding the costs of printing the briefs to Pavilion. Reversed and remanded for entry of judgment consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensing council and appellee abortion clinic both sought review of an order from the St. Joseph Circuit Court (Indiana), which awarded appellate attorneys' fees to the law firm representing the abortion clinic in the appeal of a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim. The claim involved the constitutionality of the application of a statute that infringed on the abortion clinic's practice of performing first-trimester abortions.


OVERVIEW: The abortion clinic was successful in the underlying action and in the appeal, which determined that the attempted regulation of first-trimester abortions through the application of Ind. Code § 16-10-1-7 constituted an impermissible degree of state interference during the first trimester. After the court affirmed the judgment, it remanded the action to the trial court for an award of appellate attorneys' fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The court reversed and remanded the attorneys' fee award. The court concluded that the trial court erred in applying a 100 percent multiplier to the lodestar figure and in awarding to the abortion clinic the costs of printing briefs. Although the court found that the case could be considered undesirable, it concluded that the negative impact of the case was diminished by the fact that counsel was not a member of the local community. Additionally, because the majority of the billable hours in the lodestar were attributed to less-experienced associates, the court concluded that reputation and ability did not justify the application of a multiplier. Finally, the court found that the appellate issues were not particularly novel or complex.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that awarded appellate attorneys' fees to the abortion clinic in the licensing council's appeal of a claim involving the constitutionality of a licensing statute. The court remanded the action for a reduction in the amount of the attorneys' fee award.
