Empire Gas of Rochester, Inc. v. State


No. 3-683 A 178


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


486 N.E.2d 1036; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 3080



December 17, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer denied January 7, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Fulton Circuit Court The Honorable Douglas B. Morton, Judge, Cause Number C-81-340.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Indiana State Board of Tax Commissioners (board), assessed to appellant taxpayers personal property taxes on the value of gas storage tanks owned by the taxpayers and leased to their customers in 1979 and 1980. The taxpayers appealed the assessment to the Fulton Circuit Court (Indiana). Cross-motions for summary judgment were filed. The taxpayers sought review of the grant of summary judgment to the board as to the 1980 assessment.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers' motion for summary judgment on the 1979 assessment was granted. The grant of summary judgment to the board was due to a 1980 regulatory change to Ind. Admin. Code tit. 50, r. 4-1-6-2, which transferred primary tax liability to the taxpayers. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The tanks were neither fixtures not appurtenances and thus were not real property under Ind. Code § 6-1.1-1-15. The tanks did meet the definition of personal property under § 6-1.1-1-11 as they were tangible property held, used, or consumed in connection with the production of income. Ind. Admin. Code tit. 50, r. 6-1.1-2-4 did not place primary tax liability on the possessor. Though personal property held under capital leases were assessed to possessors, tit. 50, r. 4.1-6-3, 93 percent of the leases were residential. Because the tanks were not used in a trade or business or held for the production of income, they were operating leases which, under tit. 50, r. 4.1-6-3(B), were assessed to the owners. The court reversed the grant of summary judgment as to the remaining seven percent of the leases and remanded for a determination of whether they were capital or operating leases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the grant of summary judgment to the board in the taxpayers' action that sought judicial review of the board's personal property tax assessment to taxpayers. The court reversed that portion of the grant of summary judgment which concerned the non-residential gas tank leases and remanded to the trial court for a determination as to whether those leases were capital or operating leases.

 

1168 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Gibraltar Mut. Ins. Co. v. Hoosier Ins. Co.


No. 2-484-A-115


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


486 N.E.2d 548; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 3027



December 11, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Marion Circuit Court, The Honorable John M. Ryan, Judge, Cause No. C82-1887.



DISPOSITION: The summary judgment in favor of Hoosier and Loudermilk and against Gibraltar is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurance company appealed a grant of summary judgment by the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana) for defendants, competitor and employee, in its action for libel, claiming that it was not subject to the provisions of Ind. Code § 27-1-6-15, that even if the contents of the competitor's letter were true, dissemination of information about the insurance company's financial condition was malum prohibitum and contrary to public policy.


OVERVIEW: The competitor wrote to the insurance guaranty association, alleging that the insurance company did not have the surplus required to be maintained by § 27-1-6-15. The competitor requested corrective action or that the company be prohibited from writing insurance. The trial court granted summary judgment for defendants in the company's libel action. The court affirmed the judgment below, rejecting the company's claims that it was not subject to § 27-1-6-15 or that the statute was unconstitutional. The legislative scheme regulating the insurance business was within the exercise of the state's police power. Ind. Code § 27-4-1-1, Indiana's unfair competition act regulating the insurance business, did not support the company's position. That statute did not in any way affect the nature of common law relief afforded to a party who was libeled, whether the act constituted unfair competition or otherwise. The court also rejected the company's claim that truth as a defense was eliminated by §§ 27-9-2-3, 27-1-3-11. Those sections applied only when an insurer was subjected to an examination or delinquency proceeding and were not related to a private cause of action between insurers, as here.


OUTCOME: In the company's action for libel, the court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment for defendants.

 

1169 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Orr v. Turco Mfg. Co.


No. 4-1084 A 292


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


484 N.E.2d 1300; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2931; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P10,781



November 5, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 30, 1985; Transfer denied March 27, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Hamilton Superior Court, Room No. 2 The Honorable Jerry M. Barr, Presiding Cause No. 2S 83-378.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On behalf of her minor ward, plaintiff guardian brought a product liability suit against defendant manufacturer. The Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana) entered a judgment that granted the manufacturer's motion to dismiss the guardian's product liability suit. The guardian sought review.


OVERVIEW: When she was 10 years old, the ward was injured while playing on a swingset manufactured by the manufacturer. Over four years later, the guardian brought the product liability suit. The manufacturer's motion to dismiss alleged that the product liability statute of limitations, specifically Ind. Code § 33-1-1.5-5, prohibited the action because it was filed over two years after the injury had occurred. On appeal, the guardian contended that § 33-1-1.5-5 did not apply to persons with a legal disability or minority status established by Ind. Code § 34-1-2-5. The court held that Ind. Code § 33-1-1.5-5 was not subject to judicial interpretation because it was clear and unambiguous as to the elimination of minority and legal disability in product liability actions. For the same reason, the trial court did not err by refusing to admit legislative history to determine the meaning of § 33-1-1.5-5. Furthermore, the Product Liability Act, specifically Ind. Code § 33-1-1.5-1, did not contravene Ind. Const. art. 1, § 12. In this respect, the Indiana Legislature was not constitutionally mandated to suspend the obligation of statutes of limitation in the case of infancy or incapacity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that dismissed the guardian's product liability suit against the manufacturer.

 

1170 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hobson v. State


No. 3-585 A 132


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


484 N.E.2d 601; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2895



October 28, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Elkhart County Court Honorable James W. Rieckhoff, Judge Cause No. 04132.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the trial court's judgment is affirmed. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Elkhart County Court (Indiana) entered a judgment that convicted defendant of engaging in the business of selling motor vehicles on Sunday in violation of Ind. Code § 24-4-6-1, a Class B misdemeanor. Defendant challenged his conviction on the bases of vagueness and unconstitutionality of the offended statute.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff visited defendant's place of business on a Sunday, and asked whether he was open for business. Defendant responded affirmatively. Defendant also stated that he had not yet sold anything that day, but he would if the opportunity arose. Additionally, defendant discussed the purchase of a particular motor home with the sheriff. Consequently, defendant was charged with violating § 24-4-6-1, which prohibited engaging in the business of selling motor vehicles on Sunday. After he was convicted as charged, defendant sought review. The court affirmed, holding that § 24-4-6-1 was sufficiently definite so as to inform a reasonable person of the prohibited conduct. Defendant's vagueness attack focused on the definition of "motor vehicles." However, any self-propelled recreational vehicle was a motor vehicle pursuant to Ind. Code § 9-1-1-2(b). Defendant also challenged the constitutionality of Ind. Code § 24-4-6-1. Yet, because the state supreme court had already determined that the predecessor statute to § 24-4-6-1 was constitutional and rightfully enacted within the scope of the Indiana Legislature's authority, such analysis applied with equal force to § 24-4-6-1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of engaging in the business of selling motor vehicles on Sunday.

 

1171 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Lewis v. State


No. 3-685 A 141


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


484 N.E.2d 77; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2887



October 24, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 13, 1985; Transfer denied May 22, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from St. Joseph Superior Court Honorable Jeanne Swartz, Judge Cause Number 24414.



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons the judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of carrying a handgun without a license under Ind. Code § 35-47-2-24 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of carrying a handgun without a license under § 35-47-2-24 and upon review the court affirmed. The court held that because the jury was free to disbelieve defendant's version of the events, there was sufficient evidence to allow a finding that he "knowingly possessed" the gun. The court held that § 35-47-2-24 was constitutional. The court held that it was not unconstitutional for a statute to impose the burden of proof upon defendant that he possessed a license to carry the gun because the issue was not an element of the crime. The court held that proof of a license was an exemption or exception to, and not an element of the crime under § 35-47-2-24. The court held that even if the State had the burden on that issue, because defendant admitted in his testimony that he did not have a license to carry the gun, there was sufficient evidence that the State had carried the burden of proving that he had no license. The court held that because defendant failed to show that he was harmed by the trial court's refusal of his requested instructions, the trial court did not commit reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for carrying a handgun without a license.

Terpstra v. Farmers & Merchants Bank

Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


483 N.E.2d 749; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2820

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, property owners and bank, filed suit to have liens placed on their property by defendant individual removed. The Fulton Circuit Court (Indiana) granted summary judgment and a declaratory judgment to the property owners and the bank. The individual appealed.


OVERVIEW: The individual and his son filed suit in federal court against the property owners alleging breach of contract and tort claims. Hall v. State


No. 3-485 A 77


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


482 N.E.2d 1185; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2801



September 26, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 3, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Whitley Circuit Court Honorable Edward J. Meyers, Judge Cause No. S-84-13.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged a judgment from the Whitley Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted them of reckless homicide, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-42-1-5, and neglect of a dependent, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4.


OVERVIEW: A sheriff discovered that defendants' one month old son was dead. Defendants told the sheriff that he had been ill for approximately five days and that his condition had worsened within the last two. They had not sought medical care. Doctors testified at defendants' trial that had medical treatment been sought, there would have been a very reasonably good chance of saving his life. Defendants testified that they had sought no medical treatment because of their religious beliefs. Defendants were convicted of reckless homicide and neglect of a dependent. On appeal they contended, among other things, that the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict of guilty on the charge of neglect of a dependent. They argued that the State failed to disprove their statutory defense. When a defendant raised the defense that in the legitimate practice of his religious belief, he provided treatment by spiritual means through prayer, in lieu of medical care; the defendant had to shoulder the burden of proving the defense. Because the jury was in the best position to judge defendants' credibility and it was apparent they failed to believe their testimony; the verdict was not disturbed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1174 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


In re M.R.D.


No. 2-485 A 1051


1 This case was diverted from the Second District to the First District by order of the Chief Judge.


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


482 N.E.2d 306; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2729



August 29, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 7, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Wells Circuit Court The Honorable David L. Hanselman, Sr., Judge (Cause No. J-84-83).



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is, therefore, reversed and this case is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Wells Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted the motion of defendant juvenile to suppress evidence, in the State's delinquency petition against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a search warrant, the police conducted a search of a premises for underage drinking. The warrant was issued by a judge based upon the testimony of a parent. The affidavit stated that a parent had been told by her child that there would be underage drinking at a certain address. The police drove past the house and confirmed that there were many vehicles parked near the house, indicating a party. As a result of the search, defendant was charged with possession of an alcoholic beverage. In the delinquency proceeding, defendant filed a motion to suppress all evidence connected with the search because the affidavit failed to establish probable cause. The trial court granted the motion. The State appealed. The court held that although the affidavit lacked probable cause the evidence was admissible under the "good faith" exception to the exclusionary rule. The affidavit contained no information bearing on the parent's veracity or upon her basis of knowledge. However, although the affidavit was not supported by probable cause, it stated information sufficient to have been relied upon. Therefore, the evidence collected in a good faith reliance on the warrant was admissible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Grogan v. State


No. 1-585 A 120


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


482 N.E.2d 300; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2728



August 29, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 7, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Lawrence County Court The Honorable Raymond L. Kern, Judge (Cause No. 84 CL 79).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Lawrence County Court (Indiana), which convicted him of driving while his license was suspended in violation of Ind. Code § 9-1-4-52 and driving while intoxicated in violation of Ind. Code § 9-11-2.2.


OVERVIEW: The trial court instructed the jury in the precise language of Ind. Code § 9-1-4-52.5, which provided that the burden was on defendant to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that he had been issued a driving license that was valid at the time of the alleged crime. On appeal, defendant argued that the instruction shifted the burden of proof away from the state and effectively required defendant to prove his innocence. Because the jury was not instructed concerning the state's burden with respect to the elements of the crime of driving with a suspended license, the court held that § 9-1-4-52.5 was unconstitutionally applied in defendant's case. Therefore, the court reversed defendant's conviction for driving with a suspended license. The court, however, concluded that § 9-1-4-52.5 could be interpreted to meet constitutional requirements. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated, rejecting defendant's contention that the results of his breath test were improperly admitted into evidence. The court concluded that the foundation for the test results adequately established the operator's certification and the technique used in administering the test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated. The court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction for driving with a suspended license.

Richard v. State


No. 1-1284 A 311


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


482 N.E.2d 282; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2725



August 28, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Harrison County Court The Honorable Maryland L. Austin, Judge Cause No. CCR-83-503.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment the Harrison County Court (Indiana), which convicted them of different offenses including unlawfully possessing a deer, Ind. Code § 14-2-3-3; hunting and taking a deer out of season, Ind. Code § 14-2-3-3; and possession of more than 30 grams of marijuana, Ind. Code § 35-48-4-11. Defendants did not appeal their convictions for hunting without the landowner's permission, Ind. Code § 14-2-6-1.


OVERVIEW: Following an accidental shooting of a man with a deer slug, the conservation officer searched the homes of the defendants who had been at the shooting. The officer found deer parts indicating that they had been deer hunting out of season and marijuana. At trial, the court denied defendants' motion to suppress the evidence obtained through the warrantless search and defendants were convicted. On appeal, the court reversed. Under Ind. Code 14-3-4-9(b) conservation officers were law enforcement officers, and the court found they were subject to the guarantees related to unreasonable search and seizures in U.S. Const. amend. IV and Ind. Const. art. 1, § 11. The court found that the state bore the burden of proving the warrantless search fit within an exception to the premise that a search warrant was required for a valid search, and that the state did not meet this burden. Even with the other reasons the officer had for searching, such as anonymous tips, the court concluded that there was not probable cause to justify the searches.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions by the trial court for unlawfully possessing a deer, hunting and taking a deer out of season, and possession of marijuana.

Davis v. State


No. 3-485 A 80


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


481 N.E.2d 434; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2695



August 15, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 25, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Porter Superior Court Honorable Roger v. Bradford, Judge Cause No. 83-PSCr-101.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), which, following a jury trial, convicted him of nonsupport of a child, a Class D felony, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-46-1-5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in ruling that he carried the burden of proving by a preponderance of the evidence that he was unable to provide support and erred in refusing a tendered jury instruction. The court affirmed the judgment. The court stated that defendant was charged under Ind. Code § 35-46-1-5, which had two elements: (1) knowingly or intentionally, and (2) failing to provide support. Ability to pay was not an element of this offense. Therefore, the court held that it was not constitutionally impermissible to require defendant to bear the burden of proving his defense of inability to pay. In addition, the court held that defendant's support obligations did not constitute a debt and, therefore, the constitutional proscription against imprisonment for debts was inapplicable to his case. The court found that defendant's tendered instruction was mere surplusage in light of the instruction given by the trial court. Thus, the trial court did not err in refusing to read it to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Jackson v. Farmers State Bank


No. 4-284 A 551


1 This case was diverted to the First District from the Fourth District by order of the Chief Judge.


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


481 N.E.2d 395; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2688



August 5, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 18, 1985. Transfer denied January 20, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Wabash Circuit Court The Honorable Douglas B. Morton, Special Judge The Honorable Lynn Ford, Judge (Cause No. C-80-383)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, debtor, guarantors, and garnishees, sought review of the decision of the Wabash Circuit Court (Indiana), which determined that the debtor and the guarantors were liable to plaintiff bank on notes and installment contracts, that the guarantors fraudulently transferred property that rendered them insolvent to avoid their indebtedness to the bank, and that the transfers to the garnishees were void as to the bank.


OVERVIEW: The debtor was a car dealership owned and operated by the guarantors who guaranteed all of the debtor's financing plans with the bank. The court found that the debtor was a recourse endorser of its customers' installment contracts and any right to notice or any right to require the bank to exercise another remedy before exercising its right of recourse had been explicitly waived. The court found that the guarantors as owner-operators were aware of the debtor's liabilities and their guaranty agreement also waived any notice requirement. The guarantors were prohibited from contending they were injured by impairment of security when they consented to release of the collateral in each instance. Although the trial court erroneously found that the guarantors' conveyances made the guarantors legally insolvent, the court rejected insolvency as an indispensable element of a fraudulent conveyance action. The court concluded that the trial court property exercised its equitable jurisdiction in setting aside the conveyances to the garnishees because there were clear indicia that the guarantors fraudulently conveyed the properties to avoid their debts to the bank.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments setting aside the guarantors' conveyances to the garnishees.

OVERVIEW: The decedent, a Seventh Day Adventist, developed a lump in her breast. She consulted defendants, two members of her church, neither of whom were physicians, but who ran a clinic. OVERVIEW: The restaurant purchased commercially zoned property near an interstate highway. Maxey v. Board of Zoning Appeals


No. 3-1084 A 280


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


480 N.E.2d 589; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2641



July 24, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 30, 1985; Transfer denied January 6, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Porter Circuit Court Honorable Raymond D. Kickbush, Judge Cause Number 84-PCC-84.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged an order of the Porter Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted the motion to dismiss of appellee Board of Zoning Appeals (board) in the landowner's action seeking review of the denial of their application for certificate of occupancy. The landowners also sought review of the decision that upheld the board's denial of their petition for a variance.


OVERVIEW: The landowners purchased property that was formerly used by the community schools as a bus maintenance and storage facility. They planned to use it as a vehicle maintenance garage. The circuit court dismissed the landowners' suit seeking review of the denial of a certificate of occupancy. Thereafter the landowners sought a variance, which the board denied. The circuit court upheld the board's denial. The court affirmed the circuit court's decisions and rejected the landowners' contention that the proposed use was a continuation of a prior nonconforming use. Instead, the use was never nonconforming because, although vehicle maintenance garages were not allowed in an R-1 zoning district, school uses were permitted and the bus barn was permitted as an accessory school use. In addition, the denial of the variance was not an unconstitutional taking of property as the change from a limited public purpose use to a less limited commercial purpose would adversely affect the essential character of the residential neighborhood as the comings and goings of the public seeking vehicle repair year round differed significantly from the maintenance of school buses during part of the year.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's dismissal of the landowners' action challenging the denial of their certificate of occupancy and the circuit court's decision that upheld the board's denial of the landowners' petition for a variance.

B & M Coal Corp. v. United Mine Workers


No. 4-884 A 2311


1 This case was diverted from the Fourth District by order of the Chief Judge.


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


480 N.E.2d 227; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2587



July 8, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Spencer Circuit Court The Honorable Edward C. Theobald, Special Judge (Cause No. C 77-261).



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant coal corporation challenged the judgment of the Spencer Circuit Court (Indiana) that found in favor of appellees, the labor union, the union members, the Spencer County, Indiana, Clerk, the Spencer County, Indiana, Auditor, the Spencer County, Indiana, Council, and the Spencer County, Indiana, Board of Commissioner, in the action to recover accrued interest on an appeal bond.


OVERVIEW: The company obtained a judgment against the union and its members to recover damages arising from a raid during a strike. When the union and the union members appealed, the County held the $ 160,363 deposited as an appeal bond. The interest on the funds was retained by the County for four years, pursuant to Ind. Code 5-13-1-3.5(b). For the remaining two years, the interest was added to the company's damage fund. After the appellate decision in favor of the company, the funds were transferred to the company, however, the judgment was not fully satisfied. The circuit court held that the company was not entitled to the interest retained by the County for four years. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment, finding that application of § 5-13-1-3.5(b) to the bond fund violated the Just Compensation Clause and Ind. Const. art. 1, § 21. The company had a protectable property interest in the accrued interest. Also, the company had a property right in the award. The court then held that the expropriation of interest was not justified as an amount lawfully due the County as a fee for the Clerk's management services. Such services were to be compensated at public expense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1183 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Sobieralski v. South Bend


No. 4-984 A 256


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


479 N.E.2d 98; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2528



June 19, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 7, 1985; Transfer Denied January 6, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the St. Joseph Superior Court The Honorable William Whitman, Judge Cause No. 4554.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee City of South Bend fired appellant former employee shortly after she was sworn in as a police officer because she over the 36-year-old statutory age limit for appointment as an officer set forth in Ind. Code § 36-8-4-7. The employee sued the City for reinstatement. The St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana) upheld the constitutionality of the statute and entered judgment for the City. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the statutory age requirement for police officers did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment's equal protection guarantee or the equal privileges guarantee of the Indiana Constitution. The court upheld the trial court's judgment. First, the court held that the trial court properly applied the rational basis test rather than the strict scrutiny test to decide whether the statute constituted an impermissible classification based on age. The court agreed that the age classification for hiring police officers was rationally related to furthering a state interest in securing the most physically capable and active police force possible and in obtaining the administrative advantages of a younger police force. Second, the employee could not invoke the protection of the Age Discrimination in Employment Act (ADEA), 29 U.S.C.S. §§ 621-634, because she was not yet 40 years old. The court held that the presumption of validity which arose once the classification was rationally related to a legitimate state interest continued to operate despite the fact that in practice the law resulted in some inequality for those over 36 and under 40 years of age.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1184 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Crager v. Fry


No. 3-1084 A 287


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


479 N.E.2d 613; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2527



June 17, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Steuben Circuit Court Honorable Dane L. Tubergen, Judge Cause No. C-83-441.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, claimants of certain real estate, sought review of a judgment from Steuben Circuit Court (Indiana), which quieted title to the real estate at issue in favor of appellee, a tax sale purchaser.


OVERVIEW: The claimants contended that the Indiana tax sale statutes were unconstitutional as applied to this case and that the auditor's failure to include the street address or other common description of the property in the tax sale notice invalidated the tax sale. The court disagreed. As to the unconstitutionality of the tax sale statutes, the claimants misplaced reliance on a case that involved a recorded mortgage. The claimants failed to record their contract of sale with respect to the property at issue. While it was true that Ind. Code § 6-1.1-24-2.1 required that the county auditor include a statement, for informational purposes only, of the approximate location of each property, it went on to provide that a misstatement in the informational statement did not invalidate an otherwise valid sale. The result of a misstatement was not any different from that of an omission. As a misstatement of the approximate location did not invalidate an otherwise valid tax sale, the omission of an approximate location under § 6-1.1-24-2.1 did not invalidate it either.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1185 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


4447 Corp. v. Goldsmith


Consolidated Cause No. 4-1283 A 415, [No. 3-484 A 106 Before Consolidation]


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


479 N.E.2d 578; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2501



June 12, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 19, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Interlocutory Appeal from the Hamilton Circuit Court The Honorable Judith S. Proffitt, Judge and Interlocutory Appeal from the Allen Circuit Court The Honorable Thomas L. Ryan, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant adult bookstores appealed from the interlocutory orders of the Hamilton and Allen Circuit Courts (Indiana), which denied their motions to vacate injunctions providing for the padlocking of the bookstores and the seizing of the contents under the Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act (RICO), Ind. Code § 35-45-6-1 et seq., and the Civil Remedies for Racketeering Activity (CRRA) statute, Ind. Code § 34-4-30.5-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The court determined that the statutes were unconstitutional as a prior restraint, both substantively and procedurally. The court concluded that the statutes were unconstitutional: 1) as imposing a prior restraint which impermissibly impinged upon the dissemination of protected materials; 2) as the statutory procedures failed to comply with the procedural safeguards required even for the suppression of obscene materials; and 3) as the statutory provisions as they related to obscenity had to fall under the less restrictive means test for the evaluation of allegedly content-neutral state regulation which had an incidental impact upon free expression. The court noted that the injunctions constituted an impermissible prior restraint of protected communication, where each item contained in the bookstores was not reviewed for obscenity. Further, an adversarial determination of the obscenity prior to the en masse seizure of such materials was required, which was not provided for in the statutes. Also, the court stated that the sanctions were unconstitutional as applied to obscenity, given the availability of less restrictive means in furtherance of the state's legitimate purpose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's denial of the adult bookstores' motion to vacate the injunctions imposed under the Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act and under the Civil Remedies for Racketeering Activity statute and held that the statutes were unconstitutional.

Indiana Dep't of Public Welfare v. Clark

Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 10, 1985; Transfer Denied December 20, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Monroe Superior Court # 2 The Honorable Kenneth G. Todd, Judge (Cause No. CV8109-023C).



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Indiana Department of Public Welfare sought review of the decision of the Monroe Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee claimant based on the Department's unconstitutional denial of the claimant's request for Medicaid payments under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The claimant submitted a request by her dentist to the Department to obtain prior approval for payment for partial dentures. The Department denied the request. The claimant pursued her administrative remedies and a Department hearing officer upheld the denial. The claimant appealed to the State Board of Public Welfare. The Board notified the claimant that it affirmed the denial of prior payment. The claimant filed a complaint. The trial court, on discovering that the tape of the administrative hearing had been erased before transcription, remanded the case for another hearing. The court reversed and held that the claimant's action was a suit in tort and consequently the Indiana Tort Claims Act (ITCA) applied. The claimant failed to provide notice to the Department and thus, her claim was barred. The court found that threshold requirement of the ITCA was that the claimant file a notice of claim within 180 days and that the 180-day notice of claim provision applied to § 1983 actions brought in state court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the claimant.

 

1188 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Kozuch v. CRA-MAR Video Center, Inc.


No. 3-1284 A 337


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


478 N.E.2d 110; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2432



May 22, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 27, 1985; Transfer Denied October 25, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the St. Joseph Circuit Court Honorable John W. Montgomery, Judge Cause No. P-9206.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order of the St. Joseph Circuit Court (Indiana) that issued a preliminary injunction against appellants in appellee's action that sought to prohibit appellants from using appellee's customer list.


OVERVIEW: Appellants obtained a copy of appellee's customer list and used for purposes of a mass mailing. Appellee sought an injunction to prohibit appellants from using the list. The court held that the evidence supported the trial court's determination that the customer list was a trade secret pursuant to Ind. Code § 24-2-3-2. The trial court did not err in granting appellee a preliminary injunction because evidence supported the conclusions that appellee would suffer irreparable harm, that harm would outweigh appellants' continued use of the trade secret, and public interest would be served by granting the injunction. The court held the trial court's order was not conflicting; thus, appellants were able to obey the order. The order did not violate appellants' freedom of speech because it did not restrict appellants' advertising; it restricted appellants' use of the customer list.


OUTCOME: Order issuing a preliminary injunction against appellants affirmed because appellee proved the customer list was a trade secret, appellants' continued use of the list would result in irreparable harm, and that harm would outweigh appellants' continued use of the list.

Garrett v. Bloomington


No. 1-784 A 173


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


478 N.E.2d 89; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2421



May 21, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 27, 1985; Transfer Denied September 25, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Monroe Superior Court The Honorable Marc R. Kellams, Judge Cause No. CV8211-001B.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestee appealed a decision of the Monroe Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment to defendant police officers on the arrestee's claim of false arrest. The trial court held that the arrestee bore the burden of proving that the police officers had no probable cause to arrest him. The police officers appealed a denial of attorney's fees under Ind. Code § 34-4-16.5-19.


OVERVIEW: An arrestee returned to his apartment after work to find that his roommate and friends had been drinking. A 9-1-1 dispatcher traced a harassing call to the arrestee's telephone number and rang it back while police officers watched. The arrestee picked up the telephone and verbally abused the dispatcher, at which point he was arrested. The charges were later dropped. The court on appeal found that the arrestee was properly required to carry the burden of showing that the police officers had no probable cause and thus no reasonable good faith belief on which to arrest him. The court so held because the "false" portion of a claim of false arrest was part of the tort alleged. The court further noted that this would help to shield police officers from groundless lawsuits. The court, however, found no abuse of discretion in the failure of the trial court to award the police officers their attorney's fees, finding that the trial court may not have found the claim completely groundless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the police officers and affirmed the denial of their attorney's fees.

Championship Wrestling, Inc. v. State Boxing Com.


No. 2-184-A-3


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


477 N.E.2d 302; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2352



April 23, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 11, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Marion Superior Court Room Two The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Judge Cause No. S282-1141.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wrestling corporation filed an action against defendant State of Indiana, challenging the Boxing Commission Act, Ind. Code §§ 25-9-1-1 - 33, which placed a 10 percent tax on tickets to wrestling events, on equal protection grounds. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) denied the wrestling corporation's request for an injunction and a declaratory judgment. The wrestling corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the state deregulated wrestling, the Boxing Commission Act, Ind. Code § 25-9-1-22, continued to impose a 10 percent tax on the gross receipts received from the sale of tickets to wrestling events. The wrestling corporation filed an action against the State, alleging that the tax was unconstitutional because it bore no reasonable relationship to any apparent purpose of the Act in its present form. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the tax on the ground that the tax was rationally related to the advancement of the state purpose and policy to prohibit public fighting except under controlled and regulated circumstances. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment, concluding that the tax was invalid. The court held that because as the Act no longer provided for any regulation of wresting and its regulatory purpose related only to boxing, there could be no relationship between the Act's purpose and the legislative classification that continued to tax wrestling.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the tax imposed on tickets to wrestling events was arbitrary and violated the wrestling corporation's right to equal protection.

 

1191 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Gash v. Kohm


No. 1-584 A 115


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


476 N.E.2d 910; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2324



April 18, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 29, 1985; Transfer Denied December 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Warrick Circuit Court The Honorable Donald G. Hendrickson, Judge (Cause No. C81-615).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant perpetrator appealed a jury verdict finding him liable for wrongful death in the Warrick Circuit Court (Indiana), arguing that the trial court erred in forcing him to assert his Fifth Amendment right in the jury's presence, that the verdict was not supported by sufficient evidence, and that damages awarded to plaintiff parents were excessive.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the parents established the proximity of the perpetrator's car on the date of their daughter's disappearance to the area where her body was found. Despite inconclusive ballistic tests, a firearms expert established that the bullet which killed her was .22 caliber and that the perpetrator owned a .22 caliber gun. At trial, the perpetrator refused to answer questions from the parent's counsel on the basis of his Fifth Amendment rights. The jury returned a verdict against the perpetrator and he appealed. On review, the court held that the perpetrator was neither compelled to testify nor directly sanctioned for his refusal to answer questions. His assertion of his Fifth Amendment right in the jury's presence was not error because the constitutional guarantee did not apply in a civil trial to prohibit the jury from drawing an inference of liability. Because the total damage award was within the evidence adduced at trial, it was reasonable. Further, the perpetrator failed to show how he was prejudiced by the denial of his motion to continue, and the trial court properly refused his proposed instruction to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment awarding damages to the parents in an action against the perpetrator of their daughter's death.

Davis v. State


No. 2-1083 A 356


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


476 N.E.2d 127; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2266



March 28, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 29, 1986; Transfer Denied January 22, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Huntington Circuit Court The Honorable Dane Mann, Judge Cause No. CR 82-49 and 50.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed with respect to Mary and reversed with respect to Reed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, alleged mother and alleged father, challenged the judgment of the Huntington Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered convictions against them for neglect of a dependent in violation of Ind. Code Ann. § 35-46-1-4 (1979), a class D felony.


OVERVIEW: An abandoned newborn baby was discovered by a passer-by. Defendants were convicted of neglect of a dependent and each appealed. The court affirmed the alleged mother's conviction but reversed the conviction of the alleged father. The court rejected defendants' arguments that the underlying statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court determined that no reasonable person of ordinary intelligence would have had difficulty determining that the alleged activity was proscribed by the statute and that the statute was sufficient to advise defendants that their treatment of the infant was proscribed. The court held that the "and/or" language in the indictment did not hamper their ability to understand the nature of the charge or to prepare a defense. The court ruled that the probability calculations of defendants' parentage were properly admitted into evidence. The court found that the evidence was insufficient to support the alleged father's conviction because Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4 required the endangerment or abandonment to have been either knowing or intentional, and the uncontradicted evidence placed the alleged father at his workplace when the baby was born, abandoned, and found.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the alleged mother's conviction for neglect of a dependent and reversed the alleged father's conviction of neglect of a dependent.

Taylor-Chalmers, Inc. v. Board of Comm'rs


No. 3-384 A 82


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


474 N.E.2d 531; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2196



February 21, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 30, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Porter Superior Court Honorable Raymond D. Kickbush, Judge Cause Number 80-PSC-1779.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed from a decision of the Porter Superior Court (Indiana) that granted summary judgment in favor of defendant county commissioners in an inverse condemnation proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The landowners challenged a summary judgment granted in favor of the county commissioners in an inverse condemnation proceeding. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court judgment. The court found that the landowners admitted that there had been no physical invasion of its property. The landowners also admitted that no nuisance had been created. The landowners' sole allegation was that a "taking" had occurred because the value of its land had been reduced from that of commercial or accommodation business to light industrial or agricultural, i.e., that it had lost the highest and best use of its land.However, the court found no evidence that the property was now under greater zoning restrictions, or that it must be rezoned to be used. There was no evidence that the property could not be sold for its remaining zoned uses, or indeed for the zoned use of commercial or accommodation business. In addition, the landowners had presented no evidence to show that the injury to the property was not incidental or inconsequential, i.e., peculiar to the property and not suffered in common with the general public.


OUTCOME: In an inverse condemnation proceeding, the court affirmed the trial court grant of summary judgment in favor of the county commissioners.

Frame v. South Bend Community School Corp.


No. 3-1184 A 314


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


480 N.E.2d 261; 1985 Ind. App. LEXIS 2614



July, 17, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 30, 1985; Transfer Denied January 6, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the St. Joseph Superior Court Honorable George N. Beamer, Jr., Judge Cause No. M81-CV-331.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the students and their parents, challenged the judgment of the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana) that found in favor of appellee South Bend, Indiana, Community School Corporation in the action for injunctive, declaratory, and monetary relief. The students and parents claimed that Ind. Code § 20-9.1-7-1, as applied, violated the Equal Protection Clause, the Free Exercise of Religion Clause, as well as Ind. Const. art. 1, §§ 2, 23.


OVERVIEW: Under § 20-9.1-7-1, which was included in the Indiana Pupil Transportation Act, parochial school students were entitled to school bus transportation. The Corporation permitted parochial school students to board the school buses only when there was available seating. No additional buses or routes were added to accommodate the students. In the subsequent action for injunctive, declaratory, and compensatory relief, the superior court adopted the order of the United States District Court for the Northern District of Indiana, which ruled in favor of the Corporation. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, ruling that the Corporation's interpretation of § 20-9.1-7.1 was consistent with legislative intent and not unreasonable, for purposes of equal protection, because several legitimate grounds existed for the decision. Also, the construction of the section was rationally-related to the valid goal of conserving limited financial resources. The court further found that providing transportation to the students was a type of "equal aide" that was not constitutionally required. Therefore, the court rejected the claim that the Free Exercise of Religion Clause was violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1195 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Iseton v. State


No. 2-883 A 295


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


472 N.E.2d 643; 1984 Ind. App. LEXIS 3173



December 27, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Grant Superior Court No. 1 The Honorable Thomas Newman, Jr., Special Judge Cause No. 3176.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Grant County Superior Court (Indiana) convicted defendant, after he was tried before a six-person jury, of two counts of theft. Defendant appealed his conviction on the grounds that the admission of the complainant's deposition in lieu of her live testimony violated his right to confrontation. He also claimed that a twelve-person jury was constitutionally required.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took sums of money from the victim for repairs to her home that were not made. Prior to trial, the elderly and infirm victim's deposition was taken. It was admitted at trial over defendant's right to confrontation objection. In addition, between the time when defendant was charged and when his trial commenced, Ind. Code § 35-1-30-1, which had required a twelve-person jury in a Class D felony case, was amended to require a six-person jury. Defendant argued that the amendment, as applied to his case, was an unconstitutional ex-post facto law. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that (1) it was reasonable for the trial court to conclude that the victim was unavailable to testify at the trial due to her age, sickness, or infirmity, (2) no violation of the ex post facto constitutional guarantees occurred because none of defendant's substantial rights was affected by the application of the amendment, and (3) a defendant does not have a substantial right to a jury composed of any specific number, so long as the number was not less than six.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on two counts of theft.

 

1196 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Avery v. Faulkner


No. 3-484 A 108 PS


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Third District


471 N.E.2d 1226; 1984 Ind. App. LEXIS 3175



December 19, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1985; Transfer Denied May 10, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from LaPorte Superior Court Room No. 2 Honorable Don E. Harner, Judge Cause Number S2-83-5937.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of a judgment of the LaPorte Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed his complaint alleging that Ind. Code § 11-11-3-2 (Supp. 1984) unconstitutionally conflicted with his guaranteed constitutional right to free speech and held that § 11-11-3-2 was facially constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Because the inmate had neither requested nor received prior approval from prison officials to send correspondence to other inmates pursuant to § 11-11-3-2, prison officials returned several letters to the inmate. The court held that: (1) where it appeared a certainty from the face of the complaint that the complaining party was not entitled to any relief, the court would not reverse the judgment of the trial court in granting a motion to dismiss; (2) constitutionally guaranteed rights could be restricted if the restriction furthered a substantial government interest and was no greater than necessary to protect the interest involved; (3) prior approval of inmate correspondence furthered substantial government interests such as order, security, and rehabilitation, and the court did not see how these interests could be adequately and effectively protected with a lesser means of involvement by the prison officials; (4) the restriction was not a prohibition per se of any communication and due process was available; and (5) the trial court was correct in finding that § 11-11-3-2 was constitutional and, thus, that the inmate failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Tribbett v. Tay Mor Industries, Inc.


No. 2-1083-A-376


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Second District


471 N.E.2d 332; 1984 Ind. App. LEXIS 3077



November 26, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Cass Circuit Court The Honorable Robert Leirer Justice, Judge Cause No. C83-93.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a decision from the Cass Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed her safe workplace negligence claim against defendant employer, pursuant to Ind. R. Trial P. 12(B)(1), on the ground that the it lacked subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the employer. Her job required her to wind coils around her shoulder and thumb. She was injured by that job function. She filed an action against the employer, which alleged that her injury was caused by the employer's willfulness and negligence in failing to provide her with a safe workplace. The employee also filed claims under the Workmen's Compensation Act, Ind. Code § 22-3-1-1 et seq., and the Workmen's Occupational Disease Act, Ind. Code § 22-3-7-1 et seq., which were pending when the negligence action was filed. The employer moved to dismiss the employee's petition under Ind. R. Trial P. 12(B)(1), based on the Indiana Industrial Board's exclusive jurisdiction. The trial court dismissed the petition. On appeal, the employee argued that her action fell within the intentional tort exception to worker's compensation exclusivity. The court upheld the dismissal because the petition failed to allege facts that showed an intentional tort. The fact that the employer knew of a risk might be recklessness but that fell short of intention. Finally, the exclusivity provision of the Workmen's Compensation Act was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. McLaughlin


No. 4-883 A 255


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


471 N.E.2d 1125; 1984 Ind. App. LEXIS 3051



November 19, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 5, 1985; Transfer Denied May 3, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Tippecanoe County Court The Honorable Kenneth L. Thayer, Judge Cause No. TC-MT-9515-82.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the Tippecanoe County Court (Indiana), which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence of a breathalyzer test result and all other evidence obtained after the initial stop of his automobile on the ground that his detention, search, and arrest were in violation of U.S. Const. amends. IV, XIV.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was detained at a police roadblock and was charged with driving while intoxicated. He filed a motion to suppress the breathalyzer results and the trial court granted defendant's motion. The trial court held that the seizure of defendant was unreasonable and that the fruits of the stop should be suppressed on the ground that the roadblock was not conducted according to administrative guidelines that qualified as previously specified neutral criteria. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the state presented absolutely no evidence regarding the availability of less intrusive methods of law enforcement for combating the drunk-driving problem. The court held that despite the gravity of the public concern for identifying and apprehending drunk drivers, the state failed to present any evidence that the roadblock procedure advanced the public interest to a greater degree than would have been achieved by traditional methods of drunk-driving law enforcement based upon a requirement of individualized suspicion. The court also held that the state failed to sustain its burden of proving that the roadblock seizure was reasonable under U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence of his breathalyzer test results.

 

1199 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Lambert v. State


No. 1-684 A 144


Court of Appeals of Indiana, First District


468 N.E.2d 1384; 1984 Ind. App. LEXIS 2992



October 18, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 27, 1984; Transfer denied March 12, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Vanderburgh Superior Court The Honorable Maurice C. O'Connor, Judge Cause No. 83-CIV-2969.



DISPOSITION:  For all of the foregoing reasons, we affirm the decision of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landfill owners sought review of a decision of the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), which found in favor of appellee state highway department, in the owners' action, which alleged violation of their constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The state issued notices requiring certain revisions to three of its demolition contracts. The revision forbid the contractor from disposing of any of the demolition materials at the owner's landfill. The state knew that construction of another project would require the state to acquire and excavate the owner's landfill. The state contended that it did not want to have to pay twice, once for dumping demolition materials and then later for removing those materials from the same facility. The owners brought an action against the state, which alleged that this revision violated their constitutional rights. The trial court found in favor of the state. The owners appealed. The court affirmed and found that (1) the contract revisions were merely a proper exercise of its proprietary powers and did not violate any constitutional provisions; (2) the state had a rational and lawful purpose for inserting the new provision into the contract; (3) the new contract provision did not constitute state action such that constitutional limitations should be brought into play; and, (4) saving taxpayer's money was a legitimate goal to be furthered by the exercise of the state's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which was in favor of the state, in the landfill owner's action to prevent the state from forbidding the construction contractor from using their landfill.

 

1200 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Cunningham v. State


No. 4-883 A 270


Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District


469 N.E.2d 1; 1984 Ind. App. LEXIS 2976



September 27, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 9, 1984; Transfer denied February 25, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Hamilton Superior Court # 1 The Honorable Dennis D. Carroll, Special Judge Cause No. 1SCR81-020.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed except as to the revision of sentence. Remanded to the trial court for imposition of sentence consistent with the findings contained in this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, husband and wife, appealed from the judgment of the Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana), entered after their jury convictions on charges of theft, a class D felony, Ind. Code § 35-43-4-2, perjury, a class D felony, Ind. Code § 35-44-2-1, and conversion, a class A misdemeanor, Ind. Code § 35-43-4-3. The convictions arose from food stamp offenses. Defendant husband also appealed from his 16-year sentence rendered by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The wife contended that she was denied a fair trial because the trial court refused to sever her trial from her husband's. The court found it clear that the trial court and jury determined the wife's culpability separately and distinctly from the charges against the husband; therefore, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by refusing to sever their trials. Both defendants alleged prosecutorial misconduct in providing information that led to a prejudicial article in a local newspaper. The court found, however, that defendants did not demonstrate prejudice because of its use, as no jurors read the article. Defendants argued that there was insufficient evidence to sustain the perjury convictions. The court disagreed, noting that defendants' signatures on the applications were unequivocal acts affirming they had disclosed all other sources of income, which they had not. The court finally noted that the husband had other convictions, but also noted that he had a stable employment history and that he would be unable to provide for his children if a prolonged sentence was imposed on him. The court, therefore, revised the husband's sentence by reducing it to two years.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed except as to the revision of the husband's sentence.
